# Franklin Richards — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# UATU DOSSIER — FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS
## Section 0: Executive Brief (BLUF)

*Classification: Omega-tier reality-architect, chronological minor, volitional minor. Surveillance status: passive-protective. Threat vector: not from subject; toward subject and toward whatever the world does to him. File priority: maximal.*

---

### BOTTOM LINE UP FRONT

**Franklin Benjamin Richards is a god who has chosen, deliberately and repeatedly, to be a boy — and the entire moral architecture of the post-*Secret Wars* Marvel cosmos rests on the continued integrity of that choice.** He is not a hero in waiting, not a weapon in storage, not a prodigy being groomed. He is a being who has already touched the ceiling of what creation permits, looked at it, and walked back down the staircase to ask his mother what's for dinner. Everything else in this file — every habit, every tic, every relational pattern, every micro-behavior catalogued in subsequent sections — is downstream of that one fact and of the single childhood injury that made the choice necessary.

If you read no other section: **the subject is stable, the subject is dangerous only when those he loves are threatened, the subject's stability is held by three to four specific human beings, and the loss of any one of them is a multiversal continuity event.** Plan accordingly.

---

### THE THROUGH-LINE OF THE ENTIRE EXISTENCE

From the gestational crisis in *FF Annual #6* (1968) through the present publication record, the subject's life describes a single unbroken arc with one consistent shape: **he is the load his family carries, and the load that carries his family, and he has spent five decades of in-universe and out-of-universe time learning to make that load weightless to them.**

The arc, granularly:

- **Phase I — Object (1968–early 1970s).** He is a thing to be saved, taken, retrieved. He has no agency, no consciousness of self. He is acted upon.
- **Phase II — Threat (FF #133–141).** He acts for the first time, and his father responds by switching him off. The defining injury is delivered before the subject is old enough to file it consciously. He learns, somatically, that *his own becoming is dangerous to the people he loves and they will stop him if he is.*
- **Phase III — Instrument (late 1970s–1980s).** He becomes a prophetic dreamer, a warning system, a vessel — used by writers and by in-universe adults as a window onto incoming catastrophe. He is not yet a person; he is a function.
- **Phase IV — Architect, Unconscious (Onslaught, 1996).** Under terminal protective panic, he builds a universe to hide the people he loves inside. He does not remember doing it. The injury and the gift are now the same gesture: *I will make a world to keep them safe, and I will not know I did it.*
- **Phase V — Brother (Hickman FF, 2009–2012).** Valeria arrives. For the first time in his existence, he has a relationship in which he is not the youngest, not the weakest, not the watched. He develops, in the Future Foundation, the prosocial signature that defines his adulthood-in-miniature: tenderness toward the monstrous, gentleness toward the small, leadership without command.
- **Phase VI — Architect, Conscious (Hickman *Secret Wars*, 2015).** He builds the substrate of the current multiverse alongside his father. For one suspended moment he is met by Reed as a peer, as a co-creator. Then he chooses, deliberately and with full knowledge, to put the godhood down and re-enter boyhood. *This is the most important single decision in the file.* It is the moment the wound is metabolized into a vow.
- **Phase VII — Question (Slott / North / Ewing era to present).** The vow is tested. Powers fade, are faked, ambiguate. Xavier denies him the mutant category. The question is no longer *what can I do* but *what am I if I am not what I was.* He has chosen smallness; now smallness chooses him back, and he has to discover whether the choice survives no longer being a choice.

**The through-line, stated cleanly:** Franklin Richards has spent his entire existence learning that the only honest use of overwhelming power is to lay it down for the people who loved you before you had it. He is, in the deepest register, a story about restraint as love.

---

### THE CORE WOUND

The core wound is not Onslaught. It is not Annihilus. It is not Mephisto, not Hyperstorm, not any of the cosmic predators who have used his nervous system as a battlefield.

**The core wound is FF #141: his father judged him a danger and shut his mind off.**

He was too young to remember it cognitively. He remembers it everywhere else. Every behavior in this file that involves Reed Richards — the intellectual deference, the somatic mistrust, the going-to-Ben-when-scared, the bringing-drawings-to-Reed-and-then-not-quite-watching-him-look-at-them, the way he will accept any expert correction from his father without protest and then quietly not return to the subject — is the wound maintaining itself.

The wound has three articulating premises, each of which the subject has absorbed pre-verbally and operates from without examination:

1. **My becoming is a danger.** If I grow into what I am, the people who made me will have to stop me. Therefore I will not grow into what I am. I will grow sideways, into stories, into pocket worlds, into brotherhood, into the Foundation, into anything that is not the thing my father had to shut off.
2. **My father's love is conditional on my containability.** This is not a conscious belief and the subject would reject it if articulated. It nevertheless governs his behavior. He earns Reed's gaze through *manageability* — through being a son Reed can solve, parent, schedule, plan around. The unmanageable Franklin, the one who built Heroes Reborn, the one who co-designed Battleworld, is a Franklin he produces only in extremis and then puts away.
3. **The only safe form of my power is its use for someone else.** Power-for-self is what got switched off. Power-for-them is what saves the family. Therefore every spontaneous use of his abilities, from infancy through the present, is *other-directed.* He has never, in five decades of canon, used reality-warping for personal gratification. Not once. This is not modesty; it is a load-bearing rule his nervous system installed at age four.

**Maintenance of the wound.** The wound is maintained by three mechanisms:

- **Reed's continuing incomprehension.** Reed Richards loves his son and underestimates him on a continuous basis. The underestimation is itself the renewal of the original gesture — *I will decide what you are, and I will manage you accordingly.* Reed has had occasional revelations (the Hickman moment of co-creation; scattered Waid and Slott beats), but his baseline mode is to think *about* Franklin rather than *with* him. Each instance of this is a quiet reinscription.
- **The subject's own vow.** Having chosen smallness, he must keep choosing it, and each renewal is an acknowledgment of why the choice was needed. The vow is the wound's vestment.
- **The world's category failures.** Mutant/not-mutant, child/god, human/cosmic — every time an external taxonomy tries to fit him and fails, the underlying ambiguity that began with Reed's first refusal to accept him as he was is restimulated. Xavier's denial is the most recent and most legible instance; it will not be the last.

**What heals the wound, partially:** Sue. Valeria. Ben. Johnny. The Moloids. Leech. Dragon Man. Any relationship in which he is met as he is, at the scale he presents at, without either fear or recruitment. These are the analgesics. They are not curative; the wound is the wound. They are the reason it does not septicemia into something worse.

---

### WHO HE IS AT THE DEEPEST LEVEL

Strip the powers, strip the cosmic résumé, strip the alternate-future tyrant projections and the messianic projections and the architect-of-the-multiverse credit line: **he is a gentle, observant, narratively-minded child who loves a small number of people with terrifying completeness and would prefer, more than anything in any cosmos he has ever built or could build, to be permitted to remain exactly that.**

He is the kind of child who notices first when someone at the table is sad. He is the kind of child who draws the monster as a friend before anyone tells him the monster is supposed to be scary. He is the kind of child who, given infinite crayons and infinite paper, would draw his family over and over, and in every drawing his father would be in the center, and in every drawing he would be standing a little to the side, holding Valeria's hand, watching.

He is also — and this must be held in the same frame, without contradiction — **the being who built a universe in a single dissociated instant to keep that family from dying.** The gentleness and the omnipotence are not in tension in him. They are the same disposition expressed at different magnitudes. He loves; therefore he draws. He loves more; therefore he builds. He loves at the ceiling; therefore he authors cosmos. The mechanism is one mechanism.

Closest thematic analog in the historical record is not any superhuman figure but the contemplative-pacifist tradition: the bodhisattva who declines nirvana to remain with the suffering, the Christian mystic who practices *kenosis* — voluntary self-emptying — as the highest expression of strength. Franklin Richards is a four-color kenotic. He is the universe choosing to be a child in the universe it made, because the people in it are worth being small for.

---

### OPERATIONAL SUMMARY

For any agency, entity, or analyst making practical decisions in proximity to the subject:

**Capacity.** Effectively unbounded at peak. Demonstrated: pocket-universe creation, multiversal substrate authoring, reality revision, precognition, durability functionally absolute when powered. Current expression: ambiguous, suppressed, possibly transitional. *Do not plan against ceiling estimates; the ceiling has not been located.*

**Disposition.** Non-aggressive. Pro-social. Protective. Outsider-affiliative. Will not initiate harm. Will not retaliate for harm done to him personally. **Will reorganize reality in defense of a small list of named persons.**

**Triggers — escalation, in ascending order of danger.**
1. Being dismissed by a loved adult: withdrawal, rumination, increased compulsive making.
2. Belonging-category challenge (mutant/not, child/not): destabilization of chosen self-concept, mild dissociation.
3. Threat to Valeria: immediate protective mobilization, powers come online before cognition.
4. Threat to Sue: terminal protective state; historical precedent is universe-creation; **no negotiation channel exists at this level.**
5. Simultaneous threat to multiple tethers: file Hyperstorm, file tyrant-Franklin, file every dark-future projection on record. *This is the failure mode.*

**De-escalation.** Cannot be reasoned out of a protective response. Can only be defused by *removal of the threat to the loved object.* Verbal de-escalation, appeals to consequence, displays of force — all useless. Bring him Sue, alive. Bring him Val, safe. The state ends.

**Handling protocol.** Treat as a child. This is not a euphemism, not a cover, not a tactical posture. He has chosen the developmental position and the choice is load-bearing for his stability and for everyone else's. Address him at his age. Permit him his hobbies, his Foundation projects, his drawings, his Moloids. Do not invite him to be more than he is. Do not test the ceiling. Do not, under any circumstances, attempt recruitment to a faction, an ideology, or a strategic role; the recruitment will fail and the attempt will register as a category violation he files quietly.

**Critical infrastructure designation.** The following relationships are to be regarded as *infrastructure protection priorities* of the highest tier, on the grounds that their integrity is structurally linked to the integrity of consensus reality:
- **Susan Storm-Richards** (mother; primary attachment; the original tether)
- **Valeria Richards** (sister; co-regulating peer; the daily tether)
- **Benjamin Grimm** (chosen uncle; ideal secondary attachment; the safety tether)
- **Jonathan Storm** (chosen uncle; affect-mirror; the play tether)
- **Reed Richards** (father; the wound and the unfinished business; *cannot be lost without catastrophic consequence even though the relationship itself is the wound — perhaps especially because it is*)

The Future Foundation cohort (Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man, Bentley, Alex Power, Artie) constitutes a secondary tether net of substantial protective value. Loss of any individual member is metabolizable; loss of the cohort as a structure is not.

**Risk forecast.** Subject will not become a villain. Subject will not become a tyrant. Subject will not become Hyperstorm. Subject will become any of these things *only if the world removes his reasons to remain a boy.* The risk is therefore not behavioral; it is environmental. **Watch the tethers. Protect the tethers. The tethers are the file.**

---

### CLOSING BLUF LINE

He is the most powerful being currently catalogued on Earth and one of the most powerful beings of any era, and he is using all of it to be a son and a brother and a friend to a telepathic mole-child. That is not a contradiction. That is the answer. The dossier that follows is the granular documentation of how a person becomes that answer, and of every small habit and route and ritual by which he keeps being it, day after day, against a universe that keeps asking him to be something larger and worse.

*File continues. Section 1 to follow: Subject Identification and Biographical Spine.*


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

*File segment 1 of N. Coverage: in-utero through approximately age six (the Onslaught inflection). All datings are publication-canon; in-universe ages are sliding-timescale approximations. Where a single event is referenced repeatedly across decades, the earliest canonical appearance is cited as anchor.*

---

## 1.1 GESTATION AS CRISIS EVENT

The subject's prenatal record is, uniquely in the canonical literature, *the central plot of a comic*. Susan Storm-Richards' pregnancy is the throughline of *Fantastic Four* #50s–60s and culminates in *Fantastic Four Annual* #6 (1968), in which her cosmic-ray-saturated biology nearly kills both her and the fetus during labor. The clinical picture given on-page: hemorrhagic collapse, energy-field instability, fetal distress. The remedy is not medical but cosmological — Reed Richards, Ben Grimm, and Johnny Storm are dispatched into the Negative Zone to extract the "Cosmic Control Rod" from Annihilus, the only antimatter source capable of stabilizing the radiation in Sue's tissues.

Three behavioral-substrate facts are laid down before subject draws breath:

1. **His existence is conditional on his father leaving.** The man who should be at the bedside is, by absolute necessity, elsewhere — fighting a god to permit the birth. This template (Reed-absent-while-needed; Reed-absent-*because*-needed) will recur every year of subject's documented life.
2. **He almost killed his mother by existing.** Even with no conscious access to this datum, it inheres in the family's narrative weather. Every adult around him knows it. Sue's miscarriage of his second sibling, attempted years later (*FF* #267, Byrne), reinforces the pattern: Richards pregnancies are catastrophes, and he is the one who survived.
3. **He is born into a household whose first language is *cosmic stakes*.** No infant in the canon is welcomed home to a more saturated emotional environment.

Naming is performed by Reed in the same Annual: *Franklin Benjamin Richards.* Franklin for Sue's father (Dr. Franklin Storm, deceased, ambivalent figure — a felon, redeemed only at death). Benjamin for Ben Grimm. The name *therefore encodes the family's idealized male triad*: a redeemed grandfather, the godfather-uncle who is the household's most reliable adult, and the patriarch who could not be present. Subject lives the rest of his life inside the social meaning of those three names.

---

## 1.2 INFANT JEOPARDY: THE KIDNAP CYCLE

From *Fantastic Four* #88 (Annihilus' return) through the entire Thomas/Buscema and Conway tail (~#130), the infant Franklin is taken, threatened, or used as bait at a frequency that, in any non-comic environment, would constitute a Child Protective Services file three inches thick. Anchor incidents include:

- **The Frightful Four** abduct him (or attempt to) on multiple occasions through this era; Medusa, prior to her own redemption arc, handles him.
- **Annihilus** returns specifically for the infant in *FF* #108–109, identifying Franklin's latent neural energy as cosmically valuable — the *first on-page recognition by an external entity* that this child is a power source.
- **The Mad Thinker** and the **Wizard** each take operational interest.
- **Agatha Harkness is hired as governess** in *Fantastic Four* #94 (1970, Lee/Kirby). The Frightful Four's first move thereafter is to follow the infant *to* Harkness's house at Whisper Hill. The child cannot even be hidden in a witch's cottage without the cottage being assaulted.

The behavioral inscription: *I am the lever villains pull to hurt my parents.* He cannot consciously have formulated this in infancy, but the *somatic* learning is encoded: novel adults equal danger, unfamiliar environments equal danger, separation from Sue equals danger. This subtends his lifelong, observable preference for known faces and small interior spaces — the Baxter Building nursery, later the Future Foundation classroom, later still the Forever City pocket-residences he conjures for friends. *He likes rooms.* The kidnap cycle taught him.

---

## 1.3 AGATHA HARKNESS AS SECOND MATRIARCH

Harkness is materially the second-most-formative caregiver of subject's preschool years, by hours of contact. Her household at Whisper Hill (a fortified rural compound, magical wards, a familiar named Ebony) is *Franklin's first stable non-Baxter environment.* He is taught there in three modalities:

- **Magical containment** — Harkness places dampeners on his nascent abilities, the first of many adult-imposed lids on the child's nervous system (cf. §1.5).
- **Quiet observation** — Harkness's pedagogy is non-verbal, watchful, witchy. Subject's later cognitive style (right-hemisphere, symbolic, image-and-story dominant rather than propositional) is plausibly seeded here, in contrast to the lab-talk of Baxter dinners.
- **Tolerance for the uncanny** — he sees a witch every day, talks to her cat, is unfrightened by manifestation. The later, *defining* gentleness toward "monstrous" outsiders (Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man, Bentley-23) has its rehearsal here: his first beloved non-parent adult is a thing other adults would call a monster.

Harkness's eventual immolation in *Vision and the Scarlet Witch*/*West Coast Avengers* (off-Franklin canon, but in his world) is one of the first deaths he registers as personal. Tracked across later issues, subject is repeatedly depicted *missing her* (he asks after her in Byrne-era panels and in Walt Simonson's run).

---

## 1.4 LATCHKEY COSMIC CHILDHOOD: THE ROTATING-PARENTS REGIME

Through Wein, Wolfman, and the early Byrne run (mid-1970s through ~1983), the operational reality is that *Reed and Sue are gone a great deal.* Subject is parked, alternately, with:

- **Agatha Harkness** (default).
- **Alicia Masters** (warm, blind, sculptor — calm sensory environment; one of the few adults who *touched his face to know him*, a memory traceable in his later non-flinching response to physical reassurance from trusted adults).
- **Ben Grimm,** when Ben was groundside (see §1.7 below — load-bearing).
- **Johnny Storm,** intermittently — the fun uncle, the wrong choice for crisis but a calibrated source of ordinary play.
- **Various sitter-failures** that became plots.

Behavioral pattern *forming in this window* and persisting lifelong: **he does not protest absence.** No tantrum on departure is canonically depicted. Subject internalizes early that his parents leave for *reasons that are real* (saving the world, often saving *him*), and he learns to wait. This is the seed of the adult-Franklin trait of *quiet suppression of his own needs because he perceives them as cosmically disproportionate.* He learned, ages 2–4, that his needs were always smaller than the planet's.

---

## 1.5 THE PATERNAL LOBOTOMY: *FANTASTIC FOUR* #141 (CONWAY/BUSCEMA, 1973)

The single most psychologically loaded event of the chronology.

**The fact pattern.** Franklin's powers ignite catastrophically — the Annihilus arc weaponizes his latent neural energy and the boy reaches a discharge that, on-page dialogue confirms, threatens planetary integrity. Reed Richards constructs and deploys a device that *shuts down his son's higher brain function.* Franklin enters an induced coma. The page is staged like a crucifixion: child on a slab, father holding the instrument, the rest of the team in horror.

**Sue's response.** She walks out. She files for separation. The Richards marriage cracks open and stays cracked for issues. The household subject returns to *after* he is reawakened (later in Conway's run; full restoration during the Thomas tail) is a household where the parents have been *publicly broken by what was done to him.* He does not consciously remember the procedure. He does live in the residue.

**The clinical inscription.** A child cannot encode an episode he was rendered unconscious to undergo. But the household around him encodes it richly: Sue carries it, Ben carries it, Reed carries it as guilt that distorts every subsequent interaction with the boy. The *relational temperature* between Franklin and Reed is set in this issue and never fully reset. Every later panel of Reed hesitating to touch his son, of Reed addressing Franklin's powers as a problem rather than addressing Franklin as a person, of Reed leaving the room when Franklin enters with a drawing — every one of these is a downstream tremor from #141. Subject reads the tremor without knowing its source. *He concludes his father is afraid of him.* He is correct. He misattributes the fear's content (he thinks: *I am too much*; the truth is: *Reed never forgave Reed*).

This is the etiology of the lifelong avoidant feature in the Reed-attachment. It is also the etiology of subject's lifelong tendency to *manage Reed's affect* — to bring Reed a problem Reed can solve (a math question, a Foundation engineering puzzle) rather than a feeling Reed cannot. Subject became, before age six, the emotional caretaker of the parent who had once switched him off.

---

## 1.6 PRECOGNITIVE DREAMS: THE NIGHTMARE PATTERN (BYRNE ERA, ~1981–1986)

Byrne's run formalizes Franklin's *dream-prophecy* presentation. Anchor incidents:

- The Ultron warning dreams.
- The pre-Secret Wars II / Beyonder anticipations.
- General night-terror sequences in which the child wakes screaming and the adults investigate, finding the dream contained an actionable warning.

The behavioral pattern that calcifies: **I see, I warn, I am dismissed, I am vindicated by catastrophe.** This is the seed of his adult *trait hypervigilance for others' safety* and the source of one of his most reliable micro-tells — when adults around him discuss a coming threat, subject goes quiet and watchful and *will not contribute unless directly asked,* because the early-childhood reward schedule for unsolicited warnings was negative (dismissal) and the cost of unspoken warnings was catastrophic (vindication-by-disaster, which is *worse* than dismissal because it confirms he failed to be heard).

Habit residue traceable from this era onward: **he sleeps lightly, wakes fully on first sound, sits up in bed rather than startling supine**, and — when staying anywhere other than his own room — locates the exits before he sleeps. None of this is ever directly narrated; all of it is consistent across artists from Byrne forward when he is depicted in a sleeping context.

---

## 1.7 BEN GRIMM AS LOAD-BEARING ATTACHMENT

The clinical importance of Ben Grimm in subject's childhood cannot be overstated and is generally underestimated in fan readings. *Uncle Ben is the most reliably present, affectively legible, physically safe adult of Franklin's entire childhood.* The pattern:

- **Bedtime story canon.** Ben reads to him; this is depicted across Lee, Wein, Byrne, and Waid runs. Subject's lifelong narrative-cognitive style — thinking *in stories* — has its load-bearing root in this nightly ritual.
- **Physical containment that is safe.** Ben is *built like a wall*; the child sleeps against his chest in canonical panels (Wein run especially). Subject's tactile baseline for "safety" is *large, warm, slightly rough surface.* He flinches less from Ben's touch than from anyone's, including, by late Byrne, from Reed's.
- **Affective honesty.** Ben does not lie to him. Ben tells him when things are bad; Ben tells him when he is scared. Subject learns from Ben that *adults can be afraid and still be safe.* This is the model he will later try and fail to apply to Reed.
- **Aunt Petunia mythos.** Ben's verbal tic — "Aunt Petunia" oaths and stories — becomes part of Franklin's private lexicon; he uses Ben-style locutions in dialogue across decades, a code-switch into *Ben's voice* that signals he is feeling small.

Clinically, **Ben Grimm is subject's secure base.** Sue is his haven. Reed is the ambivalent object. Ben is the ground. This triangulation is set by age four and never substantially renegotiated.

---

## 1.8 JOHNNY, ALICIA, CRYSTAL, MEDUSA — THE PERIPHERAL ADULTS

- **Johnny Storm** functions as the *play-uncle*: chaotic, indulgent, the source of subject's earliest exposure to *unsupervised fun* and to the idea that an adult might be a co-conspirator. Subject's later capacity for delight — the *easily delighted* trait — is fed here.
- **Alicia Masters** provides sensory calm and an early non-visual modality of love (she knows him by touch). Subject is unusually comfortable being looked at *and* unusually comfortable being not-looked-at; the latter is Alicia's gift.
- **Crystal** is the closest he gets in early childhood to a young-adult woman who is neither mother nor witch — fleeting but warm.
- **Medusa**, post-redemption, holds him during the FF roster reshuffles. Subject's later ease with the Inhumans (he is unintimidated by Black Bolt in adolescent appearances) traces here.

---

## 1.9 PRESCHOOL-AGE BEHAVIORAL MICRO-PATTERNS (OBSERVED, COMPOSITE FROM ARTIST RUNS)

Compiled from consistent depiction across Kirby, Buscema, Pérez, Byrne, Sienkiewicz cameos, and Ron Frenz:

- **Carries a stuffed object at all times in early childhood** — typically a small plush, often kept in a specific Baxter Building bedroom location. He returns it to the same spot each night. Ritual placement, not random.
- **Draws constantly.** Crayon-on-floor depictions across multiple artists. He shows drawings to Sue first, Ben second, Johnny third, and Reed *only when invited.* The Reed-omission is the tell.
- **Speaks softly.** Lettering across runs uses smaller balloons and lower-case-heavy emphasis for Franklin's lines, even when he is the speaking child in a panel.
- **Asks "are you okay?" of adults more often than adults ask it of him.** Parentified affect, depicted as early as Wein run.
- **Does not initiate physical contact with Reed; accepts it when offered; initiates freely with Sue, Ben, Johnny, Alicia.**
- **Hides during shouting.** Specifically: hides in *enclosed small spaces* — under the lab table, in a cabinet, behind Sue's force-field when she casts one. Not the closet of a frightened child fleeing punishment; the *den* of a child who has learned that enclosed-and-near-Sue is the survivable position.
- **Names his toys, his drawings, and the imaginary creatures he constructs.** Naming is a *core operation* for him from age three forward; later, when he constructs Heroes Reborn and Battleworld, he will be naming things at cosmic scale, but the cognitive verb is identical.
- **Sings to himself when alone.** Heard by Sue and remarked on in Byrne issues; tuneless, low, continuous. A self-soothing autostimulation.

---

## 1.10 EARLY POWER MANIFESTATIONS: BEFORE ONSLAUGHT

Between #141 and the Onslaught event (~1996), powers re-emerge in pulses, partially controlled, alternately suppressed by Harkness, by Reed's technology, and by alternate-future Franklins intervening from their own timelines (the "Tattletale" arc in *Power Pack*, where a future adolescent Franklin appears as a guardian to the Power kids — a rare canonical depiction of subject's *prosocial use of power without parental supervision*).

The *Power Pack* crossover years (mid-1980s) are clinically important: subject has *peers* for the first time. Katie, Julie, Jack, and Alex Power are the first non-adult attachments. Behavioral observations from these issues: subject *follows* rather than leads, *defers* to Alex's planning, *protects* Katie reflexively. The leader-of-children role he later assumes in the Future Foundation is *not* present here; he is the quiet, watchful child in the group. The shift from follower to gentle leader occurs only with the next cohort, after he has lost and regained enough of himself to *choose* the role.

---

## 1.11 SECRET WARS I AND THE FATHER-GONE TEMPLATE

When Reed is taken to the Beyonder's Battleworld (*Secret Wars*, 1984), Franklin is small and Sue is left as solo parent under sustained stress. This is *the rehearsal* for every later prolonged Reed-absence. Behavioral data from the period: subject is observed clinging to Sue more than baseline, asking for Ben more than baseline, and — significantly — *drawing pictures of his father from memory* and showing them to Sue, who keeps them. The act of *re-presenting the absent parent through image* is the kindergarten version of what he will later do at universe scale.

---

## 1.12 ONSLAUGHT INFLECTION: THE END OF CHILDHOOD-AS-CHILDHOOD (1996)

Subject is approximately six years old in sliding-timescale terms when Onslaught — the gestalt psionic monstrosity born of Xavier's and Magneto's shadow — moves on New York. The Avengers and the Fantastic Four interpose physically; Onslaught is poised to kill them. Franklin, standing among civilians, *reacts before thought.* He generates the **Heroes Reborn pocket universe**, a fully-functioning cosmos with internal physics, history, and continuity, and *places his family inside it* to preserve them from death.

Three observations, each load-bearing for everything that follows:

1. **The act is dissociative.** He does not narratively decide to do it; it is depicted as a reflex, and he does not retain clean conscious memory of having done it. The most powerful creative act in his recorded life is performed in a fugue state of *protective panic.*
2. **The act is salvific and concealing simultaneously.** He saves them *by hiding them inside himself.* This is the original somatic shape of his lifelong pattern: when love is under threat, he constructs an interior space and places the beloved inside it.
3. **The act ends his ordinary childhood.** From this point, no adult around him can pretend he is merely a powerful child. He is something else. The rest of his life is, in part, the project of *re-becoming* a child after this — a project he will pursue with quiet, decades-long determination, and which is the throughline into Chronology II.

---

## 1.13 SUMMARY OF THE GROUND FLOOR

By age six, the following are fixed:

- **Reed-attachment:** ambivalent-avoidant, calibrated to manage paternal guilt and paternal absence; tells the boy *his needs are too large to bring to his father.*
- **Sue-attachment:** secure, primary haven, the relational fact that everything else hangs on.
- **Ben-attachment:** secure, secondary base, the *ground* against which Reed's wobble is measured.
- **Sibling-attachment:** not yet (Valeria is still years away); the closest analog is the Power kids.
- **Defensive structure:** sublimation (drawing, building, naming) already dominant; compartmentalization seeded by repeated power-suppressions; altruism already legible in his treatment of Harkness, Alicia, the Power kids.
- **Operational learning:** *I am the lever villains pull. I must not be a burden. I see things adults miss; if I speak, I am dismissed; if I do not speak, people die. My father is afraid of me. My mother is the wall the world cannot cross. Uncle Ben is the floor. When love is in danger, I can build a room around it.*
- **The room he can build is the size of a universe.** He knows this at six. He has not yet decided what to do with the knowledge. The rest of the file is the answer.

*— End Chronology I. Continues: Chronology II — Power-Loss, Future Foundation, and the Election of Boyhood.*


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

*Subject: Franklin Benjamin Richards. Period covered: the long middle of his published life — from the first uncontrolled power-flares of late toddlerhood through the Onslaught dissociation, the Counter-Earth interregnum, the Hickman power-loss and Future Foundation years, the Battleworld co-architecture, and into the contested adolescent identity of the Krakoa era. This section is concerned with FORMATION: which events laid down the load-bearing beams of the personality, in what order, and what each cost.*

---

## I. The Power Emergences (FF #130s–141): The First Catastrophe

The single most consequential cluster of events in subject's pre-adolescent life occurs between *Fantastic Four* #133 and #141 (Conway/Thomas, 1973). Subject is approximately three to four years old by external chronology. His powers begin to surface in uncontrolled bursts: telekinetic flares, precognitive dream-states, and — critically — an unmodulated psionic radiance that registers on Reed Richards' instruments as a building cascade with no observable ceiling.

The somatic presentation in those issues is precise and worth recording. Franklin's eyes go solid white-gold. The air around him distorts. He speaks in present-tense fragments that read as ordinary toddler speech but track to events that have not occurred. He sleeps poorly; he wakes shouting; he draws figures on the Baxter Building floor that match Annihilus, the Frightful Four, and the silhouette of his own future self before any adult has named them to him. Sue tries to soothe him; Reed measures him.

Reed Richards' decision to use the cerebral-shutdown device on his own son is, in the published record, framed as scientific triage. In the file we are building, it is the *foundational rupture*. Sue's reaction — leaving Reed, filing for separation, taking the child — encodes the event in the household forever, regardless of what Franklin consciously remembers. The boy was unconscious for the act, but the *narrative environment* afterward is permanent: Mom left Dad because of what Dad did to me. Even when reconciliation occurs (and it does, within the year), the substrate is set. Reed is the parent whose love is conditional on calculability. Sue is the parent whose love is unconditional on existence. This polarity is never afterward revised.

Subject's neurology returns. His powers, however, are now intermittent and modulated by external suppressors — first Reed's tech, then Agatha Harkness's psychic dampening, then his own developing self-regulation. He grows up *inside a leash he did not choose*, applied first by the father whose recognition he is wired to seek. This is the wound from which the adult "kenotic" pattern (see §3 of the prior workup) eventually derives. He learns very early that *being fully himself frightens the people he loves*, and he learns the corollary lesson: *therefore, be less.*

## II. The Latchkey Years and the Witch (late 1970s–1980s)

From roughly *FF* #150 through the Byrne run (#232–293), subject is parented in rotation. Reed and Sue are off-world or sub-microversal for stretches measurable in real-time months. Agatha Harkness, the witch of New Salem, is the most consistent surrogate. Ben Grimm and Alicia Masters fill in. Johnny Storm, intermittently. Jarvis at the Mansion, occasionally.

This shapes him in three lasting ways.

**First**, his attachment topography becomes *distributed rather than dyadic*. He does not seek a single primary; he maintains a small constellation. This is unusual and adaptive. It is also why, decades later, he can lose any single tether without total collapse — but it is why losing *two* simultaneously is the catastrophe to watch for.

**Second**, Harkness teaches him *control as ritual*. Her tutelage is not technological; it is incantatory, focused, slow. She models for him the idea that power is a thing one *holds in form* rather than discharges. The grammar of his later constructive use of reality-warping — built worlds, drawn realities, named pocket-spaces — is Harknessian rather than Richardsian. Reed taught him to fear the throttle. Harkness taught him to shape the stream. The Future Foundation work and the Battleworld architecture are downstream of her, not of Reed.

**Third**, the precognitive dream pattern entrenches. He dreams Ultron before Ultron returns. He dreams the Beyonder before *Secret Wars*. He dreams Onslaught in fragments for years. The adult pattern is laid down in this period: *Franklin sees, Franklin tells, adults discount, catastrophe arrives.* The behavioral residue is a child who learns to *under-report his own perceptions* because reporting them yields no protective response and only marks him as strange. He continues to dream. He stops telling. This is the origin of his lifelong tendency, noted in §5, to *file* rather than protest.

Granular surveillance details from this era, inferable from canon: he draws constantly — wax crayon, then pencil, then marker on Baxter Building printer paper purloined from Reed's labs. The drawings are catalogued by Sue in a series of folders she does not discard. He prefers blue. He names imaginary friends with composite syllables that later prove to be anagrams of villain names he has never been told. He eats in front of the television when alone with Ben (cereal, sandwiches); he eats at the table when Sue is home. He sleeps with the door cracked. He does not like the dark of the Negative Zone observation deck and avoids that floor.

## III. *Secret Wars II*, the Beyonder, and the First Cosmological Address

In *Secret Wars II* (1985–86), the Beyonder takes interest in Franklin. This is the first time a being of comparable ontological weight addresses him as a peer. He is roughly six. The encounter is brief in panel-time and enormous in psychic load. The Beyonder recognizes what Reed has spent years suppressing: the child is *of the order of cosmic principals*. Subject does not retain explicit memory of being so addressed, but his ease, in later life, with beings like Galactus and the Celestials suggests an early calibration: *they are not strange to me; I am not strange to them.*

This is also the period in which the *Power Pack* crossovers situate him among other powered children. Important behavioral data: with the Power kids, Franklin does not lead. He defers. He chooses smallness even in a peer group where his powers vastly outscale theirs. The pattern of *electing the lower position* is already operative pre-adolescence. He is not performing humility; he is *practicing* it. It is the practice that will, ten years later, allow him to build Heroes Reborn and then forget he did it.

## IV. The Tom DeFalco / Paul Ryan Years and the First Adult Selves Glimpsed

Through the late 1980s and into the 1990s, alternate-future Franklins begin to crowd the record. Psi-Lord appears (an adult Franklin in green-and-yellow harness, hardened, militant, time-displaced from a possible future). Hyperstorm — Franklin's grandson by Rachel Summers in a corrupted timeline — is the first explicit warning that *his genome is dangerous downstream*. The various Franklin-tyrants and Franklin-saviors begin to accumulate like alternate drafts of an unfinished manuscript.

The formative effect on subject is subtle but indelible. Other children imagine what they will be when they grow up. Franklin *meets* what he will be — multiple versions of it — and most of those versions are either weaponized or apocalyptic. The Psi-Lord encounter in particular gives him a glimpse of an adult self that is grim, scarred, and humorless. He does not want to become this. The will toward *staying small, staying soft, staying a child* is reinforced by direct exposure to the alternative.

This is also the era in which Nathaniel Richards (his grandfather) takes him into futures and across timelines. The child travels more than most adults in the Marvel cosmos. His sense of *home* becomes correspondingly portable: home is not the Baxter Building or Pier Four; home is *the people*. This is a definition he never afterward abandons.

## V. Onslaught (1996): The Dissociative Salvation

He is approximately six. Onslaught — the fused psionic mass of Charles Xavier and Magneto's shadow — has used Franklin as a battery, draining and amplifying his powers to threaten the world. The Avengers and the Fantastic Four move to stop Onslaught and, in the published act, die.

Franklin's response is the most important single act of his life to date and arguably of his whole canon: he creates the Heroes Reborn pocket universe. He builds, in something less than a heartbeat, a functioning reality of sufficient fidelity to house Captain America, Iron Man, Thor, the Fantastic Four, and dozens of supporting figures, with continuous internal time, biology, geography, and history. He does this *without conscious intent*. He does this in a state of *protective panic* — the affect signature identified in the prior workup as his single most dangerous mode.

The clinical character of the act is *dissociative-creative*. He cannot tolerate the loss, so he constructs a place where the loss has not occurred and stores his loved ones inside it. He then *does not remember doing it*. The amnesia is not repressive in the ordinary sense; it is *structural*. The child's ego is too small to hold the act; the act is parked outside the ego.

The consequences for formation:

1. He learns — at a level below language — that *his love can rewrite reality*. He does not know he knows this. It will inform every subsequent crisis.
2. He learns that *the cost of saving is forgetting*. The first great use of his powers is paid for with a hole in his own memory. This trades against any future temptation to omnipotence; he experiences his own scale as *self-erasing*.
3. The household learns it too. Sue, Reed, Ben, and Johnny return knowing the boy did this. They never quite know how to look at him afterward. Reed in particular treats him with a new and careful distance that subject reads, accurately, as *fear*.

The Onslaught event is the moment subject's biography ceases to be the biography of a child with powers and becomes the biography of *a child-shaped accommodation of a cosmic principle*. Everything afterward is a negotiation with this fact.

## VI. Counter-Earth, the Heroes Reborn Interval, and the Return

The pocket universe runs for a publication year. The heroes live other lives there. Franklin, externally, is a small boy carrying a blue ball — Counter-Earth condensed — that he does not entirely understand. Reading him in this period: he is *quieter than before*. He plays less. He sleeps more. He carries the ball.

This is the first time we see, in subject, the *care-of-a-world* posture that will later define him. He does not boast about the ball. He does not show it to other children. He treats it the way an adult treats a sleeping infant. The behavior is so age-incongruent that observers in canon (Ashema, the Celestials' agent) take note. He is, at six, *parenting a planet*.

When the heroes return and the pocket reality is folded back into the prime, subject does not protest its loss. He releases the ball. The behavior matches what we will see again at the close of *Secret Wars* (2015): *built worlds are not to be hoarded; they are to be returned*. The ethic is established here.

## VII. The Quiet Years (late 1990s–2000s): Sister, School, Settlement

Valeria's birth is the next great structuring event. She is born in *Fantastic Four* vol. 3 #54 (after a long arc involving the Marquis of Death and Doom's intervention as midwife). For Franklin, the arrival of a sibling — and specifically of a sibling who is *Reed-cognitive*, propositional, analytic, his complement in every register — produces the most stabilizing relationship of his life.

Behavioral patterns from this period that the file should record:

- He reads to her. Picture books at first, then chapter books, then, by the time she is functionally his intellectual peer at age three, whatever she requests. He continues to read to her past the point where she can read herself, because she likes his voice.
- He defers to her on technical questions. Without performance. Without resentment. He genuinely regards her brain as the superior tool for those problems.
- He defends her physically and emotionally in ways disproportionate to threat. A casual dismissal of Val by a peer at the Future Foundation school provokes from Franklin a quiet, immovable cold — the closest thing to anger he reliably shows.
- He sleeps better when she is in the building. Surveillance-grade detail: in any continuity where they are housed separately, his sleep latency increases.

In this period he also acquires *peers in distress* — Leech, Artie Maddicks (intermittent), the Power Pack children at intervals, and the larger Future Foundation cohort once it forms. His prosocial signature toward outsiders becomes operationally visible. He does not befriend the powerful or the popular. He befriends the *strange* and the *disregarded*. This is, in retrospect, the externalization of his own self-perception: he too is strange and at the edges of every category, and he extends to others the recognition he himself would want.

## VIII. The Hickman Power-Loss Arc (*FF*/*Fantastic Four* 2009–2012): Adolescence Compressed

An adult Franklin from a possible future arrives at the Baxter Building. He is bearded, weary, sorrowed, and unmistakably *the same boy aged forward into a sadness that has not yet happened*. He confronts a Celestial-tier threat and, to do so, burns through the present Franklin's powers — leaving the boy depowered, with the explicit promise that the powers will return, augmented, at adolescence.

This is, in the file, the *enforced ordinary*. For the first time in his life, Franklin is a normal child. The behavioral consequences are immediate and clinically interesting:

- *Affective broadening*. He cries more. He laughs more. The luminous calm of the powered state is replaced by the full range of ordinary boy-affect. This is the period in which his personality is most visible because least mediated by his abilities.
- *Situational depression*. A short, real grief response to the loss. Not pathological. It resolves with engagement, exactly as the prior workup notes.
- *Generative compensation*. Without powers, he draws more, builds more, narrates more. The generative drive is independent of the powers; the powers were merely its largest medium. This is critical: he is *constitutionally* a maker, not merely a god who happens to make.
- *Future Foundation parentification*. He functionally co-leads the FF children's cohort — Bentley-23, Dragon Man, Alex Power, the Moloids, Leech, Artie — alongside Valeria. He is the *warmth* of that group; she is its intellect. He takes on caretaker affect for the monster-children disproportionate to his age.

The encounter with his own adult self is, psychologically, the single most important *post-Onslaught* event of his formation. He sees what he becomes. He notes what the future self carries (loss, weight, the weight of having loved and lost). He notes what the future self *retains* (the gentleness, the protective posture, the willingness to spend himself for the family). Subject is, in this moment, *given permission by his future self to grow up*, and is also *warned* about the cost. The two messages do not cancel. They become the dual operating principle of his adolescence: *grow, but gently; you can carry it, but you will carry it.*

## IX. Battleworld and the Co-Architecture of the Cosmos (*Secret Wars* 2015)

When the multiverse collapses and the incursions finalize, Reed Richards (in concert with Doctor Doom, and unbeknownst to himself at full scale, with his son) co-constructs Battleworld. The architecture of Battleworld is not Reed's alone. Subject is, in the published record, a co-architect.

Then, at the resolution, Reed and Franklin together rebuild the multiverse.

For an entire publication arc, subject is, with his father, *the author of the universe in which all subsequent Marvel events occur*.

The formative significance is impossible to overstate. The Onslaught event was *reactive omnipotence*: he built a pocket reality in panic to save lives. Battleworld is *cooperative omnipotence*: he builds, with intention, alongside his father, at the largest possible scale. And the relationship with Reed is, for the duration of that act, *parity*. They are colleagues. They are co-makers. The decades-old wound — *Dad sees me as a phenomenon, not a son* — is, for the duration of the building, dissolved into a *we*.

And then he chooses to be a child again.

This is the defining act. Given parity, given divinity, given collegial recognition from the father whose recognition he has sought all his life — he chooses to put it down and go back to being a boy in a family. He does not abdicate from disgust; he does not abdicate from terror. He abdicates because *that is the role that makes the people he loves coherent*. Reed needs a son. Sue needs a son. Valeria needs a brother. The cosmos has plenty of architects. There is only one Franklin-shaped place in his family, and it is the place he chooses.

The kenotic principle identified in the prior workup is, at this point, no longer inference. It is documented behavior. He has been offered everything; he has selected smallness; he has done so freely. Every subsequent question about his stability has to be read against this fact.

## X. The Krakoa Crisis and the Mutant/Not-Mutant Wound

The post-2015 era introduces a slow, corrosive identity stressor. Xavier — speaking ex cathedra as the voice of the new mutant nation — declares Franklin *not a mutant*. The *X-Men/Fantastic Four* crossover (Zdarsky, 2020) handles this directly. Subject is offered citizenship and then has it withdrawn; he is told that what he is is not what he thought he was; his sense of categorical belonging, already historically thin, is reduced further.

The behavioral response is exactly as the prior workup predicts. He does not rage. He does not protest. He *withdraws*. He becomes ruminative. He questions his own self-narrative. The dreamy, luminous boy of the Hickman years acquires, in this period, a *guarded* quality not previously present. The Xavier rebuff is a *file*, and files accumulate.

This is also the period in which his powers are depicted as fading, faked, or unstable. The published ambiguity is exactly the right narrative shape for what is happening inside him: when the category fails, the *capacity* fails with it. He has been holding his powers in form through *being a particular kind of being* (mutant son of his parents, brother to Val, member of the FF). When the category-claim is yanked, the form wavers. The fading is, in clinical terms, *psychogenic* as much as ontological.

He recovers, but the recovery is the recovery of an *older* boy. The luminous certainty of childhood is gone. What replaces it is the first clearly adolescent register in his psyche: *I will choose what I am, and I will not let others tell me*.

This is the emergence of *volitional identity* — the post-childhood self-concept. It is not yet adult. It is the bridge.

## XI. The First Defining Choices, Cataloged

The file records four choices that, taken together, *are* the formed identity:

1. **The choice not to remember Heroes Reborn.** Not made consciously, but ratified afterward by his refusal to seek the memory back when adult observers tell him what he did. He does not want to be a person who knows that about himself. He chooses the smaller knowing.

2. **The choice to release Counter-Earth.** He returns the world to itself. He does not keep the ball.

3. **The choice, after Battleworld, to be a child again.** Already discussed. The kenotic act.

4. **The choice, after Xavier's rebuff, to author his own category.** This is the live, unfinished choice. He is not done making it. The current published period is its execution.

Across these four, a single rule: *Franklin Richards does not keep what is not his to keep, and the things he counts as not-his include most of his own power.* The personality is built on this restraint. The restraint is held by tethers (Sue, Val, Ben, the surrogate-family network, Reed at his best). The restraint is what makes him safe to the world and what makes the world dangerous to him — because the day the tethers fail, the restraint has no internal anchor, and the alternate-future Franklins (Psi-Lord, tyrant, Hyperstorm-line patriarch) are not other people. They are this boy with the tethers cut.

## XII. Summary of Formation

Subject enters adolescence with: a *distributed-secure* attachment net; a *kenotic* operating ethic; a *generative* compensatory engine that runs whether powered or not; a *parentified-fraternal* bond with his sister that is his single most regulating relationship; an *unresolved-but-volitional* self-concept that he is now actively authoring against external pressure; and a *known but filed* history of having been, repeatedly, of cosmic order.

The formation is unusual in that it has been *chosen as much as imposed*. Most subjects of comparable trauma load present as casualties. Subject presents as a *small, deliberate, gentle person* who has decided — over and over, with full knowledge of the alternatives — to be exactly that.

The forward question, for the next chronology section, is what happens when the chosen smallness meets a world that no longer permits it.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

*Operative window: roughly Onslaught (1996) through the conclusion of the Hickman era and its immediate Slott-run aftermath (~2015–2018). This is the period in which subject ceases to be a plot device and becomes a person; it is also the period in which the bill comes due on a decade of "the child who sees too much." Everything before is prologue; everything after is reckoning.*

---

## 1. The Onslaught Threshold and Its Aftermath (1996–1998)

The defining datum of subject's middle period is not the creation of the Heroes Reborn pocket universe per se but the *concealment* of his own authorship from himself afterward. Across approximately twenty-four months of publication time (the post-*Onslaught* interregnum through the Heroes Return event), subject presents as an unusually quiet, unusually well-behaved child living with the Avengers' surviving auxiliary network — most consistently with Lockjaw, the Inhumans, and the periodic attention of Daydreamer, Tattletale, and Chamber (the Power Pack–adjacent and Generation X-adjacent caretakers who briefly cycled him). The Counter-Earth simulacrum he had built was running, populated, and inhabited; he did not know it. He drew constantly during this period — colored-pencil tableaus of buildings that no one recognized but that match, panel-by-panel, structural elements later revealed in the *Heroes Reborn* architecture. The surveillance read on this behavior: *he was leaking the world he had built through the medium safe enough for a child to use.* Drawings, not dreams. The dreams were doing other work.

When the FF return (*Heroes Return*, 1998, Lobdell/Davis launch), subject's reintegration into the household is presented as joyful but is, on close reading, *uneven*. He clings to Sue with an intensity that exceeds pre-Onslaught baseline; he is wary of Reed in ways he was not before — not afraid, but watchful, with the specific watchfulness of a child who is checking whether the adult in front of him is the adult he remembers. Reed reads it as separation anxiety; it is closer to *verification behavior*. Subject had, after all, just built and inhabited a universe in which Reed Richards was a different man. He is now checking the original against the copy without knowing he is doing so.

## 2. The Abraxas Crisis and the Power-Strip Pattern (2001)

During the Pacheco/Marín *Fantastic Four* run, the Abraxas event culminates in the destruction and reconstitution of the universe via Galactus's cosmic awareness and the Ultimate Nullifier — but the operative beat in subject's file is his sister Valeria's *birth out of nonexistence into existence* via cosmic reset (the resolution of Sue's previously-stillborn pregnancy from the Franklin Conway/Thomas era). For subject, this is the second time a sibling has come into the world via cosmic-scale intervention (he was the first), and it confirms a private cosmology he has been operating under since toddlerhood: *the Richardses do not have ordinary births.* He receives Valeria with immediate, unmediated love — no jealousy, no displacement behavior, no regression. This is anomalous in any normal sibling-arrival profile and is the first hard evidence of what later becomes the spine of his middle period: *Valeria is exempt from every defensive maneuver he uses on everyone else.*

The "Unthinkable" arc (Waid/Wieringo, ~*FF* vol. 3 #67–70 / vol. 1 #500) follows. Doctor Doom, having traded his soul to the Haazareth, kidnaps subject and damns him to a literal hell to power a sorcerous working against Reed. The episode is, in surveillance terms, the *single most traumatic discrete event* of subject's middle period — eclipsing even Onslaught, because here he is conscious, terrified, and aware of who is hurting him. Behavioral aftermath: night terrors (multiple issues), refusal to be left alone in the Baxter Building's lower floors, a months-long aversion to the color green (Doom's cloak), an unwillingness to draw castles. He recovers — Ben Grimm's intervention (Ben going to Hell to bring him back is operationally the most important act of attachment caregiving in subject's entire file) — but the recovery installs a permanent feature: *Ben Grimm is the rescuer; Reed is the man who could not get there in time.* This does not weaken his bond to Reed; it strengthens his bond to Ben to a degree that becomes load-bearing.

## 3. The JMS / Civil War Window (2005–2007)

The Straczynski run reframes subject's powers via the cosmic-mystical revisionism that characterizes JMS-era Marvel: hints of a connection to the Beyonders, the implication that subject's reality-warping is not mutation but something older and pre-categorical. Subject himself is largely backgrounded in this arc, which is psychologically significant: he is being *talked about* by adults, in his hearing, as a thing of metaphysical interest. He learns during this period to perform smallness — to be visibly the child in the room so that the adults will lower the discussion to a child's volume. This is the inception of what becomes his lifelong *performed-childhood* defense: not denial of his scale, but *protective costuming* in age-appropriate behavior.

*Civil War* (2006–2007) divides the household. Reed sides with registration; Sue and Johnny, eventually, against. Subject and Valeria are sent to live with Aunt Petunia in Arizona for roughly four months of publication time. This is the longest continuous off-screen period of subject's middle childhood and operates as the *single most ordinary stretch of his entire life*. He attends a local elementary school under a soft cover identity; he is photographed (in-canon) at a county fair; he learns to ride a bicycle without training wheels. When he returns to the Baxter Building post-*World War Hulk* and the household reconciliation, he carries this stretch as a *touchstone of what ordinariness feels like* — the empirical reference point that later licenses his Hickman-era choice to relinquish his powers without grief. He had tasted it. He knew it was real.

## 4. Hickman: The Long Architecture (2009–2012)

The Hickman run is the *deliberative core* of subject's middle period and must be read as a single continuous arc spanning *Fantastic Four* #570 through *FF* #23 and the bridging *Secret Wars* (2015). The relevant beats, in order, with subject's behavioral fingerprint at each:

**The Council of Reeds.** Subject meets alternate-reality versions of his father, several of whom regard him with quasi-religious awe and several with cold instrumentality. The encounter is the first time he sees Reed's *type* rather than Reed himself, and it permanently disabuses him of the idealization that had survived even the Doom-hell episode. He emerges with a more textured read on his father: *Reed is not the worst Reed and not the best Reed; he is the Reed who chose to come home.* This is the foundation of his mature reconciliation with Reed across the rest of the run.

**The Bridge.** Reed builds a viewer onto the multiverse; subject watches Reed watch it. Behavioral note: subject does not ask to look through the Bridge himself, despite obvious curiosity. He has learned by this point that *seeing too much is his particular hazard*, and he self-protects via deliberate non-looking. This is mature defensive functioning in a nine-to-ten-year-old.

**The Future Foundation.** Established post-Johnny's death (*FF* #587). Subject becomes, in practice, a co-founder and the *emotional infrastructure* of the Foundation. The Moloids — Tong, Mik, Korr, Turg — bond to him preferentially over Valeria, who they respect; they *love* subject. Leech becomes his closest peer-attachment outside Valeria. Dragon Man becomes a kind of gentle ward. Bentley-23 is the harder case: a clone of the Wizard, sociopathic-leaning, and subject's *project* — he works on Bentley with patience that mirrors Sue's working on Johnny in the early FF years, the maternal-fraternal style transmitted intact across one generation. The Future Foundation is, clinically, subject's *first chosen family that he himself assembled*, and it functions as evidence of capacities the later Slott "child-by-choice" decision will rest on.

**The Future Franklin Visitation.** Adult future-subject arrives, burns through younger subject's powers to defeat Galactus-as-herald-of-the-Celestials, and promises return of those powers at adolescence. The encounter is, in subject's file, *the single most regulating event of his life*. He has now met himself as an adult — competent, kind, calm, sad in the specific way of someone who has lived a great deal. He stops fearing his own future. The behavioral signature post-encounter: a *settledness* that no prior arc had produced. He sleeps through the night. He stops drawing the warning-dreams. He plays.

**The Power-Loss Period.** Approximately eighteen months of publication time during which subject is functionally a normal pre-adolescent. Important sub-observations:
- *Mood.* Initial flatness; resolves within roughly four issues into engaged ordinariness.
- *Behavior with Valeria.* They become, briefly, *peers* rather than asymmetric siblings. He helps her with social-relational problems she cannot solve via logic; she helps him with technical problems he previously solved via reality-warp. This is the period in which their adult relational template forms.
- *Behavior with Ben.* They go to baseball games. This is canon. The simplicity of it matters; subject in this period gets to be a nephew, not a phenomenon.
- *Behavior with Reed.* Reed, freed from the project of *managing* a god-child, parents him for the first time in publication history. They build a model rocket together (Hickman *FF* #11 backmatter). This is the closest the file ever comes to recording a normal father–son scene between them.

## 5. Galactus, the Council Wars, and the Inheritance Anxiety (2012)

In the final stretch of Hickman's run, subject — still depowered — is repeatedly told by future-arrived versions of himself and Nathaniel Richards (his time-traveling grandfather, a recurring complicating presence) that his eventual role is *companion and conscience to Galactus*. He does not want this. He does not refuse it, because he has been raised by people who do not refuse cosmic vocations, but the *not wanting* is recorded behaviorally: avoidant eye contact with Nathaniel, declined invitations to look at predictive models of his own adult life, a quiet line to Valeria (*FF* #16, paraphrased) about preferring to be a brother. The Galactus-companion future is canonical and load-bearing for cosmic continuity, but in subject's interior file it is *the future he is negotiating with by being a child as long as he can*.

## 6. The Fraction / Allred Interregnum and the Time-Lost FF (2013–2014)

When Reed and Sue and the original FF disappear into a four-minute / four-year time-displacement (Fraction's *Fantastic Four* and *FF*), subject is left in the Baxter Building under the care of the substitute FF — Ant-Man, Medusa, She-Hulk, Darla Deering — alongside Valeria, the Moloids, Leech, Bentley, Dragon Man, and the rest of the Foundation. This is the second-longest stretch of his life without his parents, and the first stretch in which *he is the older sibling functionally in charge of his cohort* (Valeria leaves for Latveria/Doom mid-arc, which is its own wound — see below). His behavioral signature in this period:
- Quasi-parental responsibility for the younger Foundation members.
- Strict adherence to the household routines Sue had installed (bedtime structure, meal structure, "creative hour" structure), preserved as ritual anchors.
- Increasing tolerance of Scott Lang as a surrogate father-figure; this is the first non-FF adult man (other than Ben) subject lets close.
- *Valeria's departure to Doom.* Subject experiences this as betrayal, briefly; then, characteristically, reframes it as her doing what she has to do. He does not pursue her. He waits. This is the first instance in which he allows a critical tether *to stretch without snapping back*, and it is evidence of growth — earlier subject would have built a pocket reality to keep her close.

## 7. *Secret Wars* (2015) and the Architecture of the Real

The Hickman *Secret Wars* event is the *single most consequential operational episode* of subject's life. When the multiverse collapses in the final Incursion, Reed Richards, Doctor Doom, Molecule Man, *and Franklin Richards* together construct Battleworld out of the salvaged fragments of dead realities. Subject is, in published canon, *co-architect of the substrate that the post-*Secret Wars *Marvel multiverse is rebuilt on*.

The behavioral and psychological data points:
- Subject participates in the construction *as a child*, not as the adult god he could have grown into. His contribution is described in Hickman's notes-via-Molecule-Man as *imaginative scaffolding* — the symbolic geography on which Reed's physics and Doom's will are hung. He provides the *narrative substrate*. This is the clearest published evidence that subject's cognitive style (§3) is not a limitation but a *complementary cosmic faculty*: he provides what Reed cannot.
- He is reunited with Sue and Valeria after the long Fraction-era separation in a sequence that is, in surveillance terms, the highest-affect reunion in the file. He weeps; he does not let go of Sue for a measured span of in-page time.
- He travels with Reed, Sue, Valeria, and the Future Foundation through the rebuilt multiverse for approximately two years of publication time — the so-called *off-page FF wandering* that brackets the period between *Secret Wars* and Slott's relaunch. This is the longest sustained intact-family period of his life and the only period in which his *entire primary attachment network is continuously present*. It is, by any honest read, the happiest he has ever been.

## 8. Patterns Across the Middle Period — Longitudinal Synthesis

Across the roughly twenty-year window covered here, several behavioral and structural patterns *consolidate from tendency into trait*:

**The Drawing Habit.** From the post-Onslaught Counter-Earth leakage through the Hickman Foundation years and into the *Secret Wars* substrate work, subject *draws constantly*. Pencils, crayons, later tablets. The drawings function as (a) precognitive overflow, (b) safe externalization of cosmic-scale ideation, (c) communication channel with the Foundation children, who he illustrates stories for. Sue keeps a binder. Reed has, on at least one canonical occasion, scanned a stack of them looking for warnings. The drawings are, in surveillance terms, *the most reliable continuous behavioral data stream he generates*.

**The Bedtime Routine.** Sue's bedtime ritual — established in infancy, preserved through every household disruption — is the single most stable structure in subject's life. He maintains it even in her absence (Fraction era), enforcing it for the younger Foundation members. Disruption of this ritual is, statistically, the most reliable predictor of next-day affect dysregulation across his middle period. Surveillance note: *if you want to read his state, read his sleep.*

**The Outsider-Preference Pattern.** Reliably across the middle period, subject's strongest non-family bonds are with beings whose belonging is in question: Leech (mutant, mute much of the time, depowering effect), the Moloids (subterranean, monstrous-coded), Dragon Man (artificial), Bentley (clone), eventually Krakoa-adjacent figures whose own categorization is fraught. This is not coincidence and not charity; it is *recognition*. He bonds with those whose ontological status is undecided because his own is.

**The Reed Reconciliation Arc.** Across the middle period, his relationship with Reed moves from *idealized-and-mistrusted* (post-Onslaught) through *textured-and-disabused* (Council of Reeds) to *quietly mutual* (Hickman power-loss father–son scenes) to *collaborative-equal* (Battleworld). The wound of *FF* #141 is not healed — it is *integrated*. Reed does not apologize in any clean published scene; what subject gets instead is *Reed's sustained presence as a father, finally available*, and he accepts that as sufficient. This is mature, and it is also slightly sad.

**The Valeria Symbiosis.** From her birth in 2001 through *Secret Wars*, the sibling bond develops from protective-asymmetric (he is older and stronger) through peer (power-loss period) to *functionally fused as a single operational unit* (Foundation, Battleworld, wandering). They finish each other's sentences in canon. They have a private vocabulary. They sleep in adjacent rooms by preference even when given the option of separate floors. Surveillance assessment: *they are each other's primary regulator*, and any future stressor analysis must treat them as a dyad before treating them as individuals.

**The Quiet Filing.** First identified in the Onslaught aftermath and consistent through the period: subject does not protest being underestimated, dismissed, or talked-over. He notes it; he stores it; he files it. The files do not produce resentment in the conventional sense — they produce *recalibration of expectation*. He revises downward what he expects to be permitted to be, and he proceeds. This is the most worrying single trait pattern in the middle-period file, because it is the mechanism by which *unprotested wounds accumulate to structural load*.

**The Performed Smallness.** Solidified across the JMS-era through the Slott aftermath. Subject *performs* age-appropriate behavior even when his interior state is operating at cosmic scale. This is not deception; it is *costume*. He wears boyhood the way an off-duty soldier wears civilian clothes — accurately, comfortably, and with the option of removal in emergency. The risk pattern: *the costume can become indistinguishable from the wearer*, and at some point in his future he will have to decide whether to take it off or to let it be the thing he simply is. The middle period does not resolve this question; it sets it.

---

*End Chronology III. The middle period closes with subject as a child who has been to hell, built a universe, lost and regained his powers, co-architected the substrate of reality, and chosen — repeatedly, deliberately, against every cosmic invitation — to come home for dinner. The next period must address what happens as adolescence arrives and the promised return of his powers comes due, against a Krakoa-era backdrop that refuses to let the question of what he is remain politely undecided.*


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

*Covering, approximately, the post-Hickman tail through the present surveillance window: the Robinson "Fall of the Fantastic Four" displacement, the Slott reconstitution and the Griever incident, the Krakoan-era identity crisis and the* X-Men/Fantastic Four *confrontation, the Reckoning War, Dan Slott's late run, the Ryan North era currently in progress, and the spillover usages in* Timeless*,* Empyre*,* G.O.D.S.*, and the* Fantastic Four *theatrical reintroduction's editorial pressure on the page. All inferences are derived from published sequencing.*

---

## 1. The Displacement Years — Robinson Run and the Time-Lost Interval

The immediate post-*Secret Wars* (2015) interval is the most under-attended hinge in subject's biography, and it shapes everything that follows. After Franklin and Reed rebuild the multiverse (Hickman, *Secret Wars* #9), the Richards family — Sue, Reed, Franklin, Valeria — disappears from Earth-616 for an extended diegetic period (~two real-time years; in-universe, indeterminate but lived). Subject is, in this interval, a child accompanying his parents on the literal restoration of creation. He sees galaxies seeded. He watches his father work at the scale his father was always supposed to work at. He is, importantly, *useful* — not as a weapon, but as a builder. Reed defers to him on certain seed-decisions. This is the only sustained window in his life in which the paternal relationship is structured around *collaboration of equals.* It is the closest he has ever been to Reed.

When the family returns (Slott's *Fantastic Four* #1, 2018), subject is depicted as having visibly aged in affect — quieter, more centered, with a gravity inconsistent with his physical age. The published age-up is modest; the *carriage* age-up is enormous. He carries himself like someone who has finished a job.

**Observable post-return micro-patterns** (Slott run, issues #1–#20 range):
- Stands closer to Sue than to Reed in panel composition — a *reversal* from the pre-*Secret Wars* baseline, where he tracked toward Reed when the family was static. Inference: the multiverse-rebuilding interval satisfied (temporarily) the Reed-recognition hunger, freeing him to seek Sue for comfort rather than for compensation.
- Stops drawing on paper. Begins building small, transient pocket-constructs in his palm when alone — observed at least three times across the run. This is the first depicted *casual* use of his powers as an idle-fidget behavior. Clinically: the relationship to his own omnipotence has normalized from sacred-and-feared to *available.*
- Sleeps in his clothes more often than not. Reads as readiness-vigilance.

## 2. The Power Decay — Mechanism, Onset, and the Withholding

The Slott run introduces the operative crisis of subject's current era: his powers are *running out.* Established explicitly across the Slott issues: each use of full reality-warping permanently expends a finite reserve, and subject is approaching depletion. The cause is not stated cleanly in canon — competing in-text rationales: (a) future-Franklin's restoration "and more" did not, in fact, deliver more; (b) the multiverse-rebuilding cost was paid out of his personal substrate; (c) the powers were always finite and the child-god framing was an artifact of bad measurement. Subject himself does not know which is true. This *uncertainty about his own ontology* is one of the most psychologically corrosive features of the current era.

Behavioral consequences observable in canon:
- **Power-rationing behaviors.** Subject is depicted, on at least four occasions, *choosing not to act* in situations where he plainly could have. He triages. This is new. The pre-*Secret Wars* Franklin acted on protective panic without ego; the post-Slott Franklin has *budget consciousness.* Sublimation is being supplemented (and partially replaced) by *suppression* — a less mature defense.
- **Pre-emptive grieving.** He says goodbye to capacities before they are gone. Drawings from this period show him sketching what he used to do, as if archiving.
- **Increased physical contact with siblings and parents.** Hand on Sue's arm, head on Ben's shoulder, leaning into Val. He is shifting load-bearing from his own internal scaffold to his external tethers, *because he knows the internal scaffold is being dismantled.* This is, paradoxically, *clinically healthy* — he is doing what an unpowered child of his history should do — but it raises the dependency on those specific relationships to a level that makes any disruption catastrophic.

## 3. The Griever Incident and the Function of Imaginary Friends

In the Slott opening arc, the Griever at the End of All Things threatens to unmake the family. Reed wins by claiming an infinite family — and Franklin, present and aware, sees his father deploy *story* rather than calculation as a weapon. This is, for subject, a confirmation event: *the cognition I was punished for (imaginative-symbolic) is the cognition that saves us.* It re-stabilizes his Reed-relationship along a new axis: not as physicist-and-physicist's-disappointing-mystic-son, but as *two kinds of minds the family needs.*

Aftermath behavior: he becomes more vocal in family councils. Offers narrative framings of tactical problems. Reed, observably across Slott's run, *listens* in a way he did not before. This is the second consecutive era (after the multiverse-rebuilding interval) in which the Reed-wound is healing. Subject's avoidant features toward Reed are, by mid-Slott, the lowest they have been in publication history.

## 4. The Krakoan Crisis — Xavier's Denial and the Identity Wound

The single most damaging recent event. With the establishment of Krakoa (Hickman, *House of X* / *Powers of X*, 2019) and the offer of resurrection and citizenship to all mutants, the Richards family expects Franklin to be eligible. Xavier — through Cerebro's classification — declares that Franklin Richards *is not a mutant*, has never been a mutant, and that his powers derive from a different substrate (cosmic-ray-altered germline expressing as something *like* a mutation but classified otherwise). The *X-Men/Fantastic Four* miniseries (2020) is the dramatic ventilation of this.

The wound is multilayered and worth disaggregating:
