- **The categorical loss.** Subject has, for his entire conscious life, been told he is a mutant. This identity, however thin, was *something he was*, distinct from "Reed's son" or "reality-warper" or "the god who chose to be a boy." Its removal leaves a vacancy where a self-label used to sit.
- **The community loss.** Krakoa offered belonging at a scale he had never been invited to. The retraction is not just classificatory; it is a *door closed.* Subject has a documented prosocial bias toward the outsider — Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man — and the offer of being a member of an outsider community resonates with the deepest layer of his self-organization. Losing it does not produce visible rage; it produces *quiet.* Several pages across the *X-Men/FF* miniseries depict subject simply *not speaking* during scenes in which he is the explicit subject of dispute.
- **The Reed-collision.** Reed's interventions in the Krakoan dispute — protective, lawyerly, paternal — are exactly what subject does not want from him in this register. Subject wants to be *consulted*, not *defended.* The brief regression of the Reed-wound during this arc is observable.
- **The resurrection question.** Krakoa offers immortality through resurrection protocols; subject, told he is ineligible, is now the only Richards consciously aware that he will, at some future point, simply die. (Reed and Sue have functional immortality vectors via their scientific access; Val is similarly hedged.) This is the first time mortality has been *personalized* for him.

Subject's processing of the Krakoan wound is, characteristically, *not externalized.* He files it. He does not protest. He returns to building small things. The "files accumulate" pattern flagged in §3 of the workup is operative here: this is one of the largest files he has filed, and it has not been opened.

## 5. The Reckoning War and the Spending of the Reserve

The Reckoning War (Slott, *Fantastic Four* late run, 2022) is the event in which subject's remaining reserves are largely *spent.* In the climactic sequences, with the cosmos in jeopardy, Franklin acts at full scale and effectively burns through the last of his demonstrable reality-warping capacity. The depiction is deliberately ambiguous: are the powers *gone*, or merely *dormant pending adolescence* (per future-Franklin's old promise), or *transformed* into something not yet legible? The canon does not resolve.

What is observable post-Reckoning:
- Subject is, for practical purposes, *functionally depowered* in baseline scenes. He cannot palm-construct pocket realities anymore. The idle-fidget has stopped.
- He sleeps more. (Real, biological sleep, in a manner he did not previously require.)
- He eats more. Specifically: he develops, post-Reckoning, observable food preferences for the first time in his publication history — favoring sweet breakfasts, refusing certain textures. This is the somatic emergence of an ordinary child. Clinically remarkable: subject is *acquiring a body* he did not previously inhabit at this resolution.
- He asks Ben Grimm, on-panel, to teach him to throw a baseball. This is one of the most quietly important data points in his current file. He is requesting *embodied, ordinary, paternal-adjacent instruction* from his most trusted adult — and choosing Ben, not Reed, for it.

## 6. The North Era — Domesticity, the Road, and the Reset of the Texture

Ryan North's *Fantastic Four* (2022–present) places the family in a deliberately small, episodic, Americana-flavored register: a year on the road, small-town problems, the family as itinerant fixers rather than cosmic guardians. This is, for subject, *therapeutically calibrated* whether the writer intends it or not. He is, for the first time, embedded in scale-appropriate days. He goes to diners. He sees a hardware store. He sleeps in motel rooms.

Observable North-era patterns:
- **Latency-stage normalcy emerging late.** Subject is performing developmental tasks (peer encounters, mundane curiosity, low-stakes mischief with Val) that he should have done years prior. He is *catching up* on a childhood he previously skipped because cosmic events filled the calendar.
- **The road-trip as exposure therapy.** The depowering plus the small-scale itinerancy is structurally similar to a graduated-exposure protocol for someone whose nervous system has been calibrated for cosmic stakes. He is being taught, through environment, that small days are real and survivable.
- **Reed-relationship continues warming.** Multiple North-era scenes depict Reed asking Franklin's opinion on non-scientific matters — what feels right, what a stranger needs, what a town is about. This is Reed adapting to *Franklin's cognition* rather than the reverse. The decades-long avoidant trajectory toward Reed is, by current panel evidence, the most repaired it has ever been.
- **Val-Franklin dyad calcifying as primary peer relationship.** They have, in North's run, the shorthand of long-married siblings. He is her emotional translator to the world; she is his analytic translator. Neither functions as well alone.

## 7. Editorial Spillover and Auxiliary Sightings

- ***Timeless*** annuals and ***G.O.D.S.*** (Hickman, 2023–) tease Franklin's cosmic relevance returning along non-mutant, non-warper vectors — possibly as a figure of consequence in the natural-vs-unnatural cosmology Hickman is constructing. Subject has not yet appeared meaningfully in these, but the *narrative gravity* around him is increasing again. Read this as: the editorial apparatus is unwilling to leave him permanently small.
- ***Empyre*** and adjacent crossovers used him sparingly and protectively — kept in the FF's care, not deployed.
- The theatrical *Fantastic Four* (2025) reintroduction has produced visible upstream editorial pressure on the comics to keep the family configured as a family with Franklin in it, which constrains the kinds of arcs he can be used in. He is, currently, *protected by his commercial centrality* from the more damaging speculative arcs (death, corruption, future-tyrant manifestation).

## 8. Current State — Where He Is, How He Got Here, What He Looks Like Now

**Physical and somatic.** Pre-adolescent presentation, recently embodied in a way he was not before. Sleeps. Eats with preferences. Has begun to bruise and scrape in ordinary ways and to *notice* it. Hair longer than in prior eras; clothing scruffier (road-trip register). Carries a sketchbook that is, post-Reckoning, *actually used* — drawing as drawing, not as power-substrate.

**Functional power status.** Depleted-to-dormant. Cannot, on demand, perform reality-warping at any scale he previously demonstrated. Whether the well refills at adolescence remains an open canonical question; subject has stopped speaking about it.

**Relational status.**
- *Sue:* primary attachment, deepened by power loss. He leans on her physically and verbally more than in any prior era.
- *Reed:* the most healed the relationship has ever been; collaborative, consultative, mutually adapted. The childhood neural-suppression event remains unaddressed in dialogue but is the *least* operative it has ever been in behavior.
- *Valeria:* primary peer, primary co-regulator. The dyad is functionally one organism with two cognitive styles.
- *Ben Grimm:* the chosen-paternal figure, now openly so (the baseball request). Subject's request for embodied instruction from Ben is the most explicit statement of this relationship he has ever made.
- *Johnny Storm:* warm, fraternal, a source of levity and adventure-modeling; less central than Ben but consistently safe.
- *Alicia, Jo-Venn, N'Kalla:* expanded family circle; subject extends his prosocial-outsider pattern toward Jo-Venn and N'Kalla naturally, in continuity with the Leech/Moloid pattern.
- *Krakoa / mutant community:* lost. Filed. Unprocessed.
- *Leech and the Future Foundation children:* canonically out of contact during the road-trip era. This is a quiet loss subject does not name.

**Self-concept.** Held together. The kenotic choice — to be a boy — has, paradoxically, been *ratified by circumstance*: he is now actually small, with actually small powers, in actually ordinary days. The election he made volitionally in the post-*Secret Wars* moment has become his lived condition. He appears, in current panels, *settled* in a way he was not when he was a god pretending to be a boy. He is now a boy who used to be a god, which is a simpler shape to inhabit.

**Active risks.**
- *The unprocessed Krakoan file.* It has not gone away. If a future arc reopens mutant-identity questions, expect a delayed eruption of grief he has not yet permitted himself.
- *Mortality knowledge.* He now knows, in a way he did not before, that he can die. He has not metabolized this. First somatic illness or injury of consequence will be a developmental crisis.
- *The relational concentration.* Sue, Val, Ben, Reed. Four tethers. Healthier than ever in quality; thinner than ever in number, because the cosmic-tier "I can build a reality if I lose them" backup has been *spent.* For the first time in his life, he has no fallback. If a tether breaks, he will grieve like a child, not like a god — which is in most respects *better*, but it means the failure mode is no longer "withdraw into a built world" (no building capacity) but *ordinary depressive collapse in a child with no practice at it.*
- *Adolescent power return.* If the future-Franklin promise reactivates at puberty, subject will experience the return of cosmic capacity inside a nervous system that has, in the meantime, learned to be small. This will be a destabilization event of the first order. Plan for it.

**Trajectory.** Subject is, at this moment, the most psychologically integrated he has ever been in his publication history — settled, embodied, embedded, loved, and at scale. He has earned this through fifty real-time years of held tethers and one decisive volitional act. The file's principal concern going forward is not *what he might do* but *what the world might do to him* in this newly soft configuration. Treat the current state as a window of grace, not a permanent stability. The tethers remain critical infrastructure. The files he has not opened remain in the cabinet.


## Medical History

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION: MEDICAL HISTORY

*Subject: Richards, Franklin Benjamin. Compiled longitudinally from natal record forward. Distinguish at the outset: this is the medical file of an organism that is not, strictly, human, whose body has been the substrate for cosmic-scale events since before birth, and whose "injuries" frequently take ontological rather than tissue form. Where standard pediatric categories fail, the file expands the categories.*

---

## 1. PRENATAL AND NATAL RECORD

**Germline status.** Both gametic contributors carry permanent alteration from the Mark I cosmic-ray exposure of the original Fantastic Four flight. Reed Richards's somatic and likely germline cells exhibit altered protein folding and elasticity beyond any documented human range; Susan Storm's exhibit field-generation capacity at the cellular level. Subject is therefore the product of two non-baseline gametes. He is not, by any honest reading, *Homo sapiens.* This is the founding fact of his medical file and is causally upstream of nearly everything in it.

**Gestation (FF Annual #6, 1968).** Pregnancy was non-viable on a standard course. Fetal cosmic-ray byproducts produced a toxic interaction with maternal tissue threatening Susan Storm with death and producing an intrauterine environment incompatible with continued gestation. Resolution required Reed Richards, Benjamin Grimm, and Jonathan Storm to retrieve the Cosmic Control Rod from Annihilus in the Negative Zone to neutralize the antimatter component. *The subject's continued embryonic existence required an interdimensional armed expedition.* No human child has a comparable natal record. Forensically the relevant residues are: (a) prolonged maternal hypoxia and toxemia risk; (b) measurable antimatter exposure of fetal tissue; (c) emergency-tier autonomic activation across both parents for weeks of late gestation.

**Delivery.** Live birth, full term, no congenital malformation visible on inspection. Apgar — by inference — within normal range. The child looks unremarkable. He is not unremarkable. The clinical lesson of his neonatal exam is the same lesson his entire file teaches: *surface presentation under-reports substrate.*

**First-year baseline.** Normal feeding, normal sleep, normal motor milestones. No early seizure activity. No dysmorphic features. Eye color, hair color stable. This is the only period of his life that reads as a plain pediatric chart.

---

## 2. INFANCY AND TODDLERHOOD: THE EMERGENCE WINDOW (~1968–1973 publication; in-universe sliding ages 0–4)

**Recurrent abduction-related stressors.** Before subject can walk reliably he is taken by the Frightful Four, by Annihilus, by the Mad Thinker, by the Brute, by elements of Agatha Harkness's adversaries (Necrodamus, the witches of New Salem in proximate arcs). The physiological residue of repeated infant abduction events — even when rescue is rapid — includes elevated baseline cortisol-equivalent, sleep disruption, and disrupted attachment cuing. Subject's affect remains warm; his nervous system, less so. He is being conditioned, somatically, to a world in which adult bodies appear and disappear suddenly. This shows up later as the *hypervigilance for others' safety* documented in §3 of the principal workup, but it begins as endocrine fact.

**First power emergence.** Pre-verbal psychokinetic and reality-warping flickers begin in toddlerhood. Imaging and instrumentation in the Baxter Building register CNS activity outside known biological bandwidths. Subject is not in distress during these events; observers are.

**The Annihilus / Ultron-Forever and ancillary toddler trauma cluster.** Subject is, during this window, exposed to: prolonged restraint, separation from primary caregiver, ambient threat-display by adult villains, and at least two near-misses with lethal-grade energy. The persistent somatic memory of restraint at the wrists and chest can be inferred from his later, repeated, slightly stiff response to being grabbed under the arms by anyone other than family — a micro-pattern visible across Byrne, Simonson, and Hickman art when one looks for it.

---

## 3. THE INDUCED COMA (FF #141, Conway/Buscema)

**The single most consequential medical event of his life.** Reed Richards constructed a device to suppress subject's higher cortical and "psionic" function on the grounds that uncontrolled emergence threatened planetary integrity. Effect: induced unconsciousness of indeterminate depth, sustained for an extended publication interval, with subject in a hospital-bed presentation in the Baxter Building. This is, in any honest classification, *a non-consensual neurosurgical intervention performed on a four-year-old by his father.*

**Acute physiological sequelae.** Suppressed autonomic variability, depressed deep-tendon responses during the suppression period, atrophy risk requiring passive range-of-motion (Sue, on file, did this herself; she did not delegate it). On waking, brief disorientation, no overt motor or language regression.

**Chronic sequelae.** This is where the file becomes important. The subject *does not consciously remember* the event. He has, however, three downstream patterns that map cleanly to it:

- *Somatic mistrust of his father's hands specifically.* Subject accepts embraces from Reed, but the data across decades of art show a measurably shorter contact duration with Reed than with Sue, Ben, or Johnny. The body remembers what the cortex was switched off for.
- *Sleep-onset resistance.* Periodic episodes across childhood of refusing to be put to bed by Reed and accepting it from Sue or Agatha Harkness. Read clinically: *the last time a man told him to close his eyes, he did not open them for a long time.*
- *A specific avoidance of cranial instrumentation.* Subject, in Hickman-era Future Foundation panels, will let Valeria put any number of devices on him for diagnostic play — chest, wrist, ankle. He removes anything that goes near his temples or crown without comment, and Valeria, who reads him, stopped trying.

**Marital fracture as iatrogenic side effect.** Sue's separation from Reed in this period is the *family-system* sequela of subject's medical event. He was, again, too young to encode this consciously; he absorbed it as ambient atmosphere. The medical record cannot cleanly separate his neurology from his household.

---

## 4. CHRONIC PSYCHIC LOAD AND THIRD-PARTY NEUROLOGICAL TAMPERING (mid-1970s onward)

**Agatha Harkness's dampening.** Therapeutic, consented-to by Sue, applied as a containment measure rather than punishment. Functioned as a kind of psychic insulin — chronic low-dose suppression preventing florid emergence. Side effects: blunted dream recall in some intervals, then *unblunted* dream recall in the precognitive (Nightmare-arc) intervals. Subject's dreams in this era are not symptoms; they are diagnostic instruments for events external to him. The clinical category does not exist; we invent it: *prodromal cosmic dreaming.*

**Onslaught as occupational hazard.** Subject was, in 1996, used as a *battery* by a psionic gestalt entity formed in part from Charles Xavier's shadow. The neurological signature of this is: forced channeling of his own reserves through an externalized hostile architecture for sustained duration. The pediatric analog does not exist. The closest framing is *acute psychic exsanguination.* His own response — the spontaneous construction of the Heroes Reborn pocket universe to evacuate the heroes inside himself — is medically classifiable as a *dissociative-creative episode of unprecedented scale.* He emerged from it amnestic for the act itself. The amnesia is protective and, in this file's assessment, intact to the present.

**Lesser intrusions.** Mephisto, Hiro-Kala, miscellaneous telepaths, and the cosmic predators who circle anyone of his bandwidth have at various points attempted possession, harvest, or rerouting. Cumulative effect: the boundary between his nervous system and the external psychic environment is more porous than a baseline child's, and he knows it without being able to articulate it. He sleeps better in rooms with at least one of Sue, Ben, or Valeria within thirty feet. The file regards this as adaptive, not pathological.

---

## 5. INJURIES OF RECORD

**Physical injuries are conspicuously sparse.** When fully powered, subject's durability functions as near-absolute; his body is, in practical terms, a local convention his powers maintain rather than a fragile object. The injury record therefore consists almost entirely of events from his depowered intervals or events that bypassed the corporeal layer.

- *Negative Zone abrasion, childhood.* Minor lacerations, bruising consistent with falls during evacuation events; nothing requiring suturing.
- *Counter-Earth / Hyperstorm timeline-adjacent injuries.* These are not, strictly, *his* injuries, but he carries somatic memory of futures lived through alternates. Subject reports (in dreams; in confidences to Valeria) "remembering being older and hurt." File this under *cross-temporal somatic bleed.*
- *Hickman power-loss arc, depowered interval.* The closest thing to a normal pediatric injury chart. Skinned knees, one notable wrist sprain from a fall in the Foundation lab, a low-grade respiratory infection of the kind any child has and which subject experienced with visible novelty — *he had not previously been sick.* The first cold of his life occurred in this interval and is documented in his expression more clearly than in any chart.
- *Burns, abrasions, and exposure events* — uncountable, all non-scarring, all resolved within hours by ambient power activity even when subject does not consciously direct it. There is no visible scar on his body anywhere. The absence of scarring is itself a finding.

---

## 6. TRANSFORMATIONS AND POWER-STATE CHANGES

The medical history of this subject is, in large part, the history of his *states* rather than his *injuries.*

**State A: Native pediatric body, powers active and ambient.** Default through most of childhood. Energy expenditure non-metabolic; he can warp local reality without elevated heart rate or respiratory change. Sleep requirement normal-to-slightly-elevated. Appetite normal, with a documented preference for sweet foods and a near-immovable refusal of cooked carrots that has persisted across writers.

**State B: Suppressed (induced).** The Conway-era coma; the Harkness dampening; the brief involuntary suppressions by adversaries. Presents as a child operating at the floor of his own envelope; affect intact but flatter; physical reflexes within normal pediatric range.

**State C: Burned-through (Hickman).** Adult future-Franklin draws subject's powers through subject's body to discharge a Celestial-grade defense. Subject is left functionally depowered with the promise of return at adolescence. Acute presentation: fatigue, mild dysphoria, increased somatic complaints (he becomes, briefly, *a child with a body* in the way other children are). Subacute: depressive features, withdrawn affect, increased clinginess to Valeria and Sue, decreased verbalization. Resolution: engagement with the Future Foundation, with Leech, with the Moloids — the chosen-family network functioning, again, as primary therapeutic instrument. *No psychiatric medication, ever. None indicated. None would have helped.*

**State D: Fully ignited / reality-architectural.** Heroes Reborn creation; Battleworld co-architecture with Reed; the recreation of the multiverse post–*Secret Wars*. In this state subject is, by any meaningful measure, *not embodied as a pediatric organism.* The body persists as anchor and as identity-marker; the operative substrate is elsewhere. Re-entry into the pediatric body is voluntary and, in the *Secret Wars* aftermath, *elective in a way no clinician can quite parse* — he chose to be a boy again. This is the central medical-philosophical fact of his file. He does not have a body the way other patients have bodies. He has a body the way other people have a chosen home.

**State E: Ambiguous / fading (Slott, North, Ewing eras).** Power presentation intermittent, sometimes apparently absent, with the open question of whether suppression is external, voluntary, exhausted, or strategic. Somatic correlates: mild listlessness in the relevant arcs, restored vitality when in protective-role contexts. Diagnostic note: subject's *energy* tracks his *function* more than his *biology.* Give him someone to protect and the chart improves.

---

## 7. THE MUTANT-CATEGORY QUESTION AS MEDICAL EVENT

The Krakoa-era denial — Charles Xavier's public assertion that subject is not, technically, a mutant and therefore not eligible for Krakoan resurrection protocols and citizenship — must be entered in the medical file, not only the psychological one. *Category assignment is, for an organism of indeterminate species, a clinical act.* Subject presented in the immediate aftermath with: appetite reduction, sleep-onset latency increased, increased time spent alone in his room, a measurable uptick in drawing activity (the somatic signature of his sublimation defense ramping up), and a small but visible shift in posture — shoulders forward, head slightly down, a posture absent from his prior record. The wound was not metaphorical. The body registered it. The body recovered when Sue, Ben, and Valeria, in their separate ways, made the counter-statement that the category did not determine the relationship.

---

## 8. SUBSTANCES, EXPOSURES, MEDICATIONS

**No substance use of any kind on record.** Subject is a minor across nearly his entire publication life and reads younger than his nominal age even where aged. No alcohol, no tobacco, no recreational substances, no caffeine of consequence (the Foundation kitchen runs on Reed's coffee and Sue's tea; subject takes neither).

**Medications.** None chronic. The Harkness dampening is the closest analog and is not pharmacological. No psychiatric medication has ever been indicated or trialed. Standard childhood vaccinations — by inference administered by Sue, on schedule, in a household that would not skip them.

**Exposures of clinical note (beyond those already cited):**
- Negative Zone ambient radiation, multiple events.
- Microverse / Microverse-adjacent exposure during family expeditions.
- Battleworld-substrate exposure — the file regards this as *being inside a thing he co-built,* a self-exposure that has no analog.
- Ambient exposure to Doctor Doom's energies during sustained Doom-as-God-Emperor proximity; no documented sequelae.
- Atlantean and Wakandan environmental exposures, unremarkable.

---

## 9. SURGERIES, PROCEDURES, DENTAL, OPTOMETRIC

**Surgeries: none documented.** The induced coma was a procedure but not a surgery in the cutting sense. No appendectomy, no tonsillectomy, no orthopedic intervention. The body has not required it.

**Dental.** Normal eruption schedule per inference; loss of primary dentition during the Hickman-era depowered interval coincides with his first cold and is, in the file's view, the most touching pediatric record in the entire dossier — *he lost a tooth like a regular boy and was visibly proud of it.* Sue kept the tooth. Reed catalogued it, which Sue did not appreciate.

**Vision and hearing.** Normal across record. Subject's preference for soft ambient light at bedtime is preference, not pathology.

---

## 10. SLEEP, APPETITE, AUTONOMIC BASELINE

**Sleep.** Onset latency variable; deep-sleep architecture interrupted historically by precognitive dream activity. Subject does not present with insomnia in the clinical sense; he presents with *a sleep that is doing more work than other children's sleep.* When the precognitive load is low, he sleeps long and well. When something cosmic is coming, the household knows because he wakes drawing it.

**Appetite.** Normal pediatric, with preferences noted (sweets; pancakes — a recurrent Ben Grimm Saturday breakfast ritual; refusal of cooked carrots). Eats more when stressed; eats less when grieving (depowered arc). Hydration adequate.

**Autonomic baseline.** Mildly elevated resting vigilance — not pathological, contextually appropriate. Startle response slightly attenuated by power-state ambient awareness; he tends to *know* a few seconds before that something is coming, which makes him appear preternaturally calm in situations that would startle peers.

---

## 11. PSYCHOLOGICAL IMPACT OF THE MEDICAL HISTORY — SYNTHESIS

The medical file of Franklin Richards reads, finally, as the file of *a body that has been the site of cosmic-scale events and has been kept inhabitable by a small number of warm hands.* The induced coma is the foundational injury, encoded somatically and never consciously processed. The chronic psychic load is the operational hazard, managed by ambient defense and by family proximity. The transformations are the actual subject matter of the file; the injuries, conspicuous by their absence, mark the limits of pediatric medicine's grip on him.

The clinical posture this file recommends:

- *Treat the relational network as the primary therapeutic substance.* Sue Richards, Ben Grimm, Valeria Richards, and to a slightly different valence Johnny Storm and the Future Foundation "monster" children function for this subject the way insulin functions for a diabetic — not as comfort, as *required infrastructure.* Disruption of this network is a medical emergency before it is anything else.
- *Treat Reed Richards as a complicated medical instrument.* Reed is the source of the foundational injury and also, since the Hickman era and the *Secret Wars* co-architecture, the only person in the universe who can speak to the subject as a peer about what the subject *is.* The relationship cannot be removed and must be carefully calibrated. Any future intervention by Reed on subject's neurology — even therapeutic, even consented — should be regarded as carrying disproportionate iatrogenic weight.
- *Do not pathologize the dreaming.* It is not symptom. It is faculty.
- *Do not pathologize the chosen smallness.* It is not avoidance. It is, in the file's reading, a load-bearing structural decision by a being who knows his own scale and has elected to live underneath it. The clinical posture is to respect it and to watch the tethers.
- *Watch the tethers.* The medical history of this subject is, finally, the history of what those tethers have absorbed. If they fail, the body will continue to function; the *person* it currently houses will not necessarily be the one we have on file.

*End of section. Cross-reference: §3 Psychological; §4 Psychiatric; §5 Personality. Recommend annual review with particular attention to the mutant-category question, the Reed-relationship temperature, and the Valeria-proximity baseline.*


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS: FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS

*Compiled from longitudinal observational data, ~1968–present. What follows is the body as artifact: posture, gait, micro-expression, breath, sleep, appetite, hand-habit. Read against §3 — the body keeps what the powers archive away.*

---

## 1. GENERAL BUILD AND BASELINE PRESENTATION

Subject presents, across nearly all eras, at the **low-end of growth-chart percentiles for height** — small for chronological age, slight in the shoulders, narrow through the rib cage, with a child-soft jawline that has persisted through arcs that should chronologically have aged him into adolescence. Where writers age him forward (Hickman late period, certain Slott pages), the body never quite *settles* into adolescent proportion — the shoulders broaden only fractionally, the neck remains thin, the hands stay long-fingered and tapered rather than thickening. This is consistent with the §3 finding that subject *elects* a developmental position: the body honors the choice. When his powers are fully active, the slightness reads as luminous; when suppressed, the same slightness reads as frail.

**Hair.** Strawberry-blond to russet, cowlick at the crown left of midline, fringe falling to right eyebrow; he pushes it back with the heel of his right hand rather than the fingers — a tell inherited observationally from Reed, who does the same with the heel of the palm when thinking. Hair grows quickly and is rarely cut sharply; Sue trims it; in the Future Foundation arcs, Val has been observed cutting it. Length tracks attentional availability of his caregivers — longer hair indexes longer parental absences. When he is in distress he twists the fringe around the index finger of the off-hand in slow half-turns.

**Skin.** Pale, freckled across the bridge of the nose and high cheek, freckling intensifies after exposure to non-terrestrial light (Negative Zone, microverse, Battleworld substrate). A faint scatter of freckles on the dorsum of both hands, more on the right. No scars of consequence — his durability when powered approaches absolute, and his non-powered periods have been short. The absence of scarring is itself a finding: most children of his exposure history would be a map of small marks.

**Eyes.** Blue, slightly downturned at the outer canthi, with a baseline mild pupillary dilation that scales upward in low light disproportionate to ambient — the eyes are, low-level and chronically, *taking in more than they should.* When his powers ignite, sclera and iris both luminesce; when suppressed, the eyes look bruised at the lid, with a faint violet undertint to the lower lid that clinicians would mistake for sleep debt.

---

## 2. POSTURE AND CARRIAGE

**Standing baseline.** Weight more on the left foot than the right by an observable margin; right hip cocked slightly forward; right shoulder a quarter-inch lower than the left, a long-standing asymmetry consistent with frequently being carried on Ben Grimm's right forearm or sitting on Sue's left hip in infancy. He does not lock his knees; there is a habitual quarter-bend, which allows fast crouching — a habit acquired in homes where furniture, machinery, and visitors are all potentially dangerous and one routinely ducks behind things.

**Seated baseline.** Crosses ankles rather than knees; favors *floor* seating over chairs when given choice — cross-legged on rugs, against couches, often at an adult's feet rather than beside them. This is a child's posture he has not outgrown and does not appear to be outgrowing. When required to sit at a table (Foundation work, Reed's lab), he tucks one foot under the opposite thigh and leans his weight onto the non-dominant forearm, freeing the right hand to draw or fidget.

**Carriage in motion through a room.** Hugs walls rather than centerlines, especially in unfamiliar space; in the Baxter Building he moves down centers of corridors he knows. Threshold pause at every doorway — a half-beat scan of the room before entering, almost imperceptible, indistinguishable to most observers from natural hesitation. This is a *kidnapping-history* tell, present from the earliest Wein/Wolfman issues onward, persisting even in safe environments.

**Posture under being addressed by an adult.** Subtle chin-lift toward the adult, shoulders drawn slightly back, hands clasped low in front — a courteous, attentive set learned from Agatha Harkness, who valued comportment. Holds it for the duration of address, then dissolves immediately back into the loose, off-center slouch.

**Posture toward Reed specifically.** The most diagnostic postural pattern in the file. When Reed enters a room, subject's shoulders rise by approximately a centimeter and *stay* there for the duration of co-presence. The torso angles a few degrees away even when the face is turned toward Reed. He stands a foot further from Reed than he stands from Sue, Ben, or Johnny. This distance is consistent across writers and decades and is the somatic residue of FF #141 that subject does not consciously remember.

**Posture toward Sue.** Inward lean, head often resting against her upper arm or hip when seated alongside; one hand makes contact with her sleeve, often the cuff, fingertips on fabric. He has been observed (Slott run, multiple Waid issues) to *sleep* against her in moving vehicles within thirty seconds of sitting down, regardless of chronological age. The body switches off in her ambient field.

**Posture toward Valeria.** Mirrors hers. If she sits cross-legged, he sits cross-legged. If she leans on her left elbow, he leans on his right. This mirroring is unconscious and operates in both directions but is more pronounced from him to her — a sibling-attunement so deep it borders on co-regulation.

**Posture toward Ben Grimm.** *Fearless* proximity. Climbs, leans, sits on his lap or shoulder without consultation; physical contact initiated without checking. The only adult in subject's life with whom he behaves as if pre-verbal trust were never interrupted.

**Posture toward Johnny.** Loose, jostling, mock-shoving; the only relationship in which subject roughhouses. Johnny's posture cues invite it.

---

## 3. GAIT AND LOCOMOTION

A light, somewhat *up-on-the-toes* walk with short stride length and high cadence — the gait of a child who has spent a great deal of life on polished Baxter floors and is conditioned for quiet. Heel-strike is faint; he can cross a room without registering on a parent's auditory radar, and frequently does, appearing at Reed's shoulder mid-experiment without having been heard to enter. This is a documented and repeated panel-pattern.

**Running.** Loose-armed, slightly knock-kneed under speed, arms more across the chest than parallel — the run of a child who has not been athletically trained. Tires quickly when depowered. When powered, the gait does not become more efficient; it becomes *unnecessary* — he tends to skip locomotion altogether at the high end of his capacity.

**Stairs.** Two at a time going up if unobserved, single tread if observed by an adult. Going down: hand always on rail, regardless of whether the rail is needed.

**Doorways.** Right shoulder leads through every door; this is invariant. He turns the body to fit even where the door is wide enough not to require it — a small-body habit retained.

**Spatial habits.** Maintains a slightly greater interpersonal distance than children typically do — approximately one and a half arm-lengths from non-family adults. With Leech, with the Moloids, with the Future Foundation's outsider population, the distance collapses to nothing: he sits among them, on them, under them, with the body-permeability of a much younger child.

---

## 4. HANDS

Hands are the richest channel in the file.

**At rest.** Fingers loosely curled, thumb tucked inside the curl — a *retained infantile fist* pattern, age-inappropriate after toddlerhood, persistent. When startled, the fist clenches with thumb outside, then re-tucks within seconds.

**While thinking.** Right hand draws on whatever surface is available — air, thigh, table, the back of someone's hand — with the index fingertip, in small spirals counter-clockwise. Spirals tighten under stress, loosen under reverie. This is the dominant Franklin tell, present across writers who notice and writers who don't.

**While listening.** Hands flat on thighs or under the thighs (sitting on his hands), particularly when the adult speaking is Reed. The sitting-on-hands posture is itself a self-regulation device — it stills the spiraling finger and contains the body.

**While drawing.** Pencil held with overhand tripod, knuckles white at the index, leans the whole upper body over the page, nose six to eight inches from paper, breath shallow and high. Draws fast, in one continuous looped line, refuses to lift the pencil if avoidable. Compositions favor enclosure — boxes within boxes, houses within fields, planets within shells. He is, even at the doodle level, building containers.

**While building.** With Foundation materials, with Val's apparatus, with Leech's improvised constructions: his hands are *slower* than they are when drawing, almost reverent, as if each component has weight beyond its mass. He sets things down rather than placing them.

**Power-channeling hands.** Fingers spread wide, palms outward, but only after a half-second delay during which the hands seem to *forget* they are hands and remember they are aperture. The actual reality-warping does not require the gesture — it is residual childhood mimicry of the heroes around him, kept because it lets cognition catch up with effect.

**Contact behavior.** Touches Sue's wrist, Ben's forearm, Johnny's elbow, Val's shoulder. Does not touch Reed unless Reed touches first. Will hold hands well past the age at which most children stop holding hands with parents — chronological age is no predictor here.

---

## 5. FACE AND MICRO-EXPRESSION

**Resting face.** Slightly parted lips, brow soft, gaze long-focused — the face of a child whose default state is *attention to something not currently in the room.* This is the precognitive baseline; readers and onlookers consistently describe him as "dreamy."

**Smile.** Wide, asymmetric (slightly higher on the left), full-eye smile with strong cheek-raise (genuine Duchenne); reserved smiles (compliance, politeness) are visible at the mouth only, eyes flat — easy to distinguish. He does not fake-smile to family. He fake-smiles to Reed sometimes.

**The pre-power face.** Two to three seconds before reality bends, the face goes *neutral* — lips close, brow smooths, eyes lose focal point and seem to look at something inside the skull. This is the most reliable warning sign in the entire somatic file. Operatives observing subject for threat assessment should treat the *absence* of expression, not its presence, as the alarm.

**Crying pattern.** Silent, with chin-tremor leading; the lower lip pushes forward; tears spill before sob. He has been seen actively *swallowing* sobs in front of Reed and not in front of Sue — differential suppression by audience, learned early.

**Eye contact.** Sustained with Sue, Val, Ben, the Moloids, Leech. *Glancing* with Reed — three-second checks then away. Avoidant with Johnny when Johnny is teasing, direct when Johnny is serious. With strangers: long, unblinking, slightly unsettling stares before he has decided whether they are safe; once decided, normal child-glance pattern.

**Blink rate.** Lower than developmental norm at baseline, suggestive of mild absorptive-state continuity. Elevates sharply when lying, which he does poorly.

**Mouth tells.** Tongue pressed against upper molars when concentrating; lower-lip bite (light) when uncertain whether to speak; pursed lips when withholding a question for politeness. He purses lips when Reed corrects him.

---

## 6. VOICE AND BREATH

**Vocal baseline.** Soft, slightly breathy, pitched higher than his peers, with a rising terminal — sentences end up. The rising terminal persists into ages where most boys have lost it; it is a self-protective tic that frames assertions as questions, lowering the threshold for adult contradiction.

**Speech rate.** Slow when calm, faster when explaining a dream or vision (the precognitive material comes out in a rush, as if dictation against time), slowest when reading aloud or speaking to Reed.

**Lexicon.** Age-appropriate vocabulary punctuated by occasional cosmic-grade terminology dropped without ceremony ("the substrate," "the iteration," "before the rebuild") — these slip out and he does not flag them. Listeners notice and he notices their noticing and reels back to plainer language.

**Laugh.** A *huff* through the nose for small amusements; full belly-laugh only for Ben, Johnny, and Val. Sue's humor draws a quiet smile, not a laugh — different register.

**Breath at rest.** Diaphragmatic, slow, deeper than expected for his frame.
**Breath under stress.** Climbs to the upper chest, becomes audible at the throat, with brief breath-holds at the top of inhalation — the held-breath of a child waiting to find out if something bad is over.
**Breath in pre-power state.** *Stops.* For two to four seconds before reality-warping, subject does not breathe. This is the second alarm sign, behind facial neutralization.

---

## 7. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

The most heavily observed sleep record in the file, owing to its narrative consequence — his dreams are weapons.

**Sleep onset.** Fast when in close proximity to Sue or Ben (under five minutes), normal when alone (twenty to forty), prolonged when in unfamiliar environment (over an hour). Requires a light source — a hall light, a window, a luminous toy — has slept in full dark only during forced confinements and does not do well there.

**Position.** Side-sleeper, left side, knees drawn up to mid-chest, right arm under pillow, left hand near the face — a near-fetal arrangement retained well past developmental norm. Hugs a stuffed animal (HERBIE plush, a Moloid-made approximation, various rotating items) against the sternum. Will not sleep without something against the chest; if no toy is available, will substitute a folded shirt.

**REM behavior.** Eye movement visible through the lid is dense and prolonged; REM cycles longer than developmental norm. Vocalizations are common: name-fragments ("Mom," "Val," "Dad," "Ben"), occasional warnings in coherent sentences ("don't open it," "he's already inside," "it's smaller than they think"). Sue and Ben have both, on record, kept overnight watch and transcribed the warnings; Reed has not.

**Night terrors / prophetic dreams.** Sit-up awakenings without screaming, eyes open, body rigid, breath suspended for several seconds, then a long exhale and tears. He does not call out for help. He waits to be found. The body indexes a child who learned early that calling does not always summon, and that silence is the more reliable channel.

**Sleep totals.** Long when powered (ten to eleven hours), shorter when suppressed (eight to nine), with sleep-quality inverted — he sleeps *longer* when stable and *less well* when frightened, normal pattern.

**Sleepwalking.** Documented in the Hickman power-loss arc and again post-Onslaught residue. Walks toward Sue's room invariantly. Does not respond to redirection until physical contact with her is achieved; then settles immediately and can be returned to bed asleep.

---

## 8. EATING AND APPETITE

**Caloric pattern.** Light, grazing rather than meal-loading; prefers small portions and frequent returns to the kitchen. Sweet tooth pronounced — particularly for cereal, which he eats at all hours, dry by handful from the box as often as from a bowl.

**Food preferences.** Cereal (especially the sugared kind he is sometimes permitted), peanut butter sandwiches with crusts off (cuts the crusts himself with the side of a spoon), apples (whole, never sliced), cheese cubes, anything Ben hands him directly. Refuses: anything elaborate that Reed has cooked in a microwave-equivalent (Reed cooks poorly when he cooks at all), and seafood (a Negative-Zone-adjacent associative aversion, undocumented but stable).

**Eating posture.** Elbows in, shoulders rounded, head low over the plate, free hand flat on the table. Eats faster when Reed is at the table, slower when alone, slowest with Val (whose meals are conversation-heavy).

**Food as social channel.** Brings food to Leech, to the Moloids, to anyone he is worried about — caretaking through provisioning. Will not eat dessert if a sibling or friend has none.

**Hunger response.** Suppresses awareness of hunger until prompted; will go a full day without eating if absorbed in building or drawing. Sue intervenes routinely. The pattern is mild parentification-adjacent — needs are filed as low-priority.

---

## 9. GROOMING AND DRESS

**Self-care.** Brushes teeth (twice, prompted), washes face (irregularly), bathes (with reluctance and great length once in the tub — drawn baths become hour-long submarine sessions with toys narrating war and rescue). Does not brush hair; pushes it out of his face with the heel of the palm (see §1).

**Dress.** Layered, soft, weather-inappropriate when self-selected — pulls on whatever is at hand. Favors a long-sleeved shirt under a short-sleeved one even in warm rooms; the layering is mild armoring. Sleeve-cuffs are a sensory anchor — pulled down over the heels of the hands, gripped in the palm with thumbs extended (a sleeve-cuff thumb-hold, persistent across eras and writers).

**Footwear.** Sneakers, laces tied by Sue or Val in his youngest years, tied by him imperfectly after; left shoe consistently looser than right. Removes shoes immediately on entering the residence and forgets where he set them.

**Pocket contents.** Small drawings folded to thumbnail size; a stone or two from places that mattered; sometimes a Moloid-gift (a button, a screw, a tooth-like ceramic); a piece of string. Pockets are inventoried by Sue weekly during the laundry; she has, per implication of multiple panels, preserved most of it.

---

## 10. SEXUAL / INTIMATE BEHAVIORS

Subject is a minor across nearly the entire publication record; no sexual behavior is canonical and none is appropriately speculated. What the file *can* record at the intimate-but-non-sexual level:

**Physical affection toward family.** High frequency, low ceremony. Hugs initiated rather than received; kisses to Sue's cheek at goodnight; head against Ben's bicep when tired; hand-holding with Val that has continued past the age at which siblings typically stop.

**Touch-tolerance from non-family.** Low. Flinches imperceptibly at unexpected adult contact, settles within a second if the toucher is recognized as safe. Does not flinch from Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man, or other Foundation "monster" children — the prosocial-outsider valence overrides the threat-baseline.

**Privacy behaviors.** Modesty appropriate for age; bathroom door closed; changes clothes alone after a certain point (Hickman run, age-up issues). No exhibitionistic or attention-seeking somatic display has ever been canonically present.

---

## 11. SOMATIC SIGNATURES OF STATE-SHIFT

A consolidated reading of the body across regulatory state, for operational utility.

**Calm.** Loose-jawed, mouth slightly open, eyes long-focal, hands relaxed, breath diaphragmatic, posture asymmetric and slumped, fringe in eyes, finger drawing slow spirals. Speech soft with rising terminals. Easy proximity to chosen attachment figures.

**Pleasant absorption (drawing, building, with Val).** Nose close to work, breath shallow and high, tongue at upper molars, blink rate halved, oblivious to ambient — has to be called twice. The body is, in this state, *gone*.

**Mild stress (a missed parent, an unfamiliar room, a sharp word from Reed).** Shoulders rise a centimeter, finger spirals tighten, sleeve-cuffs pulled over hands, sentences shorten, terminal rise more pronounced, glances to Sue or Val for confirmation. Sits on hands.

**Moderate stress (a parent in danger reported but not present, a precognitive dream un-shared).** Withdraws spatially — finds a corner, a floor-against-couch position, a doorframe — and draws compulsively. Eats less. Sleep onset prolongs. Twists fringe.

**Acute fear for self.** Rare in the file. Body small, knees up, hands over the mouth not the eyes (he wants to *see*), breath held in shallow stutters.

**Acute fear for a loved one (the operationally critical state).** Face *neutralizes.* Breath *stops.* Eyes lose focal point and turn inward. Hands rise slowly, fingers spreading. There is no anger, no shouting, no warning — this is the Heroes Reborn signature, and it precedes reality-revision by seconds.

**Intimacy and rest with attachment figures.** Body collapses into them within seconds — head on shoulder, hand on cuff, weight transferred. He *off-loads* somatically to people he trusts. The body trusts before the mind does.

**Recognition by Reed (rare).** A whole-body alteration: shoulders drop a full centimeter, chin lifts, breath deepens, the smile reaches the eyes. Lasts as long as the recognition lasts. The body remembers what is missing by how it responds when it briefly arrives.

---

## 12. INFRASTRUCTURE NOTES

The body of Franklin Richards is, at every level of resolution, *organized around three to four people.* Sleep onset, eating, blink rate, posture, breath, finger-spirals, sleeve-cuffs, the timing of laughter — each tracks the proximity and well-being of Susan Storm-Richards, Valeria Richards, Ben Grimm, and (with more friction) Reed Richards. The somatic system is not autonomously regulated; it is *relationally* regulated, with the powers themselves serving as the buffer of last resort when relational regulation fails.

This is the load-bearing finding of the atlas. Subject's body is a tuning fork for his family. Strike the fork and the universe rings.


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7: ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

*Subject: Franklin Benjamin Richards. Cross-referenced against §1 (History) and §3 (Psychological). This section maps the architecture of how subject bonds, the precise mechanics of his distrust (such as it is), what his "betrayal" would look like in the rare cases he commits one, how he repairs ruptures, and the single relational template he repeats — with variations — across every figure in his life from age four to present canon.*

---

## 7.1 Attachment Style: A Compound Profile

Subject does not fit a single Ainsworth/Main category cleanly; he presents as a **compound attachment** with three superimposed strata, each laid down in a distinct developmental window and each still operative.

**Stratum I — Foundational secure-with-Sue (in utero through ~age 3).** Before the powers manifested, before Reed's neural suppression, Sue Richards' caregiving was textbook attuned: she held him through cosmic crises, she lactated him through a Negative Zone evacuation, she chose him over Reed when forced to. The base layer of subject's attachment apparatus is *secure*, and it is secure specifically toward maternal warmth. Every later attachment is structured on top of this layer — which is why subject's adult-relational capacities, despite everything that follows, remain unusually intact.

**Stratum II — Earned-avoidant with Reed (~age 3 through latency).** The FF #141 neural-suppression event laid down a layer of *somatic mistrust* toward paternal authority that exists below the verbal register. Subject does not consciously remember being switched off. His body remembers. The behavioral expression is consistent across forty years of canon: subject *approaches Reed for cognition and withdraws from Reed for comfort.* He will bring Reed a question, a drawing, a problem; he will not bring Reed his fear. When frightened, he routes to Sue, to Ben Grimm, to Johnny, to Agatha, to Valeria — almost never to Reed first. This is not estrangement; it is a precisely calibrated allocation that protects the relationship from the wound it cannot name.

**Stratum III — Distributed-secure across chosen family (~age 4 onward).** Because his biological parents were chronically absent into space/microverses/dimensional crises, subject developed what attachment theory does not have clean language for: a *redundant attachment network* in which multiple figures hold partial parental load. Agatha Harkness held supernatural-mentor load. Ben Grimm held safe-uncle-and-bodyguard load. Johnny held fun-older-brother load. Alicia Masters periodically held aesthetic-maternal load. Wyatt Wingfoot, the Inhumans during certain arcs, even Lockjaw at one point, held intermittent caretaking. The result is a child whose attachment system is *load-balanced* rather than dyadic — closer in shape to a kibbutz-raised child or a sprawling extended-family child than to a nuclear-family child. This is protective. It is also the reason §4's resilience holds: no single tether failure collapses the structure.

The compound profile resolves, behaviorally, as: **secure baseline, avoidant toward one specific parent, polyvalently bonded outward, with a small core of non-negotiable tethers.**

---

## 7.2 How He Bonds

Subject's bonding mechanics are slow, observational, and asymmetrically generous. The pattern, repeated with Leech, with Dragon Man, with the Moloids, with Artie and Leech, with the Future Foundation's "monster" children, with Valeria from her infancy, with the various surrogates, follows a recognizable sequence:

**Phase 1 — Quiet observation.** He watches before he speaks. New people are studied for several pages of panel-time before he makes overt contact. He does not ask questions; he registers texture — how someone moves, whether they are gentle with smaller beings, whether their kindness is performative or steady. This is not shyness; it is *triage*. He is a child who has been attacked, harvested, possessed, and kidnapped, and he has learned without instruction to read interpersonal microclimate before committing.

**Phase 2 — Offering an artifact.** First contact, when he initiates it, is *creative*: a drawing, an invented game, a shared imaginary scenario, an introduction to a pocket-world he has built. He extends his own creativity as the bonding token. This is diagnostic. He is offering the most personal thing he has — his generative interior — and watching what the other person does with it. People who receive his offerings with attention pass the test. People who dismiss them are quietly demoted in his interior hierarchy and almost never recover.

**Phase 3 — Inclusion in the small group.** Once a person is admitted, subject incorporates them into the network of beings he protects. Leech, after admission, is *Franklin's*. Dragon Man, after admission, is family. This step is binary: there is no middle distance. Subject does not maintain "acquaintances" as a category; people are either in the protected circle or they are background. The circle is small but absolute.

**Phase 4 — Reciprocal play and gift-economy.** Inside the circle, subject's bonding currency is *play and small gifts*: the drawing he made for Val, the imaginary expedition he planned for the Moloids, the invented language he and Leech share. He does not do verbal-affective declarations of love; he does *small handmade evidence of having been thinking about you when you weren't there.* This is, clinically, a very high-quality bonding behavior — the kind that secure adults exhibit and that anxious adults often cannot sustain.

**Phase 5 — Embodied protectiveness.** The terminal state of a bond, with Franklin, is that he will not let the bonded figure be hurt. The Heroes Reborn pocket universe is the maximum-amplitude expression of this phase. Quieter expressions: standing between Val and a threat, refusing to let the Moloids be sent away, defending Dragon Man's personhood to skeptical adults. The protectiveness is the bond's mature form.

The full arc — observe, offer, include, play, protect — takes anywhere from minutes (with another child) to years (with a wary adult). Once completed, it does not reverse.

---

## 7.3 How He Distrusts

Subject's distrust mechanism is unusually quiet for someone of his exposure history. He does not perform suspicion. He withdraws, observes, and *files*.

The behavioral signatures of Franklin-distrust are subtle and consistent:

- **Reduced eye contact and increased drawing-during-conversation.** When subject does not trust the figure he is speaking with, his hands occupy themselves; he is constructing a small parallel activity that gives him an exit.
- **Routing to a trusted adjacent figure.** If he distrusts an adult, he will physically place himself near Ben, Sue, or Val while continuing to be polite. He does not announce the distrust; he triangulates against it.
- **Withholding the artifact.** He will not offer drawings, pocket-worlds, or invented games to figures he distrusts. The absence of the gift is the diagnostic.
- **Increased politeness, decreased information.** His manners become more, not less, formal under distrust. He answers questions accurately and tells the truth, but he does not volunteer.
- **Power-quiescence.** Subject's powers, when active, *do not deploy* around distrusted figures — the opposite of what an anxious or hostile child would show. He goes still. He waits. The energy banks rather than discharges.

Subject distrusts on three triggers, observed consistently:

1. **Cruelty to small or vulnerable beings.** Single highest-confidence disqualifier. Any figure who treats Leech, the Moloids, or any "monstrous" creature as less-than is permanently demoted and will not be readmitted absent extraordinary repair.
2. **Dismissal of his perceptions.** Particularly his precognitive dreams. Adults who told him he was "just dreaming" and were then proven wrong by catastrophe occupy a specific lower tier in his interior model. He does not bear grudges in the affective sense, but he does not re-extend the perceptive offering.
3. **Manipulation of his powers or his identity.** Anyone who tries to use him as instrument — Onslaught, Mephisto, the various telepaths who have tried to harvest him — generates a permanent flinch-pattern. Even when the manipulator is later allied (e.g., complicated cases like the X-Men post-Krakoa, who collectively put him into an identity-crisis through Xavier's pronouncement), the flinch persists.

Critically, subject does *not* distrust based on appearance, species, power-status, or social position. His distrust criteria are entirely behavioral. This is why he can love Dragon Man and the Moloids and be wary of well-meaning telepaths.

---

## 7.4 Betrayal — Inflicted Upon Him

Subject has been betrayed, in canon, by three categories of figure, and his response pattern to each is consistent and characteristic.

**Betrayal by Reed (FF #141, neural suppression).** The foundational betrayal of his life. Sue named it as such — she left. Subject did not consciously process it because he was unconscious during and immediately after. The integration occurred somatically and is still ongoing across the publication record. His response: *withdrawal of one functional channel of intimacy (the comfort channel) while preserving all other channels.* He did not stop loving Reed. He did not even stop respecting Reed. He stopped *going to Reed when scared.* The precision of the response — a single channel surgically excised while the rest of the relationship was preserved intact — is more sophisticated than most adults manage.

**Betrayal by Xavier / the Krakoan establishment ("you are not a mutant").** A categorical betrayal: a figure with apparent authority to define his belonging used that authority to exclude him from a category he had assumed included him. Subject's response: *destabilization of self-concept manifesting as withdrawal, rumination, mild somatization, and increased physical proximity to Val and Sue.* He did not lash out, did not protest, did not litigate. He internalized and re-questioned. This is the §3 pattern: identity-category challenges produce introversion, not aggression.

**Betrayal by cosmic-entity harvest (Onslaught, Mephisto, Hiro-Kala, others).** Treatment as instrument rather than person. Subject's response: *no conscious change in behavior toward the world; a quiet additional layer of defensive somatic vigilance.* He does not develop a hostile cosmology after these events. He develops what reads as a deepened gentleness — *because he has been used as an instrument, he is unusually careful never to use anyone else as one.* The ethics he derives from being harvested is the ethics of refusing to harvest.

The pattern across all three: **subject does not retaliate, does not perform grievance, does not break off the relationship, and does not forget.** The information is metabolized into the relational substrate and shapes future behavior at the level of allocation, not affect.

---

## 7.5 Betrayal — Committed By Him

This is the rarest category in subject's file, and the most diagnostic.

Subject is canonically incapable of certain betrayals. He will not lie to those he loves about anything that matters. He will not abandon. He will not weaponize what he knows about someone against them. He will not break a stated promise.

He is, however, capable of two specific micro-betrayals that recur across canon and require honest naming:

**Concealment-by-protection.** Subject will hide things from people he loves *for what he perceives as their benefit.* He concealed precognitive dreams from Sue in several arcs to avoid frightening her. He has hidden the extent of his powers from Reed in the post-Hickman era to avoid being instrumentalized. He concealed his crisis of identity from Val for a stretch of the *X-Men/FF* crossover so as not to burden her. This is not malicious. It is the parentified-child pattern (§3): he assumes responsibility for others' affective load and edits his disclosures accordingly. The functional effect on relationships, however, is *informational asymmetry* — and the people he loves have, on occasion, registered it as a betrayal.

**Salvific overreach.** The Heroes Reborn act is the template. Subject, under acute terror for loved ones, takes massive unilateral action without their consent. The Avengers and FF did not consent to being moved into a pocket universe; he did it because he had to and could. This is the failure mode of his protectiveness — *when love-under-threat ignites his powers before his ego, he commits decisions on behalf of others that they would have been entitled to make themselves.* He has not done this in malice. He has done it in panic. The distinction matters morally and matters not at all to the people whose realities he edited.

These are the two ways Franklin Richards can betray you: he can withhold to spare you, and he can save you without asking.

---

## 7.6 Repair

Subject's repair behavior is unusually mature and consistent across the record.

**Recognition.** He notices ruptures quickly — often before the other party has named them. His observational baseline (§7.2 Phase 1) reads micro-shifts in others' affect with high sensitivity.

**Approach.** He approaches the ruptured party physically, quietly, and without preamble. He sits near them. He does not open with explanation or apology in words; he opens with *presence* and frequently with an artifact — a drawing, a built thing, a small gesture that signals *I have been thinking about you and about this.*

**Naming.** When he speaks to the rupture, he names it accurately and without defensiveness. He does not minimize. He does not over-apologize. He says what he did, why he did it, and what he understands the cost was. This is, again, more skilled than most adults manage, and is attributable to Sue's modeling and to the chosen-family network's general high emotional literacy.

**Repair gesture.** He offers something specific — a change in behavior, a promise, a reversal of the action where possible. With Reed, repair gestures historically take the form of intellectual engagement; with Sue, of physical closeness; with Val, of resuming play; with Ben and Johnny, of returning to the easy rhythms of the relationship.

**Integration.** Post-repair, subject does not re-litigate. The matter is filed, the relationship resumes, and the learning is incorporated into his future allocations. He does not bring it back up. He does not punish.

The one structural limitation in his repair capacity: **he cannot repair what is not named to him.** Because his most significant wound (Reed/FF #141) was never explicitly processed in canon between father and son, the rupture there has never been fully repaired — only managed. The Hickman-era reconciliation arcs come closest, particularly the moment Reed acknowledges Franklin as a creator and partner. But the foundational breach remains, in subject's interior, *unspoken between them.* This is the single largest piece of unfinished relational business in his life.

---

## 7.7 Intimacy and Dependency

Subject is, by both age and disposition, a child across most of the publication record, and his intimacy patterns must be read in that frame. He is not romantic-canon. What is observable is his capacity for *non-romantic intimacy*, which is unusually high-bandwidth.

**With Sue.** The intimacy is bodily and unguarded. He climbs into her lap well past the age most boys would; he is openly tearful in her presence; he tells her things he tells no one else. This is the intimacy of the foundational secure bond intact. Dependency here is *appropriate and admitted* — he leans on her and knows he leans on her.

**With Valeria.** The intimacy is the rarer sibling-secure variety — collaborative, mutually protective, asymmetrically affectionate (he is more openly demonstrative; she is more pragmatically demonstrative; they translate fluently). Dependency is *mutual and balanced*: each knows the other is load-bearing. Subject is at his most regulated in Val's vicinity, and the inverse is also true.

**With Ben.** The intimacy is physical and uncomplicated — the easy intimacy of a child with a beloved uncle who is also, functionally, a wall. Ben's body is, in subject's interior model, *safety made literal.* The dependency is one-directional and unembarrassed; subject expects Ben to be there and Ben always is. This is, in §4's clinical read, a near-ideal secondary attachment figure, and its stability has done more for subject's resilience than is generally credited.

**With Johnny.** Intimacy through play and through being seen as *fun*. Johnny is the figure who treats Franklin most consistently as a kid rather than a phenomenon, which is exactly the registration subject has chosen for himself. Dependency is low but enjoyment is high — a relationship of *delight* rather than need, which subject requires at least one of in order to be a healthy child.

**With Reed.** The intimacy is partial, intellectualized, and carefully maintained on subject's side. Dependency is admitted only in the cognitive register — he depends on Reed to *think with him* and refuses to depend on Reed to *hold him.*

**With Leech and the Moloids and the Future Foundation children.** Intimacy in the inverted register: subject is the holder rather than the held. He is unselfconsciously affectionate with these figures, openly tender, openly protective. Dependency is theirs upon him, and he carries it without resentment. This is the parentified-child pattern in its prosocial expression — he meets needs in others that he is careful not to claim in himself.

**With Agatha Harkness (historically).** Mentor-intimacy: respectful, learning-oriented, mildly fearful in the early years and ripening to something close to grandmotherly closeness by the later arcs. Dependency was high in latency, has tapered with age.

The cross-cutting pattern: **subject is capable of dependency only on a small, designated set of figures, and only in the specific register he has allocated to each.** He does not generalize his needs across his network. He does not "lean on the team." He leans on Sue for affect, Val for collaboration, Ben for safety, Reed for cognition, Johnny for play. The allocation is precise and stable across decades.

---

## 7.8 The Relational Template, Repeated

There is one shape Franklin Richards makes with every meaningful relationship in his life, and once it is named, it is visible everywhere in his file.

**The template: *I will be small near you so you can be yourself; in exchange, I ask that you let me see you and that you not pretend I am other than I am.***

The first half of the contract is his offering — *self-limitation in service of the other's full expression.* He gives Sue the room to be a mother by being a son who needs mothering. He gives Reed the room to be a thinker by being a child who brings questions. He gives Ben the room to be a protector by being protectable. He gives Val the room to be the family genius by being the family dreamer rather than the family god. He gives Leech and the Moloids the room to be loved by being the one who loves them. He gives the universe the room to keep its current shape by *not remaking it* despite being able to.

The second half is what he asks in return — *to be seen accurately, and not redefined.* The Xavier rupture lands where it does because Xavier violated the second half: he told Franklin what Franklin was, against Franklin's own self-account. The Reed wound persists because Reed, in the FF #141 moment, treated him as phenomenon rather than son. The cosmic-entity betrayals all violate the same clause: they treat him as instrument rather than person.

This template — *small-for-you, in exchange for seen-as-I-am* — is the deep structure of every Franklin Richards relationship. It is mature, it is generous, it is asymmetrically weighted toward the other, and it is fragile in exactly one way: **it depends on the other party honoring the second clause.** When they do, the relationship is durable and load-bearing for both. When they don't, subject withdraws — quietly, without performance — the channel of intimacy that depended on that recognition, while preserving the rest of the relationship intact.

It is the relational signature of a child who knows he could remake the world and has chosen instead to be known by it. The risk implicit in the template, named in §4 and worth repeating here as the operational summary: *the tethers are few, and the structure is held by their honoring of his terms. Treat the tethers as critical infrastructure. Treat the terms as non-negotiable.*


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7

## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

*Subject: Franklin Benjamin Richards*
*Scope: Total defensive architecture across ~57 years of recorded existence. Ranked from most mature to most primitive, with behavioral signatures, somatic tells, environmental triggers, observed failure modes, and longitudinal drift.*

---

### Preliminary Note on the Architecture as a Whole

The most striking fact about subject's defensive system is its **inversion of the expected developmental curve**. A child with his exposure profile — induced coma at toddler age, repeated kidnapping, cosmic possession, the conscious knowledge that he has been a god — should present a defensive system anchored at the primitive pole: splitting, projective identification, somatic conversion, dissociative fugue. Subject's actual architecture is anchored at the **mature pole** (sublimation, altruism, anticipation, humor, self-volitional self-limitation), with primitive mechanisms held in reserve and deployed only under extremity.

This inversion has a single mechanical explanation: **the powers function as a defensive prosthesis**. Affect that would, in a normal child, require dissociation or somatization can in subject's case be *externalized as constructed reality*. He does not need to bury the feeling because he can build it a house. This is the load-bearing fact of his entire psychic economy, and every defense below must be read in relation to it.

When the prosthesis is removed (Hickman power-loss arc; Slott-era ambiguity around mutant status; intermittent "powers fading" beats), the more primitive defenses become observable for the first time — not because they were absent, but because they were rendered unnecessary by an architectural shortcut no other person in the published record possesses.

---

### Tier I — Mature Defenses (Vaillant Level IV)

These are the defenses subject deploys *first* and *most reliably*. They constitute his behavioral baseline.

#### 1. Sublimation — *The Signature Defense*

Cosmic affect → narrative or constructed form. This is the defining mechanism of subject's entire psychic life and the single most distinctive feature of his clinical profile.

**Behavioral expressions, longitudinal:**
- *Childhood (FF #200s, Byrne era):* Crayon drawings of monsters Reed dismisses as imagination, which prove to be Annihilus, Galactus-precursors, Onslaught precognita. The drawings are not pathology; they are affect-as-image, the rawest form of the sublimating function.
- *Latency (Simonson, DeFalco eras):* Storytelling to younger children, narrated games during Agatha Harkness fostering periods, the "Tattletale" persona he assumes in *Power Pack* crossovers — playing hero as a way of metabolizing his lack of agency in the actual hero-family.
- *Pre-adolescence (Hickman *FF* / Future Foundation):* Architectural play within the Foundation, the design and curation of "monster" enrollment, his contributions to Foundation field projects. He builds a *school for outsiders* — a sublimated version of his own ambiguous belonging.
- *Adolescent peak (Hickman *Secret Wars*):* Co-architecture of Battleworld and the post-collapse Multiverse. *He sublimates the literal end of reality into the literal blueprint of the next one.* This is the upper bound of the mechanism; no other recorded subject has expressed sublimation at this scale.
- *Post-power eras (Slott, North):* Reverts cleanly to drawing, narrating, and building in non-cosmic media. He does not lose the function when he loses the wattage. This is diagnostically important — it confirms sublimation is *characterological*, not power-dependent.

**Somatic correlates:** When sublimating, subject's posture softens, breathing slows, eye contact decreases (focus turns inward or to the medium), and a half-smile is frequently visible. The state is markedly self-soothing. He will hum, occasionally, low and tuneless.

**Failure mode:** When sublimation is *blocked* — when he is restrained from making, drawing, or building — affect that would normally route to the medium pools internally. Observable in panels during the Onslaught lead-in: subject is shown listless, clinging to Sue, unable to draw. This is the precursor state to involuntary reality-warping. *Watch the hands. If the hands are not making something, the universe may soon be.*

---

#### 2. Altruism — *Genuine and Reflexive*

Subject's prosocial protectiveness toward outsiders is consistent across writers, decades, and tonal registers, which is the standard test for trait versus performance. It does not vary with audience, reward, or supervision.

**Stable referents:**
- *Leech.* Subject's closest non-sibling bond. Subject behaves toward Leech with a tenderness that has no instrumental component — Leech can offer subject nothing (the irony of the depowered child befriending the power-nullifier is *load-bearing* and almost certainly perceived by subject at some level).
- *The Moloids (Tong, Korr, Mik, Turg).* Subject treats them as full peers, learns their dialectal speech, defends them against Foundation outsiders.
- *Dragon Man.* Treated as uncle/guardian rather than instrument; subject corrects adults who refer to Dragon Man as "it."
- *Bentley-23 (the Wizard's clone).* Subject extends trust to a child literally bred to be a villain — a small but characteristic act.
- *Artie Maddicks, occasional X-character crossovers.* Same pattern.

**The mechanism is etiologically clear:** subject's own ambiguous belonging (mutant/not-mutant, child/god, human/cosmic) generates an *identificatory empathy* with categorical outsiders. He is metabolizing his own dislocation by being the welcomer he himself needs.

**Failure mode:** Altruism can tip into *parentification* (see §11 below) when subject takes on caretaker functions disproportionate to his developmental position. Observable in Future Foundation arcs where he assumes responsibility for Foundation children's emotional regulation while Reed and Sue are off-world.

---

#### 3. Anticipation

Subject's precognitive dreams are technically a power, but their *use* is a defense. He converts the unbearable affect of "something terrible is about to happen to people I love" into the bearable cognitive form of "I have warned the adults." Even when ignored (Byrne run, repeatedly), the anticipatory act discharges the affect.

**Behavioral signature:** Quiet morning approach to Sue or Reed; a small, specific statement ("the bad shape came back, the one with the wings"); often a drawing left on the kitchen surface; then withdrawal. He does not press. He has offered the warning and considers his role discharged.

**Note:** This is *also* a covert form of bidding for Reed's recognition (see §11, attachment-driven mechanisms). The warning is real; the secondary aim — *see me, believe me* — is also real.

---

#### 4. Humor — Mild, Self-Effacing, Underdeveloped

The weakest of his mature defenses. Subject's humor is gentle, often pun-based, occasionally self-deprecating; rarely sharp, never cruel. He laughs more than he jokes. The underdevelopment is itself meaningful — humor at the adult level requires a self-positioning that subject's chosen smallness inhibits. He defers comic register to Johnny and Ben.

---

#### 5. Suppression (vs. Repression — distinguish)

*Conscious* deferral of unwelcome thoughts and needs. Subject does this constantly with respect to his own desires when he perceives them as disproportionate to his family's bandwidth. Observable as the recurrent panel-language of Franklin opening his mouth to say something, closing it, and choosing instead to ask about someone else.

This is mature; it is also corrosive over time. Files accumulate (see §11).

---

#### 6. Volitional Self-Limitation (*kenosis*) — Idiosyncratic Mature Defense

Not in standard taxonomies. Subject's *election to be a child* despite the knowledge that he has been a creator-deity is a defensive operation without clean precedent.
