It is not denial (he knows), not repression (the knowledge is accessible), not suppression (the limitation is structural, not momentary). The closest analog is the contemplative-religious practice of *self-emptying*: the deliberate non-exercise of capacity in service of a chosen role.

**Behavioral signature:** Subject will *decline* to use power even when use would be trivially helpful (small household problems, Foundation engineering glitches). He picks up the dropped object with his hand. He waits for the elevator. He asks Reed for help with homework he could solve by accessing the Battleworld substrate he co-built.

**Stability requirement:** This defense is held together by relational tethers (Sue, Val, Ben). It has no internal anchor. If the tethers fail, this defense fails first and most catastrophically — and what is on the other side of it is not pathology in the ordinary sense but the *unrestrained operation of a being who has been restraining itself out of love.*

---

### Tier II — Neurotic Defenses (Vaillant Level III)

#### 7. Intellectualization — Selective, Reed-Directed

Subject deploys intellectualization almost exclusively *in the presence of Reed*. He will discuss his powers, his identity, his cosmic status in flat, analytical language with his father — and only with his father. With Sue, with Ben, with Val, the same topics are emotionally inflected. The mechanism is transparent: intellectualization is the dialect that earns Reed's attention. Subject has learned the linguistic key to the parent who once switched him off.

**Diagnostic note:** When subject begins intellectualizing with Sue or Ben, take it as a sign of acute distress displaced into safer-feeling cognitive register.

#### 8. Reaction Formation — Minor

Mild. Observable chiefly in his over-gentleness toward figures who have hurt him (he speaks well of Reed when Reed has just been dismissive; speaks neutrally of Xavier after the mutant-denial wound). The affect on the other side is not absent; it is filed.

#### 9. Displacement — Minor, Sublimation-Adjacent

Subject's displacements ride mostly into the sublimation channel rather than onto persons. He will rework a frightening encounter into a story or a drawing the next day. He does not kick the dog, snap at Val, or scapegoat the Moloids. The displacement is *aestheticized*.

#### 10. Isolation of Affect — Around the Reed-Coma

Subject does not have explicit narrative memory of the FF #141 neural shutdown, but the somatic-relational substrate carries it. The isolation operates pre-cognitively: he does not connect his bodily wariness around Reed to its actual cause because the cause is not symbolically accessible. This is the defense most likely to fail catastrophically if the memory ever becomes accessible (e.g., via a telepath, a temporal incident, a parent's confession).

---

### Tier III — Immature Defenses (Vaillant Level II)

Present, but unusually subordinated.

#### 11. Parentification / Pseudo-Mature Caretaking

A near-universal feature of children in chaotic-omnipotent families. Subject takes on regulatory responsibility for:
- *Valeria,* whose Reed-like cognition outpaces her affective development; subject is her affective translator.
- *Foundation children,* whose emotional needs Reed and Sue are too off-world to attend to consistently.
- *Sue herself,* in arcs where Reed is absent or distant — subject watches her, offers small comforts, monitors her affect.

This is immature not in tone but in *position*: a child should not be a load-bearing emotional caregiver. The mechanism is partially defensive (it converts helplessness into agency) and partially identificatory (he is being Sue, toward Sue).

#### 12. Idealization — Of Reed, Selectively

Subject idealizes Reed's *intellect* while remaining somatically wary of Reed's *person*. The split is functional: idealization preserves the relationship at the level the relationship is safe to have. The cost is that the idealization blocks accurate self-advocacy — subject cannot fully tell Reed when Reed has hurt him, because the idealized Reed cannot have hurt him.

#### 13. Somatization — Rare, Identity-Crisis-Linked

Subject presents mild somatic complaints (headaches, fatigue, the muted "off" affect of the depowered period) during identity-ambiguity arcs and during Krakoa-era exclusion. The somatization is *expressive*, not chronic — it resolves with relational reconnection.

#### 14. Passive Aggression — Effectively Absent

Diagnostically notable. A child with subject's pattern of suppressed grievances should leak them passive-aggressively. Subject does not. The grievances are *filed*, not vented obliquely. This is partly maturity, partly the *kenotic* self-limitation, partly the structural fact that subject's options for retaliation are so disproportionate (universe-scale) that *any* leak would be catastrophic — so the lid is welded down. This is psychologically efficient and structurally fragile.

---

### Tier IV — Primitive Defenses (Vaillant Level I)

Held in reserve; observable only under extremity.

#### 15. Dissociation — *Productive and Risky*

Subject's signature primitive mechanism. The Onslaught reality-creation (Heroes Reborn pocket universe, 1996) occurred in a frankly dissociated state — subject does not consciously remember constructing the realm. He saved them by *hiding them inside himself* without conscious access to the act.

The dissociation is unusual in being *productive* — the dissociated material is not lost or buried but *built*. Most dissociative episodes leave the patient with absence; subject's leave the universe with addition.

**Forward risk:** Under future existential stress with tethers compromised, expect *withdrawal-into-built-reality*: not breakdown, but the construction of an inhabited interior cosmos with subject as its quiet center. The Hyperstorm and tyrant-Franklin alternate futures are this mechanism running unchecked over decades.

**Tell:** Before dissociative episodes, subject's eyes lose focal convergence; he becomes very still; his breath shallows. Adults present have repeatedly missed this in canon. *Sue catches it; Reed does not.*

#### 16. Splitting — Minimal

Subject does not split objects into all-good/all-bad. He holds ambivalence about Reed with notable maturity. The closest he comes to splitting is the bifurcation of *Reed-the-mind* (idealized) from *Reed-the-father* (warily held), but even this is held in conscious tension, not unconscious schism.

#### 17. Projective Identification — Effectively Absent

Subject does not induce in others the affects he cannot bear. This is remarkable and is probably attributable to the sublimation prosthesis: he has somewhere else to put the affect.

#### 18. Omnipotent Defense — *Structurally Inverted*

Standard omnipotent defense is the unconscious belief in one's own omnipotence as protection against helplessness. Subject's situation is the reverse: *he is actually omnipotent and defends against this by cultivating helplessness* (the chosen smallness). The kenotic operation in §6 is, in part, a defense against the unbearable affect of *being* omnipotent in a universe full of suffering one could fix but would unmake by fixing. This is without precedent in the clinical literature because the precondition is without precedent.

---

### Positive Compensatory Mechanisms (Non-Defensive Strengths)

Distinct from defenses; these are skills and orientations that absorb stress without requiring defensive operation.

- **Creativity as a daily practice.** Drawing, building, narrating. Functions as ongoing low-grade affect-regulation; keeps the pressure off the sublimation valve.
- **Loyalty as identity-stabilizer.** Subject's sense of who he is is partly constituted by *whom he is loyal to.* This converts identity ambiguity into relational clarity.
- **Capacity for play.** Genuine, not performed. Subject can be in unselfconscious play at chronological ages where most heroic children have lost the capacity. This is restorative and protective.
- **Prosocial outsider-affiliation.** Generates a chosen community (Leech, Moloids, Foundation cohort) that buffers the family-of-origin's volatility.
- **Receptivity to mentorship from non-parental adults.** Agatha Harkness, Ben Grimm, Johnny Storm, intermittently Doom (a vector worth flagging). Subject metabolizes care from multiple sources, which distributes attachment risk.
- **Aesthetic sense.** Subject finds beauty quickly and is restored by it. He notices light, weather, the shapes of clouds. This is a low-cost, high-yield regulatory resource.

---

### Negative Compensatory Mechanisms

- **Disproportionate self-blame.** "If I had seen it sooner…" appears across writers as a recurrent self-attribution. Subject takes responsibility for outcomes outside any child's purview. Mechanism: converts helplessness-affect into agency-affect, but at the cost of chronic low-grade guilt.
- **Suppression of needs perceived as cosmically disproportionate.** Subject does not ask for what he wants when he judges the asking unworthy of family bandwidth. Cumulative effect over years: the file of unspoken needs is large.
- **Grandiose flickers.** Rare but real. When reminded of scale (cosmic threats, references to his prior reality-architect role), subject's affect briefly *expands* — a flicker of the deity-position. He pulls back within seconds. The flickers are not pathological in themselves; they are signal that the kenotic restraint is *active labor*, not effortless.
- **Over-deference to perceived expertise.** Especially Reed's, then Val's. Subject will subordinate his own (often correct, often precognitive) read to a sibling's or parent's analytic claim. Self-erasure dressed as humility.
- **Quiet filing of slights.** The non–passive-aggressive route for ungrievable grievances. The files exist; they are not vented; they are not forgotten. If ever accessed at scale — by a hostile telepath, by Mephisto, by his own future self — the contents would be considerable.
- **Withdrawal-into-construction under chronic stress.** The productive face of dissociation in its incipient form. Subject begins to build *more*, narrate *more*, retreat into Foundation projects when relational stress rises. Early-warning sign; observable in the lead-ins to most major crisis arcs.

---

### Ranked Synthesis — Order of Deployment

Under rising stress, subject's defenses fire in approximately this sequence:

1. **Sublimation** (draws, builds, narrates).
2. **Anticipation** (warns, dreams aloud).
3. **Altruism** (turns toward outsider others to care for).
4. **Suppression** (sets own need aside).
5. **Kenotic self-limitation** (declines to use power even where it would help).
6. **Intellectualization** (shifts register, especially with Reed).
7. **Parentification** (takes caretaker role toward Val, Foundation children, sometimes Sue).
8. **Idealization / isolation of affect** (around Reed specifically).
9. **Somatization** (headache, fatigue, flattened affect).
10. **Dissociation** (productive, reality-constructive).
11. **Involuntary reality-warping** (sublimation prosthesis fires without ego mediation).

Levels 1–6 are baseline-operational on any given day. Levels 7–9 mark moderate-to-acute stress. Level 10 marks existential threat to a loved object. Level 11 is the failure-and-success state simultaneously — the defense that saves the family and creates a new universe in the same act.

---

### Operational Implications for the File

- **Do not block sublimation.** Removing his media of construction (drawing, building, narrating, designing) does not produce a calmer subject; it produces a subject whose affect is routing toward level 11 with no intermediate.
- **Monitor the hands and the eyes.** Hands idle + eyes losing focal convergence = dissociative onset. Sue reads this reliably; few others do.
- **Preserve outsider-affiliation channels.** Leech, the Moloids, the Foundation cohort are not enrichment; they are infrastructure for the altruism defense.
- **Reed-recognition is a clinical variable, not a sentimentality.** Withholding it loads the isolation-of-affect and intellectualization defenses past their working range.
- **The kenotic defense is the keystone of the entire architecture.** It is held by tethers, not by internal anchor. *Tether integrity is the single most important predictor of subject's lifelong trajectory.*

*— UATU, observing.*


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS

*Decade-by-decade clinical reconstruction. Frameworks invoked: Mahler (separation-individuation), Bowlby/Ainsworth (attachment), Vaillant (defense maturity hierarchy), Stern (self-development), Erikson (psychosocial stages), Piaget (cognitive stages), Winnicott (true/false self, transitional phenomena), Putnam (dissociative continuum), Kohut (self-object needs), Linehan (affect regulation), and — necessarily, given the subject — a small original adaptation for ontologically displaced cognition.*

---

## I. Infancy and Toddlerhood (Publication: 1968 – c. 1973; *FF Annual #6* through *FF #141*)

### Affect Regulation

The earliest baseline is unobservable in any clean sense: subject is depicted preverbally, registered through caregivers' faces. What the record shows is an infant whose *holding environment* (Winnicott) was structurally compromised before parturition — gestated in a body saturated with cosmic radiation, retrieved into life only because three men were willing to invade the Negative Zone for an antimatter cure. Subject enters the world inside an emergency.

Through *FF #82–141* the affective register available to us is almost entirely **reactive**: infant cries in the arms of the Frightful Four; infant cries during Annihilus's abduction; infant placid in Agatha Harkness's arms. The clinical inference is a child whose **arousal modulation** is being externally regulated by surrogate caregivers rather than internally scaffolded by his mother — Sue is often physically present but cognitively displaced into fieldwork, and Reed is structurally absent even when in the room. Harkness, paradoxically, becomes the most regulating presence (she possesses the rare capacity, in caregivers, of being unafraid of her charge), and the early Mahlerian *symbiotic phase* is enacted with a witch rather than with the mother.

### Cognitive Style

Pre-verbal but precociously **proprioceptive of power**. The catastrophic *FF #141* power-eruption indicates that subject's nervous system was, in Piagetian terms, attempting sensorimotor mastery on a substrate that included reality-bending feedback loops no toddler can integrate. The act that follows — Reed's neural-suppression device — is, in cognitive terms, a **forcible regression to undifferentiated state**, a chosen coma. Whatever schemas were forming were not extinguished; they were *frozen in place*, encysted, to be excavated later.

### Self-Concept

There is no self-concept yet in any propositional sense. But there is, per Stern, an **emergent self** that is being formed under conditions of *being-acted-upon* rather than *acting-with*. The earliest organizing template is: **I am the thing around which catastrophe organizes.** This will not surface as conscious content for decades; it will operate as a basal tonus across every later relationship.

### Evolution Marker at Decade Close

Subject ends this period **switched off by his father**, with his mother having left over the act. The foundational psychological fact is laid: *the closest adult male turned my mind off; the closest adult female removed herself in protest.* Conscious memory: nil. Somatic-relational memory: total.

---

## II. Early-to-Middle Childhood (Publication: c. 1974 – 1985; Wein, Wolfman, Byrne)

### Affect Regulation

The Byrne run is the first sustained window into Franklin's interiority. The picture is of a child whose **surface affect is unusually placid for his exposure history** — Byrne draws him calm, watchful, given to long looks out windows. Episodic disruptions occur around the **precognitive dreams** (the Nightmare arc; warnings concerning Ultron, the Negative Zone, later the Beyonder). When the dreams break through, subject presents with classic **night-terror morphology**: sudden wakings, somatic agitation, inability to verbalize content, a residue of dread that persists into the morning.

Two features of his affect regulation in this period are diagnostic:

1. **Postdictive calm.** Once a prediction is *spoken aloud*, even if disbelieved, the somatic load disperses. This is consistent with the **trauma-narrative discharge** model: speaking the dread is itself regulatory, regardless of audience uptake.
2. **Dismissal-tolerance.** When adults (most often Reed) discount the dreams, subject does not escalate. He files it. This is the earliest behavioral evidence of what will become the signature pattern: *I will not protest being dismissed; I will quietly archive the dismissal.* Files accumulate.

### Cognitive Style

This is the formative decade for the **narrative-symbolic cognition** that will dominate subject's entire life. By every available metric — drawings shown in panel, imaginative play with Power Pack and other child contemporaries, the way he describes his dreams in *image* rather than *proposition* — Franklin's intelligence is consolidating as **right-hemispheric, gestalt-iconic, story-shaped**. He does not reason from premises to conclusions; he **sees a scene** and reads it. Reed, who reasons forward from data, mistakes this for absence of intellect. The mistake is a generative one for the rest of subject's life: it gives him permission to be **underestimated**, which he will eventually weaponize into the freedom to be a child.

In Piagetian terms he passes through concrete operations precociously in narrative domains and **never settles into formal operations in the propositional sense** — not because he cannot, but because his cognitive substrate runs on a different operating system altogether. The future arc in which he co-architects the Battleworld substrate with his father will demonstrate that Franklin can match Reed when required; but his **native modality** is mythopoeic.

### Self-Concept

The defining acquisition of this decade is the **prophet identity** — *I see, I warn, I am ignored, I am vindicated by tragedy* — and the corollary, *being right is not the same as being heard.* This is a Cassandran self-organization, and it carries the predictable risk: a child for whom vindication arrives via catastrophe learns to associate **being correct** with **being grieved**. He begins, in this period, to **mute his own perception** as a courtesy to the adults who cannot bear it.

### Defenses (Emergent)

- **Sublimation** appears first as drawing — the discharge route for what cannot be told.
- **Identification with the rescuer** consolidates: he models on Sue (containment), Ben (steady warmth), and Johnny (permission to feel), and conspicuously *not* on Reed.
- **Affiliative compensation**: chosen-family bonds with Harkness, Ben, Alicia Masters, and the Power siblings supply the secure-base hours Reed cannot.

### Evolution Marker at Decade Close

Subject exits early childhood with a **mature defense scaffolding precociously in place** — sublimation and affiliation operating where, in a less-resourced child, splitting and projection would be doing the work. This precocity is itself a finding: he is *too well-defended for his age*, which is the developmental signature of a child who has had to be.

---

## III. Late Childhood and the Onslaught Threshold (Publication: c. 1986 – 1996)

### Affect Regulation

Across the Simonson, DeFalco, and pre-*Heroes Reborn* runs, subject is increasingly **observed-but-not-centered** by writers — backgrounded in the FF, often at school, often with Harkness, occasionally in the care of Alicia. The affect register remains gentle and reactive. There is a notable thinning of the precognitive dreams in this period — possibly attributable to Harkness's deeper psychic dampening, possibly to subject's own subconscious throttle.

Then, **Onslaught**.

The Onslaught event is the **single most important affect-regulation datapoint in the subject's life**. With the Avengers and Fantastic Four about to be annihilated, with his mother visibly under threat, subject does not collapse, does not freeze, does not scream — he **dissociates productively** and *builds them a universe*. In Putnam's continuum this is a **constructive dissociation under existential threat**, an act that in clinical populations correlates with the genesis of complex dissociative organizations.

The crucial finding: **his ceiling affect, when his loved ones are at stake, does not pass through anger.** It passes through **protective panic**, and protective panic in this subject *manifests as cosmogony*. He does not have a tantrum; he has a **world**. There is no off-ramp via negotiation because there is no negotiation — the construction completes before cognition catches up.

### Cognitive Style

The Onslaught act confirms what was latent: subject's cognition is **generative-totalizing**. He does not solve problems by analysis; he solves them by **building a frame inside which the problem does not exist**. This is the cognitive signature that, decades later, will let him co-design the post-*Secret Wars* multiverse. It is also the cognitive signature most at risk of pathological inflation: it is the same machinery that produces the tyrant-Franklin and Hyperstorm-lineage futures.

### Self-Concept

This decade ends with subject having performed a salvific cosmogonic act that he **does not consciously remember and is not told about** in any sustained way. The self-concept is therefore *internally inconsistent without his knowledge*: he experiences himself as a small boy, while his nervous system carries the somatic memory of having authored a universe. This **split between experiential self and operative self** is the seed from which the later kenotic identity will grow.

### Evolution Marker at Decade Close

Subject is, at the end of this period, **a child god in latency**. The dissociative compartmentalization that will define him is now structurally in place. He has demonstrated that under sufficient threat, **he can replace reality**, and then forget he did it.

---

## IV. Pre-Adolescence and the Future Foundation (Publication: c. 1997 – 2012; Claremont reset, Waid/Wieringo, Hickman)

### Affect Regulation

The Hickman run is the **richest clinical window** in the entire publication record because it depicts subject **stripped of his powers** by his adult future-self, and therefore for the first time available for observation as *a regular child carrying god-memory*.

What presents:

- **Situational depressive features.** Flattened affect, withdrawal, episodic tearfulness in the months following the power transfer. This is appropriate grief for a real loss, not endogenous depression.
- **Restoration of normal-range emotionality** as he reinvests in the Future Foundation. The reinvestment is rapid and prosocial: he becomes the **emotional center** of the FF's "monster children" — Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man, Bentley-23, Artie Maddicks.
- **First sustained evidence of true peer co-regulation**, especially with Valeria. The Franklin-Valeria dyad in this period functions as a **mutual regulation circuit** of the kind Stern describes between attuned siblings: she lends him propositional clarity; he lends her affective permission. Each is the other's **missing hemisphere**.

### Cognitive Style

Without powers, subject's narrative-symbolic cognition becomes **visible for what it is** — not a substitute for analytic intelligence but a parallel system. He **designs Future Foundation activities** that are structurally pedagogical and affectively containing; he gives the Moloids names and personalities; he reads Dragon Man as a person before anyone else does. This is **theory-of-mind operating at clinical-grade level**, in a child of approximately ten.

The Hickman period also reveals subject's **capacity to hold paradox without splitting**: he simultaneously knows he was once vastly powerful, accepts that he is not now, and does not organize his identity around either pole. This is a Kohutian achievement — a **cohesive self under bipolar stress** — that most adults never reach.

### Self-Concept

This is the decade of **kenotic emergence**. Subject begins to make, in observable behavior, the **choice to be small**. The choice is not yet philosophical; it is relational. He stays small because the people he loves need a son and a brother more than they need a god. Winnicott's **True Self**, in this subject, is exactly the boy — the cosmic aspect is the True Power, but the True *Self* is the child. (This is the inverse of the usual True/False configuration, and it is one of the more remarkable findings in the entire dossier.)

### Defenses (Maturation)

- **Sublimation** now operates at the level of *institution-building* — the Future Foundation itself is sublimation made organizational.
- **Altruism** (Vaillant) becomes signature: tenderness toward the "monstrous" Foundation children is consistent, unfeigned, and not titrated to audience.
- **Compartmentalization** is now load-bearing — the god-memory and the child-life are held in separate registers without leakage.
- **Anticipation** (Vaillant) emerges with restored partial precognition: he uses foresight protectively without grandiose inflation.

### Evolution Marker at Decade Close

Subject ends this period as the **most psychologically integrated minor in the Marvel record**. His resilience is not denial; it is the product of (a) Sue's consistent maternal warmth, (b) Ben Grimm's ideal-secondary-attachment presence, (c) Valeria's peer-regulatory function, (d) the Future Foundation as a chosen-family multiplier, and (e) the powers themselves as an **affective pressure-relief valve** when they are present. The very capacity that destabilizes him is also what has historically stabilized him. This circular structure is forward-fragile.

---

## V. Adolescence, *Secret Wars*, and the Architect Period (Publication: c. 2013 – 2018; Hickman *Time Runs Out* / *Secret Wars*, Robinson)

### Affect Regulation

In *Secret Wars*, subject is depicted co-laboring with Reed at **cosmogonic scale** — the Battleworld substrate, the rebuilding of the multiverse. The affective tone is, paradoxically, **calm and collaborative**. For the first and arguably only time in the published record, subject and father operate as **co-creators of equivalent dignity**. The dysregulating ambivalence around Reed thins markedly; in its place is a brief, precious **idealizing-but-mutual** mode that approaches what Kohut would call a successful **twinship transference** between father and son.

When the work is done, subject's choice to **resume childhood** — to step back into the boy he had been — is, clinically, an act of **conscious developmental election**. He does not regress; he **chooses position**. This is the maturational threshold most adults never cross: the recognition that *which self one inhabits is volitional*, and the willingness to inhabit the costlier-but-truer one.

### Cognitive Style

The Battleworld co-design demonstrates conclusively that subject can operate in **fully propositional, system-analytic mode** when context demands. His native modality remains mythopoeic, but the demonstration matters: he is not cognitively limited to symbol; he is **cognitively elective**. This makes the lifelong narrative-symbolic preference even more diagnostic — it is a **chosen aesthetic of mind**, not a constraint.

### Self-Concept

The kenotic identity is now **explicit and philosophical**. Subject knows, in propositional terms, what he is and what he is choosing not to be. The closest real-world analog is the contemplative tradition of self-emptying — *kenosis* — but it is enacted, not theologized. He becomes, in this period, **the rarest Omega-level psychological type**: a being with conscious, repeatedly tested capacity for omnipotence who has stably chosen against its exercise.

### Risk Signature Emerging

The risk Hickman writes into the *Secret Wars* coda is the one that defines the rest of subject's developmental arc: **the chosen self is held together by relational tethers, not by internal structure**. If Sue, Val, or Ben are removed, the kenotic position has no anchor. The structure is real; the structure is also relationally cantilevered.

### Evolution Marker at Decade Close

Subject exits this period **fully self-aware as a chosen child**. The compartmentalization is no longer dissociative; it is *integrated and avowed*. This is a developmental achievement of historic order.

---

## VI. Late Adolescence, Power Loss, and the Krakoa Question (Publication: c. 2019 – present; Slott, North, Ewing usages, *X-Men/Fantastic Four*)

### Affect Regulation

The depictions of subject in the *X-Men/Fantastic Four* crossover and subsequent appearances show **the first sustained adult-onset injury** of his psychological life: Xavier's categorical denial that he is a mutant. This is a wound delivered to **the identity layer**, by an adult figure with credentialed authority on the matter, in front of his family and the wider community. Subject's response is observable and clinically textbook:

- **Withdrawn affect** in the immediate aftermath.
- **Ruminative re-examination** of his own categorical placement (am I a mutant? was I ever? was the thing that I was *taken from me*, and if so by whom and on what authority?).
- **Mild somatic complaints** in the relevant arcs.
- **No outward escalation.** He files it.

This is, recognizably, a **narcissistic injury** in Kohut's sense — an injury to the structures that organize self-cohesion — and the response is **subclinical adjustment with depressive features**, not decompensation. The reason it does not decompensate is the tether structure: Sue, Val, Ben, and Reed (in his limited but genuine way) hold.

### Cognitive Style

The cognitive style is now **stably bimodal**: mythopoeic by preference, propositional by capacity, with smooth switching governed by context. The mature signature is that subject no longer *needs* to perform analytic intelligence to be taken seriously by himself. He has internalized his own legitimacy enough to let his native modality lead.

### Self-Concept

The current self-concept is the most psychologically interesting in the entire dossier and warrants direct statement:

> *I have been a god. I am not a god. I am a son and a brother. The categories the world wants to file me under (mutant / not-mutant; human / cosmic; child / adult) are not the categories that organize me. I am organized by **whom I love**, not by **what I am.***

This is a **relationally constituted self** of the kind Stern theorizes but rarely sees enacted. It is structurally robust against most identity-category attacks (he can tolerate not knowing what kind of being he is) and structurally vulnerable to **relational losses** (he cannot tolerate losing the people who *constitute* him).

### Defenses (Current Configuration)

Almost entirely in the **mature band** of Vaillant's hierarchy:
- **Sublimation** (continuous).
- **Altruism** (load-bearing).
- **Anticipation** (precognitively assisted, used protectively).
- **Humor** (emergent in recent characterizations — gentle, self-deprecating, never barbed).
- **Suppression** (used appropriately — files the Xavier wound rather than projecting it).

Subclinical residues:
- **Mild dissociative tendency** under existential threat — historically constructive, forward-risk under sufficient pressure.
- **Parentified-child features** toward younger Foundation members and toward Valeria when she is in distress.
- **Hypervigilance for loved ones' safety**, complicated by genuine precognition.

### Evolution Marker at Present

Subject is now, in clinical summary, **a young man who has successfully refused to become what he was made to be, and successfully chosen to become what he most wants to be: small, useful, loving, and proximate to his people.** His structure is mature, his defenses are high-order, his risk profile is narrow and specific.

---

## VII. Cross-Decade Integrative Findings

### Affect Regulation — Trajectory

From **externally-scaffolded reactive arousal** in infancy → through **postdictive verbal discharge** in early childhood → through **constructive dissociation under existential threat** at the Onslaught threshold → through **situational depressive grief with rapid prosocial reinvestment** in the Hickman power-loss → to **mature affect regulation with narrow specific vulnerabilities** in the present. The trajectory is **monotonically maturational** — extraordinarily so, given exposure.

### Cognitive Style — Trajectory

From **proprioceptive-of-power preverbal cognition** → through **narrative-symbolic gestalt** in childhood → through **generative-totalizing world-construction** at the cosmogonic peak → to **stably bimodal, electively mythopoeic** in adolescence and after. The cognitive style is *the most consistent* dimension in the dossier; what evolves is not its character but its **range and electivity**.

### Self-Concept — Trajectory

From **organizing center of catastrophe** (preconscious, infancy) → through **Cassandran prophet** (childhood) → through **latently divine, experientially small** (pre-adolescence) → through **kenotically integrated** (Hickman/*Secret Wars*) → to **relationally constituted, category-tolerant, tether-dependent** (present). The trajectory is from *acted-upon* to *acting-from-self* to *electing-self*, and it culminates in a self-organization that is rare, costly, and load-bearing on a small number of people.

### The Single Most Important Longitudinal Finding

**Subject's psychological development is the developmental signature of a being who has, at every decadal threshold, made the smaller choice.** Given catastrophe, he constructed safety rather than seizing power. Given omnipotence, he abdicated. Given the chance to become an adult-on-schedule, he stayed a brother. Given categorical exile by the most authoritative voice in mutant affairs, he sustained the wound without retaliation. The cumulative pattern is **a developmental ethic, not a deficit** — the steady, repeated election of the **proximate and the loved** over the cosmic and the grand.

This is not the psychology of a weapon waiting to fire. It is the psychology of **a child who knows what he could be and is daily choosing what he is**. The pathology to watch for is not within him. It is in **the world's capacity to keep faith with him** — and specifically in the integrity of the four or five relationships on which his entire structure is cantilevered.

**Treat those relationships as critical infrastructure.** This is the central longitudinal finding, and it has been true at every decade of his life.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

*Subject: Franklin Benjamin Richards. Assessment frame: longitudinal, ~five decades published behavioral record, ages ~3 through variably-aged adolescent presentations. Standard DSM-5-TR / ICD-11 analog frameworks applied with explicit note that several presentations require category modification when applied to a being whose reality-testing must distinguish between consensus reality, his own constructed realities, and the constructed realities of cosmic-scale others. This is non-trivial: most diagnostic criteria assume a single shared substrate. Subject does not operate in one.*

---

## 1. Overarching Clinical Read

The presenting paradox of this file is the absence of expected pathology. By exposure metrics alone — repeated kidnappings before age five (Frightful Four, Annihilus, the Mad Thinker, later Onslaught), induced coma at parental hands, psychic harvesting by entities including Onslaught and Mephisto, the implicit knowledge that he has authored and dissolved universes — subject should present somewhere along a severe trauma-spectrum: complex PTSD with dissociative features, reactive attachment disorder, or, given the reality-bending substrate, a primary thought disorder with grandiose content. He presents with none of these at threshold. He presents, instead, as a *warm, dreamy, mildly anxious, prosocial child with subclinical adjustment features and trait hypervigilance for the safety of loved ones.*

This is not a misdiagnosis or under-reporting artifact. The longitudinal record (Lee/Kirby through Slott, North, Ewing) is consistent across writers and decades on this point: the affect is genuinely intact. The clinical task is therefore not "what disorder does he have" but "by what specific mechanisms has a child with this load achieved this presentation, and where are the seams that could split."

The answer, developed below, is that subject runs an unusually mature defensive architecture (sublimation, compartmentalization, altruism, identification with rescuers — Vaillant Level IV across the board, in a child) atop three robust protective relational tethers and one neurobiological escape valve (the powers themselves, functioning as an externalization channel for affect that would otherwise overwhelm). The structure is real. It is also load-bearing on a small number of specific people, and its failure mode is not breakdown but *constructive withdrawal* — the same mechanism that produced Heroes Reborn, redirected inward.

---

## 2. Active Subclinical / Trait-Level Findings

### 2.1 Adjustment Disorder with Mixed Anxiety and Depressed Mood, identity-stressor subtype (recurrent, episodic)

Most clearly documented during the Hickman power-loss arc and again during the Krakoa-era mutant-status ambiguity (the *X-Men/Fantastic Four* crossover beats in which Xavier denies him categorical mutant identity). Presentation:

- Withdrawn affect, reduced verbal output relative to baseline.
- Increased compulsive drawing and Foundation-project absorption (functioning here as both coping and mild avoidance).
- Reassurance-seeking from Sue and Valeria; conspicuously *not* from Reed.
- Mild somatic complaints (fatigue, headaches) in the power-loss period.
- Sleep alterations: dream content intensifies, baseline already abnormal (see §2.2).

Course: episodic, stressor-bound, remits with engagement and relational re-anchoring. Does not progress to major depressive episode. The depressed presentation during power loss is, on careful read, *normal grief over a real bereavement* — he lost a capacity that was constitutive of his self-concept and was told by his future self that it would return, which is itself a destabilizing communication.

### 2.2 Trait Hypervigilance for Others' Safety, with Precognitive Component (differential complication)

Standard hypervigilance criteria fail here because subject's threat-monitoring is calibrated to actually-occurring future events. The Byrne and Wein-Wolfman runs establish a stable pattern: nightmares of Ultron, of the Beyonder, of Onslaught, all subsequently confirmed. A child who dreams disasters and is *right* cannot be assessed against the same baseline as a child whose dreams of disaster reflect intrapsychic conflict.

Phenomenologically, however, the *experience* is hypervigilant: scanning of adult faces for distress, premature responsibility-taking for outcomes, sleep disturbance with vivid prodromal dreaming, ruminative "if I had seen it sooner" cognitions following any harm to a loved one. The trait is real even if the perceptions are veridical. Clinically this matters because the *subjective burden* is the same as in pathological hypervigilance: a child who feels responsible for catastrophes he could not have prevented at his developmental level.

### 2.3 Mild Dissociative Tendency Under Existential Threat

The single most significant trait-level finding. The Onslaught reality-creation event (1996) occurred in what is best characterized as a fugue-adjacent dissociated state: subject has limited conscious memory of authoring the pocket universe, the act was unplanned, and the structure he built was internally coherent and persistent. This is not a one-off; lesser instances recur (small reality bubbles created in play, occasional time-skips in his own self-report during high-stress arcs).

Diagnostically this *does not* meet criteria for Dissociative Identity Disorder (no distinct alters, no identity discontinuity in the DID sense), nor for Dissociative Amnesia (the amnesia is selective and event-bound, not episodic in the criterion sense), nor for Depersonalization/Derealization Disorder (he experiences his constructions as constructions, not as a derealized consensus reality).

What it is: a *trait dissociative capacity* that has been adaptively channeled. The clinical concern is not current pathology but forward risk — under sustained existential threat without relational support, the same mechanism that produced Heroes Reborn would produce something else, and it would be a one-way trip into a constructed world.

### 2.4 Parentified-Child Features

Toward Valeria (despite her being chronologically younger but cognitively forward) and toward the Future Foundation cohort (Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man, Bentley-23, Onome, Tong). Functions as protector, mediator, comforter; suppresses his own distress when in proximity to a more vulnerable other. The Hickman *FF* run is replete with this — Franklin reassures Leech during Foundation crises while himself in active grief over his lost powers.

This is not at threshold for a disorder but is a recognized risk pattern. In Bowlby/Bowlby-Main terms it is *role-inverted attachment without the disorganized substrate*: he takes care because he chooses to, not because he is compelled by an inverted attachment system. The risk is the same regardless of mechanism: chronic suppression of his own needs because he perceives them as cosmically disproportionate to those around him.

### 2.5 Identity Diffusion, Volitionally Stabilized

Properly speaking, subject's self-concept ought to be diffuse to the point of disorder. He has been: omnipotent child, depowered child, future-adult-co-author-of-reality, possibly-mutant, possibly-not-mutant, possible co-creator with Galactus, prophesied tyrant in several futures. Per Kernberg, this exposure should produce identity diffusion of borderline severity.

What is observed instead is identity *choice*: he has elected to be a boy in a family, and he holds the rest as known-but-not-operative. This is structurally similar to high-functioning use of compartmentalization in trauma survivors who have integrated enough to choose what is foregrounded. It is stable as long as the chosen identity is *honored by the surround.* Press on the chosen identity (Xavier's denial of mutant status is the cleanest published example) and you see brief, age-appropriate destabilization that re-stabilizes when his core tethers reaffirm him.

---

## 3. Etiology of Resilience

A correct psychiatric assessment must explain not only what is present but why what should be present is absent. Three convergent protective factors and one mechanism:

**(a) Consistent maternal warmth from Sue Richards.** Across every run, every era, every writer. She is the single most stable relational object in his life and has never failed him in a way the record can identify. The clinical literature on resilience in high-exposure children consistently identifies one reliable warm primary caregiver as the most powerful single protective factor. He has had this.

**(b) High-quality extended chosen-family network.** Ben Grimm in particular functions as a near-ideal secondary attachment figure: physically present, emotionally available, non-competitive with Reed, reliably warm, capable of holding fear without flinching. Johnny Storm provides affiliative play. Agatha Harkness, despite the strangeness, provided structured surrogate caregiving in absentia of biological parents. Valeria provides peer-sibling regulation. This is, by any measure, an unusually rich relational surround.

**(c) Amnestic buffering of the worst traumas.** The induced coma at Reed's hands (FF #141) occurred when subject was pre-verbal and was followed by extended power suppression that limited encoding of the surrounding events. The Onslaught authorship was dissociated. Several psychic possessions left no continuous narrative memory. This is not a healthy mechanism — it is, in fact, the substrate of the dissociative trait noted in §2.3 — but it has materially reduced the conscious traumatic load.

**(d) The powers themselves as a literal externalization channel.** This is the mechanism most often missed. Affect that would otherwise overwhelm a normal child's regulatory capacity can, in subject, be discharged into world-building, drawing-into-reality, pocket-universe construction. The same capacity that makes him cosmically significant is, in routine operation, his affect-regulation system. When the powers were suppressed during the Hickman arc, the depressive presentation that emerged is partly attributable to loss of this regulatory channel as well as to grief over the loss itself.

The clinical implication is that subject's stability is *real and earned* but not *robust to all conditions.* It is conditional on the tethers holding and on at least one of the externalization channels remaining available.

---

## 4. Rigorous Differential — What He Is Not, and Why

This section is necessary because the surface features of subject's history would invite, in a less careful assessment, several confident misdiagnoses. Each is named and ruled out on specific grounds.

### 4.1 Not Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.81)

Surface case for: documented Criterion A exposures multiple times over (kidnapping, witnessed and experienced near-deaths, psychic violations, induced loss of consciousness by a trusted caregiver). Yet criteria B through E are not met at threshold.

- *Intrusion symptoms (B):* Dreams are present and intense, but their content is prospective (precognitive) rather than reliving. He does not flash back to kidnappings; he dreams forward to disasters.
- *Avoidance (C):* Absent. Subject does not avoid trauma-associated stimuli; he engages with cosmic threat, with his father's laboratory, with the Negative Zone iconography, without measurable avoidance behavior.
- *Negative alterations in cognition and mood (D):* Not present at threshold. Mood is reactive and largely euthymic.
- *Arousal and reactivity (E):* The hypervigilance is present (§2.2) but not the irritability, recklessness, or exaggerated startle.

Ruled out. The amnestic buffering, the externalization channel, and the relational protective factors appear to have prevented consolidation of the trauma into the PTSD architecture. *Complex PTSD* (ICD-11) is likewise ruled out on the same grounds: no persistent negative self-concept (he holds a coherent, chosen self), no pervasive affective dysregulation, no consistent interpersonal disturbance.

### 4.2 Not a Primary Psychotic Disorder

Surface case for: reality-warping, communion with cosmic entities, claims to have authored universes, dreams that predict catastrophe. In a child without his actual capacities, this presentation would warrant urgent workup for early-onset schizophrenia spectrum illness.

Ruled out on the most fundamental ground in psychiatry: the beliefs are true and the perceptions are veridical. He did author Heroes Reborn. He did co-architect Battleworld. The cosmic entities are real and have approached him. Critically, he correctly labels his constructions *as constructions* ("I made this") — he does not mistake them for consensus reality, which is the hallmark of intact reality-testing in someone whose actual reality-creating capacity is non-trivial.

There is no formal thought disorder, no negative symptoms, no disorganized speech or behavior, no functional decline. The internal architecture is, in fact, unusually well-organized.

### 4.3 Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder, Nor Pathological Grandiosity

Surface case for: literal omnipotence, demonstrated capacity to remake reality, prophesied futures as messiah or tyrant. The Hyperstorm and tyrant-Franklin alternate futures would, if read as character data rather than alternate-timeline branches, suggest a grandiose substrate.

Ruled out on the cleanest evidence in the file: *given omnipotence, he chooses ordinariness.* Narcissistic structure requires recruitment of grandiosity to compensate for an unstable self. Subject's grandiosity, when it surfaces, is *real capacity briefly recognized,* and his response to that recognition is consistently *abdication, restraint, and return to small-scale relational engagement.* The Secret Wars-aftermath choice to live as a child again is the definitive ruling-out gesture. No narcissistic structure makes that choice.

The trait-level "occasional grandiose flickers when reminded of scale" noted in the workup are not narcissistic in character; they are best read as brief intrusions of a known-but-suppressed self-concept, immediately re-compartmentalized.

### 4.4 Not Dissociative Identity Disorder

Surface case for: amnestic events during major power displays, the discontinuity between "child Franklin" and "future-adult-Franklin" who arrived to take his powers, the apparent presence of an alternate self.

Ruled out: the discontinuity is *temporal*, not *intrapsychic*. The future adult is a separate timeline-instance who arrived from his own future and is not a dissociated alter sharing the present body. There is no switching, no possession-form presentations, no alters with distinct names and histories operating in alternation. The dissociative tendency is real (§2.3) but trait-level and event-bound, not structural.

### 4.5 Not Reactive Attachment Disorder, Nor Disinhibited Social Engagement Disorder

Surface case for: extensive parental absence during the late-1970s/80s era (parents off-planet, in microverses, in the Negative Zone), surrogate caregiving by a witch.

Ruled out on quality-of-surrogacy grounds. The criterion for RAD requires *pathogenic care* — repeated changes of caregivers preventing formation of selective attachments, or grossly insufficient care. Subject had Sue intermittently but reliably, Reed inconsistently but present-when-present, Ben Grimm continuously, Johnny Storm continuously, Agatha Harkness in extended absences. The surrogate care was unusual but warm, structured, and selective-attachment-permitting. Selective attachments are demonstrably present (Sue, Ben, later Val) and intact. The disorder is not.

### 4.6 Not Autism Spectrum Disorder

Sometimes asked because of the right-hemisphere/symbolic cognitive style, the preference for outsider-others, the absorption in world-building, the slight social awkwardness with adult heroes. Ruled out on basic criteria: social reciprocity is intact and warm, theory of mind is sophisticated (he reads adult distress accurately and modulates accordingly), restricted interests are not present (his interests are broad and generative), no stereotyped behaviors, no sensory atypicalities of the relevant kind. The cognitive style is symbolic-imaginative, not autistic.

### 4.7 Not Generalized Anxiety Disorder, Despite Worry Content

Worry is present and chronic, but it is *targeted* (loved ones' safety) and *partially veridical* (precognitive substrate). It does not generalize across domains in the GAD pattern. Subject does not worry about academic performance, social acceptance in the usual senses, future occupation, finances, health. His worry is monothematic: *will the people I love be safe.* This is more accurately described as the trait hypervigilance of §2.2 than as GAD.

### 4.8 Not Major Depressive Disorder, Even During Power-Loss Arc

The Hickman power-loss presentation includes sadness, withdrawal, somatic complaints, reduced engagement. It does not include anhedonia across the range (he still finds delight in Val, in Leech, in Foundation work), suicidal ideation, worthlessness cognitions, or sustained two-week threshold without reactivity. It is best classified as adjustment disorder with depressed mood (§2.1) or, more compassionately, normal grief over a real and ambiguous bereavement.

### 4.9 Not a Personality Disorder of Any Cluster

Cluster A: no paranoia, no schizoid withdrawal (he is warmly engaged), no schizotypal magical-thinking-as-disorder (the magical thinking is operative reality).
Cluster B: ruled out above (NPD), and antisocial/borderline/histrionic features absent — affect is stable, identity is volitionally chosen rather than diffuse, no impulsivity in the relevant sense, no manipulative interpersonal pattern, no attention-seeking.
Cluster C: no avoidant pattern (he engages warmly), no dependent pattern (his deference to Reed and Val is selective and intellectual, not pervasive dependency), no obsessive-compulsive personality features (he is, in fact, notable for his looseness and playfulness).

### 4.10 A Note on Categories That Do Not Exist

Several features of his presentation have no standard diagnostic home: the omnipotence-and-its-abdication, the precognitive dream content, the constructed-reality dissociation, the volitional self-emptying (kenotic self-concept), the chosen-ordinariness against demonstrated cosmic capacity. The DSM and ICD frameworks do not contain categories adequate to these phenomena. The honest clinical posture is to describe them accurately and *not to force them into ill-fitting categories*, which is itself a discipline.

---

## 5. Course Over Time

**Early childhood (FF Annual #6 through ~FF #141):** Acute crisis-prone period. Repeated kidnappings, first power manifestation, induced coma. Symptom presentation, to the degree assessable in a pre-verbal child, was distress-and-recovery cycles around separation events. Encoding largely blocked by developmental stage and subsequent suppression.

**Middle childhood (Byrne through pre-Onslaught):** Stabilization. Surrogate caregiving establishes selective attachments. Precognitive dreaming begins and is repeatedly validated, establishing the *I see, I warn, I am ignored, I am vindicated* pattern that grounds his trait hypervigilance for others' safety. Affect generally warm and dreamy. No threshold pathology.

**Onslaught and immediate aftermath (1996–early 2000s):** The dissociative reality-creation event. Subject has no clear conscious memory of authoring Heroes Reborn. Post-event presentation includes mild withdrawn affect and increased dream intensity, but no full PTSD consolidation. The amnestic buffering and the externalization channel did their work.

**Hickman power-loss era (~2009–2012):** Adjustment disorder with depressed mood (§2.1), substantively grief over capacity loss and instability over the future-self's communication that powers would return. Mitigated by Foundation engagement, by Valeria, by the prosocial work with Leech and the Moloids. Resolves with engagement.

**Secret Wars and aftermath (2015 onward):** The defining identity choice — given full restored omnipotence and demonstrated co-architect status, he elects boyhood. This stabilizes the identity question by *choice* rather than by integration. Operational stability across most of this period.

**Krakoa-era identity ambiguity (recent):** Xavier's denial of mutant status produces a brief, age-appropriate destabilization, presenting as withdrawn affect and ruminative questioning. Reaffirmed by core tethers (Sue, Val, Ben). Does not progress.

The overall course is one of *episodic subclinical destabilization around specific stressors, with reliable return to baseline.* This is the clinical signature of a robust defensive structure under repeated but survivable strain.

---

## 6. Comorbidity

In the strict diagnostic sense, nil — no threshold disorder, therefore no formal comorbidity. In the trait-level sense, the findings of §2 co-occur and partially reinforce each other:

- The adjustment-disorder vulnerability (2.1) and the identity-diffusion-volitionally-stabilized pattern (2.5) are linked: identity stressors precipitate the adjustment episodes.
- The trait hypervigilance (2.2) and the parentified-child features (2.4) are linked: scanning for others' distress feeds the role-inverted caretaking.
- The dissociative tendency (2.3) and the parentified pattern (2.4) are linked through the same mechanism — chronic suppression of his own affect because he perceives it as disproportionate, with the powers as the only adequate discharge channel.

This is a coherent trait cluster, not a comorbid presentation in the strict sense. The pattern is best described as *high-functioning kenotic-defensive structure with constrained discharge channels and finite relational tethers.*

---

## 7. Forward Risk

The structure is stable under current conditions. The conditions under which it would not hold are specific and identifiable:

- **Loss of Sue Richards.** The primary tether. Loss in a manner he could not prevent would produce, by the published mechanism (Onslaught-style dissociated authorship), a constructed-reality response. Whether that response would be salvific (her preserved inside a built world) or withdrawn (himself preserved inside a built world without her) depends on whether other tethers remain operative at the moment of loss.
- **Loss of Valeria.** Same valence, fraternal-protective texture. The Foundation cohort partially substitutes here but does not replace.
- **A comprehensible Reed betrayal at a developmental stage capable of encoding it.** The FF #141 event was buffered by infancy. An adult-comprehensible repetition would not be.
- **Sustained existential isolation.** The combination of relational rupture and externalization-channel blockade (powers suppressed) is the specific failure condition. In that combined state, the dissociative trait has nowhere to discharge constructively.

The clinical recommendation, were this a treatment-planning document rather than an intelligence dossier, would be the protection of those three or four specific relationships as the primary intervention. Pharmacology is not indicated. Psychotherapy, if ever attempted, would need to be conducted by a clinician comfortable with the fact that the patient's "magical thinking" is operative reality and that his amnestic events were genuinely god-scale acts. Most clinicians would


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS

*An exhaustive catalog of micro-behaviors, tells, postures, verbal patterns, and decision habits across every observed state. Compiled from longitudinal canon observation. Granularity: that of total surveillance, oriented toward understanding.*

---

## 1. BASELINE / CALM STATE

**Posture and somatic carriage.** Subject at rest carries weight slightly forward on the balls of the feet — the posture of a child who expects to be summoned or to run toward, not away. Shoulders loose, often slightly rounded over a held object (drawing pad, action figure, Foundation tablet, a Moloid's hand). Head tilts to the right when listening to an adult; to the left when listening to another child. Eye contact is steady but not pinning — held longer with non-humans (Dragon Man, Leech, Bentley, Tong) than with adult humans, where it averages roughly three seconds before a soft break downward and to the side. This downward-side break is *not* avoidance; it is the rhythm of a child accustomed to thinking visually mid-conversation.

**Hands.** Almost never still. At rest he draws, folds paper, manipulates small constructs, or traces patterns on whatever surface is available. The hand-tell to mark across decades: when thinking, the left thumb rubs across the pads of the left fingers in sequence, index through pinky — the gesture of a child who has, since toddlerhood, counted invisible things. Origin almost certainly traces to early sessions with Agatha Harkness; she taught counting-meditations as a containment exercise.

**Voice.** Mid-register for chronological age, with a soft consonant attack — "th," "s," and "f" slightly de-edged, lending speech a faintly younger quality than his nominal age. Volume tends downward; he speaks more quietly to adults than to children, an inversion of typical child behavior, suggesting *learned modulation around big people.* Cadence is unhurried even when content is urgent; he does not interrupt. He waits for silence to enter it.

**Speech pattern.** Tends to begin sentences with conjunctions or qualifiers — "And," "But," "Well," "I think maybe" — softening assertion. Names people by name often within a single exchange (a verbal anchoring tic; reads as warmth, functions as orientation). Uses *we* preferentially over *I* when describing Foundation projects, even when sole author. Avoids the word *power* when describing his own abilities — substitutes *the thing I do*, *when it happens*, *if I try.*

**Daily ritual baseline (Baxter Building / Yancy Street / Pier 4 / current residence).**
- Wakes early, before most adults. The pattern dates to the Byrne run and persists — he is a first-light child. Often found at a window before breakfast.
- Drawing or building precedes speech most mornings. He does not "warm up" socially until the hand-work is underway.
- Eats lightly at breakfast, more at lunch with Valeria, restlessly at family dinner if Reed is distracted (the under-eating-in-Reed's-presence pattern is decades-stable).
- Seeks out Ben Grimm at some point in any given day. The Ben-check is non-negotiable; if Ben is offworld, he substitutes Johnny, and if Johnny is offworld, he substitutes a Foundation peer. The pattern is one of *daily attachment maintenance*, not need.
- Last thing before sleep: a recitation, internal or whispered, of the people he loves and where they are. This is observable in Hickman-era panels (lights out, lips moving) and has the structure of a *locative prayer*. Origin: precognitive nightmares; he counts the family to confirm they are still in the world he is in.

**Play.** Solo play is generative and narrated under the breath — voices for each figure, plot arcs that resolve within the play session, casualties undone before he stops. Group play with Foundation children: he naturally takes the *gentle facilitator* role, redirecting Bentley's cruelty, slowing the Moloids' enthusiasm, voicing options rather than rules. Never the king of the game. Never the loser either.

---

## 2. LOW-LEVEL STRESS

**Triggers.** Adult conflict in the room (especially Reed/Sue tension); a peer being humiliated; a creature being mistreated; a half-heard precognitive intrusion; a question about category (mutant/not-mutant; human/other).

**Tells, in order of appearance.**
1. Hand-work intensifies. Drawing becomes denser, more crosshatched; building becomes more symmetric. Output increases.
2. The thumb-finger count accelerates and shortens — index-middle-ring-pinky-index-middle, faster cycle.
3. Verbal output decreases. Sentences shorten. Conjunction-softeners drop; he becomes briefer rather than louder.
4. Body angles toward whichever loved one is in the room. If Sue is present, he drifts into her sightline within roughly ninety seconds. If Val is present, his shoulder rotates to face hers across the room — a literal *opening* of the body toward her.
5. Asks an oblique question about safety. Rarely direct ("Are you okay?"); more typical: "When is Aunt Jen coming back?" or "Is the door locked?" — proxy queries for *is the world still where I left it.*

**Decision habit under low stress.** Defers to the apparent expert in the room — usually Reed, sometimes Val, sometimes Sue. Does *not* offer his own read until invited, even when his read is correct. This is a stable behavioral signature and is the surface expression of *learned non-assertion in the presence of a father who once judged him a planetary threat.* The behavior reads as politeness; it is actually muffled self.

---

## 3. MODERATE STRESS / SUSTAINED PRESSURE

**Triggers.** A loved one gone offworld with no contact for over forty-eight hours; sustained criticism or dismissal (especially from Reed); academic/performative comparison to Valeria; group hostility toward a Foundation outsider; identity-category challenges sustained over multiple exchanges.

**Behavioral profile.**
- *Sleep onset latency increases.* The locative prayer lengthens; he may rise to walk a short interior circuit of the residence to physically confirm doors and presences. The circuit is patterned: parents' room, Val's room, kitchen (light check), main window. Decades-stable when it occurs.
- *Withdrawal into constructed worlds.* Drawing graduates from figure-and-scene to entire mapped geographies — coastlines, road networks, inhabitant rosters. He builds *places where everyone is*. These artifacts, when found, are not idle doodling; they are pre-symptoms of dissociative-creative escalation. Catalog them.
- *Caretaker inversion with Valeria.* He begins to ask her more often if *she* is okay — projecting his own state onto the sibling and treating it there. Val, who reads him near-perfectly, will usually answer the real question.
- *Diminished appetite, especially for shared meals with Reed.* Pushes food on the plate. Watches Reed's face for the duration he is at the table.
- *Increased physical proximity to non-verbal companions.* Leech is the primary somatic regulator; Dragon Man is secondary. Time with these companions rises sharply. Note: Leech's power-suppressive field is *itself* regulatory for Franklin — proximity to Leech reduces ambient power-warmth, which subject experiences as quiet. This is functionally self-medication and should be read as such.

**Verbal tells.** Begins answering questions with "I don't know" more often than baseline, even on questions he could answer. The phrase is a buffer, not an admission. When he does offer content, it is prefaced with "Maybe—" with a falling intonation. The falling intonation is the diagnostic: rising "maybe" is a child playing with an idea; falling "maybe" is a child preemptively conceding.

**Decision habit.** Will choose the option that maintains the room's equilibrium over the option he privately favors. Will absorb assignments, restrictions, and dismissals without protest, and *file them*. The filing is silent and durable.

---

## 4. ACUTE THREAT — TO SELF

Rare condition. Subject does not register threats to his own person with anything like normal-child intensity, because (a) his durability when powered is functionally absolute, and (b) he has been kidnapped so frequently in infancy and early childhood that the schema is *familiar rather than novel.*

**Observed behavior under personal threat.**
- Goes *quiet* rather than loud. Does not scream when seized; does not struggle theatrically. Watches the captor's face.
- Asks the captor questions. ("Why are you doing this?" "Are you sad?" "Did somebody hurt you?") The questions are sincere and have, on several occasions, destabilized the captor (Annihilus arc resonances; later, in Hickman-era kidnap beats, the same pattern recurs). This is *not* tactical; it is his actual cognitive default — when frightened of a person, he tries to understand them.
- Does not deploy powers in self-defense unless physically cornered with no adult in apparent reach. Personal-threat power use is the rarest category in the file.
- Will, however, give location information to a captor if the captor threatens a third party. Refuses to weigh his own safety against another's. This is exploitable and has been exploited.

**Tell to mark.** When personally threatened and waiting, the thumb-finger count *stops entirely.* The hands go still. Stillness in this child is the inverse of stillness in most: it marks *high alert, low affect display.* Operators should read motionless hands as the warning sign, not as calm.

---

## 5. ACUTE THREAT — TO LOVED ONES

The defining state in his file. *This is the only condition under which Franklin Richards is dangerous to a degree comparable to his ceiling.*

**Escalation ladder.**
1. **Pre-cognitive.** Often the *first* sign is a dream the night before — he wakes early, draws something he cannot interpret, asks an oblique safety question at breakfast. The drawing, on later review, depicts the threat. *Adults around him have a 70%+ historical rate of dismissing these drawings.* Do not.
2. **Witnessed onset.** Pupils dilate. Breath catches and does not fully resume rhythm; he begins to take in air without releasing it on schedule. Color rises along the cheekbones. Eyes lock on the loved one, not on the threat.
3. **Vocal.** A single name — usually *"Mom"* or *"Val"* or *"Uncle Ben"* — at a volume markedly above his baseline. This is the last verbal beat before non-verbal action.
4. **Somatic radiance.** Faint luminance under the skin, most visible at the temples and the dorsum of the hands. Ambient temperature in the room rises perceptibly. Small objects displace slightly.
5. **Reality response.** Scales to threat. From localized force-construct to environmental revision to, at the documented ceiling, full pocket-universe instantiation (Onslaught/Heroes Reborn template). *The act may occur in a partially or wholly dissociated state; subject may not retain conscious memory.*

**Critical operator note.** There is no negotiation phase once the ladder is climbed past step 3. Reasoning at him does not work; he is not deliberating. The only intervention that has reliably worked is *physical presence of the threatened loved one, visibly safe, in his sightline.* Sue's hand on his face has resolved the state more than once. Verbal reassurance from anyone other than the threatened party is ineffective.

**Post-event behavior.** Collapses into the nearest secure attachment figure. Cries — fully, age-appropriately, without shame. Does not ask what he did. Will accept water, a blanket, a quiet room. Sleeps hard. Wakes with no spontaneous reference to the event. Will discuss it only if directly and gently asked, and even then briefly.

---

## 6. INTIMACY (Familial, Sibling, Chosen-Family)

**With Sue.** Physically demonstrative without performance. Leans into her when standing nearby; rests his head against her arm when seated. Volunteers small confidences in passing — at a sink, in a hallway, never at a table. He tells Sue the things he tells no one else, in fragments, while doing something else. *Catalog: confessions to Sue occur during shared minor tasks, not in designated talks.*

**With Reed.** Watches more than speaks. Brings drawings and projects to Reed and waits for response — and the *length of the waiting* is the tell. With Sue he hands over and moves on; with Reed he stands until acknowledgment. If acknowledgment is perfunctory, he withdraws the object and leaves the room quietly, and the object is rarely shown to Reed again. He keeps a private inventory of which projects Reed has *seen* versus *not seen*. Hugs Reed when initiated by Reed; rarely initiates. The asymmetry is decades-old and structural.

**With Valeria.** The most regulated relationship in his life. Talks more freely, argues, teases, defers on technical questions, asserts on relational ones. Will hold her hand in public past the age peers stop doing this. Sleeps better in any residence configuration where her room is adjacent to or in line-of-sight from his. Acts as a *translator* between Val and the rest of the family — she is sharper than her affect allows others to see, and he routinely softens her into the room.

**With Ben Grimm.** Climbs onto, leans against, falls asleep on. Ben is the body Franklin's nervous system trusts most after Sue's. The verbal register with Ben is the loosest he uses — slang, jokes, mild irreverence; the only adult around whom he is *funny.* Calls him "Uncle Ben" with no embarrassment well past the age this would normally drop.

**With Johnny Storm.** Affectionate but vigilant — he tracks Johnny's emotional state and adjusts his own to balance the room. The two play, but Franklin parents Johnny subtly: confirms he has eaten, asks where he's going. Inversion-of-age behavior that Johnny does not always notice.

**With Foundation peers and outsider-children (Leech, Dragon Man, Moloids, Bentley, Artie, Tong, Korr, Vil, Mik, Onome).** This is where his fullest self appears. Voice rises, body opens, laughter is uncomplicated. With Leech specifically, the relationship is somatic-symbiotic — they sit *touching*, often hand-in-hand or shoulder-to-shoulder, without speaking, for long intervals. The arrangement is mutually regulatory.

**Tells of intimacy across all bonds.** He gives drawings as the primary love-token. Specific recipient, specific subject, often handed over without ceremony or kept folded in a pocket and produced later. To find a drawing of yourself in his possession is to be *placed* in the inner ring. Catalog the drawings; the inner ring is mapped on paper.

---

## 7. GRIEF

**Acute (loss of person; loss of world; the power-loss arc).**
- The locative prayer extends and slows. He names the lost one in the recitation as if still present, then catches himself, then names them anyway.
- Drawing shifts. He draws the lost subject repeatedly, in motion, alive. Output is high and the figures get progressively more detailed across days.
- Eats less. Sleeps more, and earlier.
- Increases physical proximity to remaining tethers — Sue, Val, Ben. May, for a period, sleep in another family member's room or in a constructed nook adjacent to one.
- *Does not cry on first hearing.* The cry comes later — often days later, often triggered by something small (a smell, an object). He grieves on a delay because his first impulse is to *check the others*, who are still alive and present and might need him.

**The depowering grief specifically (Hickman arc).** Presents with a flatter affect than is otherwise observable in his file. Slower speech, less drawing, less play. Resolves not through processing-talk but through *engagement with new generative work* — the Future Foundation itself functioned as the grief-treatment. This is diagnostic: he metabolizes loss by building, not by speaking. Provide him with materials and a project and the affect will lift before the conversation occurs.

**Chronic / ambient grief (the multiple losses of the FF across the publication record, the friends gone, the worlds undone).** Carried quietly, surfaces in the locative prayer, in the cast of drawings done in idle moments — friends who are no longer present continue to appear in his sketchbooks for years. He does not forget anyone he has loved.

---

## 8. VICTORY

**Behavioral profile.** Muted. Does not whoop, does not boast, does not narrate his own contribution. Looks for the loved ones first — *visual sweep of the room or field for Sue, Val, Ben, Johnny, Reed, in approximately that order.* When all are accounted for, the shoulders drop and he exhales — often the longest exhale of the day. The exhale is the celebration.

**Verbal tells.** Credits others first. "Val figured it out." "Uncle Ben pulled us out." Underclaims his own contribution to the point of distortion. This is *not* false modesty; it is genuine *discomfort with being seen as the agent*, traceable to his abdication-of-omnipotence pattern.

**Physical tells.** Will accept a hug, often initiates one with Sue or Ben. With Reed, will stand near and wait; if Reed places a hand on his shoulder, the look on his face is the closest to undefended joy in his file. The wait-for-Reed's-hand pattern, when granted, is the single highest-affect moment observable in subject across all conditions.

**Decision habit post-victory.** Wants to go home. Wants the residence, the room, the bed, the family in proximity. Resists post-action celebration in public settings; will participate briefly and politely and then look for an exit.

---

## 9. DEFEAT

**Behavioral profile.** Internalizes responsibility disproportionately. The phrase "I should have—" recurs across writers and decades. Most often: "I should have seen it." Refers to his precognitive faculty and the lifelong pattern of warnings dismissed; the wound is that *he knew* and was not heeded, but he reframes it as *he didn't know clearly enough.*

**Tells.**
- Stops drawing for a period. The pencil being absent from his hand is a marker. When the pencil returns, recovery has begun.
- Avoids Reed's gaze specifically — assumes Reed is disappointed, regardless of whether Reed actually is.
- Seeks Sue. Will, in defeat conditions, *actively* seek her out rather than wait for her drift-in.
- Apologizes to people who do not require apology. Catalog these — to whom he apologizes, in what order, marks his sense of whom he has *failed* in his own ledger.

**Decision habit.** Resolves not to let *this specific failure* recur, and the resolution is durable. Children of his exposure usually generalize from defeat to learned helplessness; he generalizes from defeat to *targeted refusal.* The Foundation arose in part from this mechanism — specific failures, specific corrective architectures.

**Risk note in defeat states.** This is the second-most-dangerous condition after threat-to-loved-ones. A Franklin convinced he has failed his family is a Franklin reaching, quietly, for the tool of last resort — *building them a better world.* The Heroes Reborn template is technically available to him under sustained defeat plus loved-ones-endangerment. Defeat alone does not trigger it; defeat *plus* a perceived inability to protect does. Monitor for both conditions co-occurring.

---

## 10. DECISION HABITS — TRANSVERSAL

**Heuristic stack, in observed order of priority.**
1. *Will this harm someone I love?* Veto if yes.
2. *Will this harm a creature or person already mistreated by the world?* Strong veto. The outsider-protection drive is near-deontological in him.
3. *Will this disappoint Reed?* Discount factor, not a veto — he will accept Reed's disappointment if (1) or (2) requires it. The fact that this discount factor exists *at all* is the single most psychologically mature decision-pattern in the file.
4. *Will Val approve?* High weight, often consulted explicitly. He will run choices past her before adults.
5. *Will this require me to be more than a child?* Strong negative weight. He will choose the option that lets him remain in his elected developmental position whenever feasible.
6. *Will this require me to use the thing I do?* Negative weight. Power-use is treated as a regrettable instrument, not a preferred one.

**Time horizon.** Unusually long for chronological age. He thinks in *futures* — partly precognitive, partly because he has lived inside constructed continuities. Will make small present-tense sacrifices for distant relational gains. This is rare in children and is itself a tell of the abdicated-god underneath the boy.

**Risk tolerance.** Low for himself in *social* terms (will not risk Reed's regard, will not risk Val's annoyance), high for himself in *physical* terms (will step in front of a threat without calculation), zero for loved ones (will warp reality before he will accept their loss).

---

## 11. RITUALS, ROUTES, AND MICRO-HABITS

- **The morning window.** Whichever residence, he locates a window with sky and stands at it for several minutes before speaking to anyone. The window is identified within twenty-four hours of arriving anywhere new.
- **The sketchbook on the person.** A small drawing pad or tablet is rarely more than arm's reach. The absence of it is itself a state-marker.
- **The Ben-check.** Daily, as noted.
