- **The Val-check.** Visual confirmation of his sister at intervals; in any room, he locates her within seconds of entry.
- **The locative prayer.** Nightly, as noted.
- **The folded-paper pocket habit.** Tends to keep a folded drawing in a pocket — often a portrait of someone he loves. Functions as transitional object. Cycle the pocket and you can map who is currently weighing on him.
- **The thumb-finger count.** Constant, as noted; cycle rate is a stress indicator.
- **The kindness reflex to monsters.** When confronted with a designated-monster figure (creature, mutant outsider, villain's victim, escapee), his first behavior is to *make eye contact and speak softly to it.* The reflex precedes assessment. It has gotten him into trouble (creatures that were genuinely hostile) and has, more often, defused situations adults expected to escalate.
- **The drawing-as-gift.** As noted. Map the recipients.
- **The pause before the pronoun "I."** Subtle but observable across decades. He hesitates on the first-person singular, especially when the verb that follows describes capability. *"I... can try."* The hesitation is the boy-not-god reasserting itself in real time.

---

## 12. WHAT THE FILE INDICATES OPERATIONALLY

Franklin Richards is, behaviorally, the most readable Omega-level entity in the record — *if* one knows what to read. He telegraphs everything: in the count of his fingers, in the angle of his shoulders toward the loved one in the room, in the falling "maybe," in the locative prayer, in the absence of the pencil, in the silence of his hands. He does not lie well. He does not hide what he feels. The only thing he hides is *the scale of what he could do about it.*

The atlas above is, therefore, less a profile of a subject and more a *map of the load-


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

*What a week of continuous surveillance on Franklin Benjamin Richards would actually record. Compiled from longitudinal canon (Byrne, Simonson, DeFalco, Waid, Hickman, Robinson, Slott, North, Ewing) and inference appropriate to the subject's chosen developmental position and household ecology.*

---

## 6.1 Habitat and the Geography of a Day

Subject's primary residence across the publication record cycles between three structures, each of which produces a recognizably different daily pattern: **the Baxter Building** (Manhattan, 42nd & Madison vicinity in most depictions), **Pier Four** (interim quarters during Baxter destructions), and **Four Freedoms Plaza** in its various iterations. Beneath the architectural variance the household ecology is stable: a vertical home with laboratories below the living quarters, observation decks above, and — critically — a *children's floor* with progressively customized rooms. Subject's bedroom is invariably on an upper residential level, near Valeria's, with direct corridor access to Sue's quarters and a longer route to Reed's lab. The geometry matters: in any panic event subject can be at his mother's door in under twelve seconds and at his sister's in under five. He has measured this. He has not been asked to measure this. He measured it the first time he was old enough to map a corridor.

The Baxter's secondary residences — the Connecticut house (Waid-era), the rebuilt FF tower post-*Secret Wars*, and the Yancy Street brownstone variant — each preserve the same essential adjacency: **subject sleeps within sprint-distance of his mother and sister, and at deliberate remove from his father's workspace.** This is not framed in canon as choice; it is choice. He inherits a bedroom assignment in a new building and quietly trades for the one with the shorter line to Sue.

---

## 6.2 The Wake Cycle and the Morning Ritual Set

Subject is a *natural early waker* — documented across multiple writers in panels of Franklin already dressed and drawing while adults are still on coffee. Sleep onset is typically late by child standards (10–11 PM in Hickman/Slott depictions) because of his evening drawing practice (see §6.5); rise is nonetheless between 6:30 and 7:15 AM. This is not insomnia — it is the schedule of a child who has structured his own waking time around being alone with paper before the household ignites.

**The morning ritual, reconstructed from cumulative panels:**

1. **The check.** Within ninety seconds of waking, subject performs a relational sweep. He listens for Sue (kitchen sounds, voice in the hall, the specific cadence of her footfall — he can distinguish hers from any other adult's in the building). If she is not immediately audible, he goes to her door and looks in, then closes it without waking her. This is not anxious attachment in the clinical sense; it is the consolidation behavior of a child who has lost adults to space, to the Negative Zone, and to comas. He does the check, registers *present*, and exhales.
2. **The Valeria pass.** Sibling sweep. Val is usually already up and reading or in the lab; if she is still in bed, subject leaves her undisturbed but notes it. If she is in the lab, he detours to greet her — invariably gentle, often with a snack he has brought down for her because she forgets to eat.
3. **Dressing.** Subject is functionally indifferent to clothing — t-shirts (often FF-logo, sometimes faded shirts of unclear origin he refuses to retire), jeans, sneakers laced loose. He has been depicted in the same approximate uniform for two decades of publication; the constancy is the data. He does not perform identity through dress. His one consistent accessory across eras is a sketchbook, kept in a hip pocket or a small backpack.
4. **Breakfast.** Subject prefers breakfast in company; he will wait for whoever is around. Cereal-and-toast child by default; will eat what Sue makes; takes coffee in the recent aging-up depictions but adulterates it with milk. He eats *slowly* and *with conversation* — a behavioral tell of a child whose mealtime is his most reliable family-co-presence window.
5. **The window.** Many depictions show him at a tall window of the residence in the early light, looking outward at the city. Duration approximately one to four minutes. The function appears to be settling, not surveillance — though it is also surveillance.

---

## 6.3 The School and Education Pattern

Subject has been variably enrolled in standard private school (DeFalco/Ryan era), tutored at home by Sue and rotating FF associates, and — most consistently and importantly — taught within the **Future Foundation**, the in-house school Reed and Sue convened for gifted and "monster" children (Hickman). The Foundation is the most psychologically congruent education subject has ever had, and a surveillance log of his Foundation days reads like a single continuous social bond:

- **Morning seminar / project block** (Reed or guest lecturer): Subject attends, attentive but visibly less engaged than Val. Notetaking is *drawn* rather than written — he renders concepts as small marginal cartoons. He asks one or two questions per session; the questions are reliably *ethical-implication* questions rather than mechanism questions. ("But what happens to the people who already live there?")
- **Lab / build block:** Subject pairs with Leech by gravitational preference; with Bentley-23 by adult assignment, which he accepts without complaint. He is the child the Moloids cluster around. The Moloid clustering is documented and consistent.
- **Lunch:** Eaten with the Foundation kids, never alone, never with adults if he can avoid it. He distributes food. He gives away dessert with regularity that crosses from generosity into reflex.
- **Afternoon free block:** This is when his actual life happens — drawing, story-telling to the younger children, devising elaborate imaginative games whose rules he negotiates with patience that adult observers find startling.

In non-Foundation eras, his schooling is patchier and he is visibly less regulated. *The Foundation is, clinically, the best environment ever constructed for him* and the file should note any erosion of it as a leading indicator of decompensation risk.

---

## 6.4 The Sibling Ritual

Franklin and Valeria operate as a **paired daily unit** in every era they coexist. The ritual texture:

- **Morning snack delivery** (above).
- **Lab visitation:** He drops in on her work multiple times a day, asks what she's doing, listens to answers that exceed his vocabulary, and treats the explanation as a gift rather than a lecture. He does not try to keep up. He *witnesses* her — which is what she needs and what Reed often fails to provide.
- **Co-bedtime drift:** In residential panels, the two often converge in one of their rooms in the last hour before sleep — her on a tablet or text, him drawing, minimal conversation. This is the day's emotional decompression chamber for both. A surveillance log would mark it as the most stable hour in the household.
- **Crisis protocol:** When alarms sound in the building, subject's first movement is *toward Valeria*, not away from the threat. This is established behavior, not improvisation.

---

## 6.5 The Drawing Practice

The single most important non-power behavior in the file. Subject draws **daily, for hours, across his entire published childhood**, and the drawing is not casual — it is his cognitive externalization, his emotional regulation, and his sublimation channel (see §3). Specifics:

- **Materials:** Crayon in early eras; markers and colored pencils mid-childhood; in Hickman/Slott depictions, a mix of physical sketchbook and tablet, with subject preferring physical paper when distressed.
- **Subjects:** His family (frequent, schematic, affectionate), monsters (sympathetic monsters — never frightening ones), invented worlds with their own geographies and inhabitants, and — critically — *futures*. He draws what he dreams, including precognitive content (Byrne run). He has, on multiple occasions, drawn events before they occurred. He does not flag these; he files them in the same stack as everything else.
- **Volume:** Inferable at hundreds of pages per month at peak. Reed's archives contain a non-trivial fraction of them, catalogued by Sue.
- **Location:** Floor of his bedroom, kitchen counter, lab corner near Val, occasionally the observation deck. He does not draw in Reed's lab; that workspace is coded as not-his.
- **Tell:** When subject stops drawing for more than a day, something is wrong. The Hickman power-loss arc shows reduced drawing volume; the Krakoa identity arc shows the same. Drawing cessation is a leading indicator and should be flagged.

---

## 6.6 Habits of Care — The Outsider Routine

A surveillance week would record, with metronomic regularity, **caretaking behavior toward the household's marginal members**. Specifically:

- **Leech.** Daily contact. Subject seeks him out, sits near him, shares food, includes him in games. The bond predates and survives multiple continuity shifts.
- **The Moloids.** Subject names them, distinguishes them, and remembers their preferences. They orient toward him in any room he enters.
- **Dragon Man.** Treated as family, not as construct. Subject talks to him in the same register he uses with Ben.
- **Any new "monster" child** introduced to the Foundation: subject is the first to make contact, reliably, within the first hour.

This is not performance and not strategy. It is a settled habit of orientation. The file should mark that subject's *daily attention budget is disproportionately spent on whoever in the room has the least social capital.* This is the most consistent behavior in his published life after the drawing practice.

---

## 6.7 The Uncle Network

Subject's two most-utilized adult attachments outside of Sue are **Ben Grimm and Johnny Storm**, and his rituals with each are distinct and well-documented:

- **With Ben:** Physical co-presence, low verbal load. Subject sits near Ben when scared and does not need to talk about it. Ben reads. Subject draws. The room regulates. Ben taught him to throw a baseball (Waid run, explicit); subject is mediocre at it and does not care, because the lesson was the point. Ben is the adult subject goes to *when he is afraid and does not want to alarm his mother*. This is a precise and clinically significant role.
- **With Johnny:** Higher-energy, play-coded, performative — subject is *louder* around Johnny, more childlike in the cartoon sense. Johnny is the adult subject goes to *to be silly*. Johnny is also the adult who, in multiple panels, has flown subject across the city for no reason but delight; subject remembers each occasion in granular detail.
- **With Reed:** Brief, formal, intellectually framed. Subject seeks Reed out for *information*, not comfort. He times these approaches — he goes to Reed when Reed is between projects, never during, because he has learned the cost of interrupting. He leaves Reed's lab when Reed's attention drifts, without protest, and goes to find Ben.

The triangulation is the behavior. Subject has unconsciously distributed his attachment needs across three men because no single one of them can or does meet the full set, and Reed is the partial-availability node.

---

## 6.8 Food, Sleep, Body

- **Appetite:** Normal for age. Mild preference for sweets, indulged by Ben, rationed by Sue. Will eat what he is given without complaint; will not eat shellfish (one panel-established aversion, Waid era, never explained).
- **Sleep:** 7–8 hours nightly. Sleep is *guarded* — door cracked, hallway light on in younger depictions, never fully dark. Nightmares (the canonical "Nightmare" arcs) historically intrude; subject does not always wake, and does not always remember, but Sue has been depicted finding him standing in the hallway in the small hours, not fully awake, having drifted toward her room. This sleepwalking-toward-mother behavior is rare but documented and should be flagged as the somatic signature of his deep attachment-anxiety substrate.
- **Body usage:** Unathletic, unhurried, comfortable in his skin in a way most powered children are not. He moves like a child who has never been chased and also like a child who has never had to chase. He sits on floors. He climbs furniture in the Baxter the way another child would climb a tree. He is physically affectionate — leans on Sue, accepts Ben's headrubs, hugs Val without negotiation.
- **Hygiene:** Age-appropriate, indifferent. Hair is uncombed unless Sue combs it.

---

## 6.9 Weekly Rhythm

A reconstructed week of surveillance would show approximately the following pattern, with the caveat that crisis events overwrite it without warning roughly twice a month:

- **Weekday mornings:** Wake-check-eat-school, as above.
- **Weekday afternoons:** Foundation work, drawing, sibling co-presence.
- **Weekday evenings:** Family dinner when possible (Sue enforces this; Reed attends with variable success; subject's mood tracks visibly with whether Reed showed up); drawing or reading after; sibling drift hour; sleep.
- **Saturdays:** Most variable. Often a "Johnny day" (outing, low-stakes adventure, ice cream); occasionally a "Ben day" (slow, ballgame on, lunch out). Sometimes a Sue day — museum, walk, neutral co-presence. *Rarely a Reed day* — those are scheduled by Reed, anticipated by subject with visible eagerness, and disappointing more often than not.
- **Sundays:** Quiet. Home day. Subject draws longer on Sundays than any other day. The household is most cohesive on Sundays and subject's affect is correspondingly highest.

---

## 6.10 Crisis-Mode Routine

When the Baxter alarms sound — which a week of surveillance will, statistically, record — subject's behavior is *protocol-tight* and self-trained:

1. **Locate Val** (under five seconds).
2. **Locate Sue** (verbal call, not movement, if Sue is already in motion toward him).
3. **Secure Leech / nearest Foundation child** if present.
4. **Move to the designated shelter point** Reed established (varies by building; subject knows all of them).
5. **Wait.** Subject is *good at waiting*. He draws while waiting. The drawing during shelter is qualitatively different — tighter, smaller, more controlled — and Sue has learned to read his post-crisis drawings as an affective barometer.

The protocol is followed *until* the threat reaches someone he loves, at which point the protocol dissolves and the powers — if available — fire. This is the dangerous seam in his routine. Subject is compliant, regulated, and patterned right up to the moment compliance fails to protect, and then he is something else entirely, and then he is a small boy again, and then he does not remember the middle part with full clarity.

---

## 6.11 The Quiet Rituals

A surveillance file is incomplete without the small repeated behaviors that carry disproportionate meaning. Subject's set:

- **The doorway pause.** Before entering any room containing Reed, subject pauses fractionally in the doorway. Not hesitation — *registration*. He is checking the weather.
- **The pocket sketch.** When anxious in public, subject draws a small figure on the inside of his own wrist or the corner of any available paper. Always the same figure — a four-pointed star, sometimes with a face. Self-soothing iconography. Origin unestablished; consistency over many years.
- **The goodnight circuit.** In residential eras, subject performs an end-of-day round: Val's door, Sue's door, sometimes Ben's door, occasionally Reed's lab from the threshold without entering. He says goodnight or he doesn't — the *route* is the ritual.
- **The window again, at dusk.** Mirror of the morning window. Longer in duration. He is, by inference, scanning the sky.
- **The name-saying.** Subject says the names of the people he loves, quietly, when alone — caught on panel only a handful of times but consistent enough across writers to be canonical. It is an inventory. It is a tether-check. It is, functionally, prayer.

---

## 6.12 Synthesis

A full week of surveillance on subject would produce a record of remarkable, almost suspicious *normalcy* — a child who wakes early, draws constantly, loves his sister, eats with his family, keeps gentle company with the household's strangest members, defers to his father, leans on his uncles, watches the city from windows at the day's hinges, and goes to sleep with the door cracked. The omnipotence is invisible in the daily log. *That invisibility is the achievement.* It is the daily, hour-by-hour, ritual-by-ritual labor of a being who has chosen to live as a small person inside the shape of an ordinary boyhood, and who is held in that shape by routines as load-bearing as the walls of the building he lives in.

Disrupt the routines and you disrupt the boy. Disrupt the boy and you disrupt the cosmos he has agreed, daily, not to remake.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS
## Section 6: RELATIONSHIPS I — Family & Origin Bonds

*The subject's nuclear and quasi-nuclear attachments mapped at maximum granularity. These are the load-bearing tethers identified in §4 as critical infrastructure. Each is presented as a longitudinal file: origin, observed micro-behaviors across publication, evolution by era, present-day state, characteristic failure mode, and leverage profile. Note: "leverage" here is diagnostic — what would shift him — not adversarial recommendation.*

---

### 6.1 — SUSAN STORM-RICHARDS (Mother)

**Origin and Foundational Imprint.** The mother nearly died giving him form (*FF Annual #6*); the infant's first environmental fact was that he existed because she had been willing to be torn apart for him, and because three men had crossed into anti-matter to keep her from being torn apart. This is encoded somatically, pre-verbally. Subject does not "remember" it; he *runs on it*. Every behavior toward Sue across fifty years of canon reads as an unconscious repayment schedule against an originating debt the child cannot articulate.

**Micro-Behavior Inventory (longitudinal).** Across the Byrne, Simonson, Waid, Hickman, and Slott runs the following tells recur with statistical reliability:
- He orients his body toward her in group panels. When Sue is in a room, Franklin's shoulders square fractionally toward her even when he is speaking to someone else. Compare with his orientation toward Reed, which is frontal-deferential at greeting and then *lateral-avoidant* thereafter.
- He reaches for her hand without looking — a high-confidence attachment tell, indicative of internalized object permanence of caregiver.
- He calls her "Mom," never "Mother," never "Sue" — consistent across writers and ages, including his adolescent and aged-up depictions. The diminutive is preserved as a deliberate marker of position.
- When frightened, he goes *to* her, not *behind* her. He does not seek shelter; he seeks contact. Distinguishing tell from anxious-clingy attachment, which seeks concealment.
- He sleeps better in her vicinity. Multiple bedside scenes (Byrne run; Hickman *FF* #6, the bedtime-story beats) show him settling into theta-state breathing within seconds of her presence.

**Dynamics.** Sue is the *only* relationship in his file with no recorded ambivalence vector. She is the regulated mother of an unregulatable child — and the canon repeatedly shows her as the figure who can *hear* his powers as something other than a threat or a resource. She is the only adult who treats his reality-warps the way one would treat a child's drawings: with curiosity, pride, gentle critique, and an insistence on bedtime regardless. This stance — *I see what you can do and I am still requiring you to brush your teeth* — is the single most therapeutic intervention in his life. It anchors his chosen-ordinariness self-concept (see §3).

**Evolution.** The relationship has not transformed so much as *thickened.* The toddler reaching for her hand and the post-*Secret Wars* adolescent who returns to her as a son after co-architecting a multiverse are doing the same thing. What changes is what he has on the other side of the equation; what does not change is the relational gravity. Notably, during the Hickman power-loss era — clinically his depressive window — Sue's increased physical proximity (hair-stroking panels, walk-and-talk scenes) correlates with his recovery curve.

**Trust / Safety.** Maximal. The only adult to whom subject discloses without internal editing. He tells Sue things he does not tell Reed *and* does not tell Valeria — the privately-frightened things, the cosmic-vertigo things, the things he has seen in dreams he cannot decide are dreams.

**Failure Mode.** Catastrophic. The *Heroes Reborn* event was a Sue-jeopardy response; the original template will refire under any sufficiently credible threat to her, with outcomes scaling to the perceived magnitude of risk. If Sue is killed in his presence and he cannot prevent it, the differential per §4 collapses immediately into *dissociative-creative withdrawal* — the construction of a reality in which she is not dead. This would not present as villainy; it would present as a child who has gone very quiet and a universe that has gone subtly wrong.

**Leverage.** She is the only person who can verbally talk him down from a powered state. Voice alone, no contact, no force — her *spoken instruction* registers at a pre-cognitive level that bypasses his powers' protective autopilot. This has been demonstrated across writers. It is also the most dangerous fact in his file, because it means anyone who can imitate, coerce, or replace her acquires a control surface.

---

### 6.2 — REED RICHARDS (Father)

**Origin and Foundational Wound.** *Fantastic Four* #141: the father switched the son off. The act was triaged as planetary necessity; it was nonetheless, in any framework of attachment, a breach of the floor. Sue understood this and left over it. The child does not consciously remember it. *His nervous system does.* This is the operative substrate of every Franklin-and-Reed interaction in the subsequent half-century.

**Micro-Behavior Inventory.**
- Franklin's body language at Reed's approach: frontal-bright at first contact, then a half-step lateral within ten seconds. Across writers. He does not turn his back; he turns his side.
- He brings Reed *artifacts* — drawings, devices, schematics co-developed with Valeria — and watches Reed's face during evaluation with a hunger that is the file's most painful recurring image. He is auditing for *seeing*.
- When Reed is distracted (which is most of the time), Franklin does not interrupt. He waits, then withdraws, then files. This non-protest is the file's most pathognomonic tell. Sue interrupts Reed. Ben interrupts Reed. Johnny interrupts Reed. Valeria interrupts Reed. Franklin does not.
- He uses Reed's first name in his head and "Dad" out loud. (Inferred from internal-monologue beats across the Hickman and Slott runs where the registers slip.)
- He asks Reed scientific questions he already knows the answer to. This is a courtship behavior; he is offering Reed a stage on which Reed can be the father Franklin wants.

**Dynamics.** Idealized intellectually; mistrusted somatically. He admires Reed in a register that is almost theological — the man who explains the universe — and avoids Reed in a register that is almost cellular. Reed underestimates him with shocking consistency because Franklin's cognition is symbolic-narrative rather than propositional (see §3), and Reed cannot parse symbolic cognition as *intelligence*. The compound injury is therefore *original breach* + *ongoing illegibility* — Reed both hurt him and cannot read him.

The corrective arc, partial: the *Secret Wars* (2015) sequence in which Reed and Franklin co-architect the rebuilt multiverse is, in attachment terms, the single most reparative event of the relationship. For one extended interval, Reed sees Franklin as a *peer* and a *son simultaneously*. Subject's affect in those sequences (Ribić art, Hickman script) is the most relaxed in his canon. Notably, Franklin chooses to revert to boyhood *after* this — i.e. he accepts the gift of being seen, then declines to remain in the position that required the seeing. He would rather be the son than be the equal.

**Evolution.** Three phases. (1) *Pre-suppression infancy*: Reed as awe-object. (2) *Post-suppression childhood through adolescence*: the lateral-avoidant pattern crystallizes; Franklin routes around Reed for safety needs while routing toward Reed for validation needs. (3) *Post-Secret Wars*: a tentative repair, fragile, contingent on Reed maintaining the recognition. Reed's tendency to reabsorb back into work has caused this repair to oscillate.

**Trust / Safety.** Asymmetric. Subject trusts Reed's *competence* absolutely and Reed's *attunement* not at all. He would let Reed perform surgery on him without anesthesia. He would not tell Reed he was sad.

**Failure Mode.** If Reed acts on Franklin again in a way that recapitulates the original suppression — overrides his agency for stated greater good, switches off a part of him for safety — the attachment will not detonate; it will *crystallize.* Franklin will become permanently formal with his father. No rupture, no argument, just a closing of the last door. Sue would notice within hours. Reed might not notice for years.

**Leverage.** Reed's recognition is the unfilled hunger. Any actor — benign or otherwise — who supplies sustained, accurate paternal seeing accrues attachment credit at a rate Reed cannot match while Reed remains Reed. This is why surrogate-father figures (Ben, briefly Wyatt Wingfoot in his orbit through Sue) have historically held disproportionate weight.

---

### 6.3 — VALERIA RICHARDS (Sister)

**Origin and Foundational Texture.** Valeria's gestation, birth, and metaphysics are tangled beyond ordinary biography — first failed pregnancy lost in the Malice arc; later born with Doom's assistance, named for Doom's lost love, briefly aged into adolescence and back. Franklin's relationship to her therefore begins in *loss* (the sister who almost wasn't) and stabilizes into *the most reliably regulated relationship in his file* (§3).

**Micro-Behavior Inventory.**
- They share a private register — vocabulary, half-sentences, look-and-nod sequences — visible across the Hickman *FF* run and Slott's *FF* (2018). They communicate at compression ratios no adult in the family achieves.
- He defers to her cognitively; she defers to him morally. Each has accepted the other's domain. This division is unforced and observable in every cooperative-problem panel: she proposes the *what*, he proposes the *whom for*.
- Physical proximity baseline is high — shoulder-to-shoulder seating, shared workspace at the Future Foundation, parallel-play in shared imaginative spaces.
- He lets her be the older sibling functionally while remaining the older sibling chronologically. This is unusual and deliberate.
- Under stress he checks her location before his own. Tell repeats across the *Future Foundation*, *FF*, and *Empyre* tie-in sequences.

**Dynamics.** Complementary by design and by election. Where Reed and Sue produced two children whose cognitive styles are nearly orthogonal — Franklin's right-hemispheric symbolic narrative cognition versus Valeria's hyperanalytic Reed-pattern — they have, against odds, *braided* rather than competed. Each child appears to have unconsciously decided that the other's gift is theirs to protect. Valeria shields Franklin's softness from Reed's underestimation; Franklin shields Valeria's hardness from the cost of being a child genius surrounded by people who keep forgetting she is a child.

The Future Foundation crucible — Leech, the Moloids, Bentley-23, Dragon Man, Alex Power, Onome — functioned as their *shared parenting laboratory*. They co-raised a household of difficult, brilliant, monstrous-looking children together. The bonding effect of this is structural; clinically they are something between siblings and co-parents of a chosen family. (See §6.7–8.)

**Evolution.** From infant-and-older-brother through Hickman's pivotal co-leadership of the Foundation through their adolescent depictions in recent runs, the relationship has not weakened with age — the opposite of typical sibling drift. This is because their relational task (mutual protection from being misread by their own brilliant family) is *renewable*; the problem they solve for each other does not go away.

**Trust / Safety.** Maximal in a different register from Sue. Sue is the safety floor; Valeria is the safety *peer*. He tells Sue what he is afraid of. He tells Valeria what he is *thinking*.

**Failure Mode.** If Valeria is killed or fundamentally altered, expect not a Heroes-Reborn-scale response (that template is Sue-keyed) but a *quieter* and more permanent shift: subject will collapse the chosen-ordinariness self-concept (§3) and re-assume powered self, on the grounds that the version of himself that elected boyhood is the version that had a sister to be a brother to. Without her, the rationale dissolves. The "Hyperstorm"/tyrant-future templates are reachable from this gate.

**Leverage.** Threats to Valeria do not produce protective-panic discharge — they produce *focused, premeditated* power use. The most dangerous Franklin in the file is not the one with Sue in danger (loud, reflexive, reality-scale) but the one with Valeria in danger (quiet, deliberate, surgical).

---

### 6.4 — JOHNNY STORM (Maternal Uncle)

**Origin.** Present from before birth; one of the three men who entered the Negative Zone to save Sue during the gestation crisis. Foundational, though Franklin has no memory of it. The somatic encoding is the same as Sue's: Johnny is part of the *reason he exists.*

**Micro-Behavior Inventory.**
- Franklin laughs more around Johnny than around any other adult. Documented across writers. Johnny is his *play-attachment* figure — the adult whose presence relaxes the chosen-restraint and permits foolishness.
- Physical play tolerance is high: roughhousing, aerial rides, pranks initiated by either side.
- He goes to Johnny with embarrassing questions before he goes to Sue or Reed. The Slott run and several Waid-era beats show this — questions about girls, about looking foolish, about being uncool.
- He defends Johnny verbally to other adults more than he defends any other family member. Sue does not require defense; Reed does not invite it; Ben is universally beloved; Johnny is the one people roll their eyes at, and Franklin will not tolerate it.

**Dynamics.** The *peer-adult* — the uncle who refuses to be wholly adult, which gives Franklin permission to be wholly child. Where Sue holds the floor and Reed holds the ceiling, Johnny holds the *play space* between. Johnny's own arrested-development features, often read as a flaw in his own file, function in Franklin's life as a clinical asset: an adult who has not given up on play models that play is permitted.

**Evolution.** Stable. Johnny is the family member whose relationship to Franklin has changed least across publication.

**Trust / Safety.** High. Different valence: trusted with his *frivolity* in a way no one else in the family is. The things he cannot bring to Sue (too heavy) or Reed (too unread) or Valeria (too undignified), he can bring to Johnny.

**Failure Mode.** Johnny's repeated near-deaths and Negative Zone disappearance (Hickman arc) have already stress-tested this attachment. Subject's response to those losses was *grief without dysregulation* — the rare clean response, suggesting that the Johnny-attachment, while warm, is not load-bearing for self-structure. He can survive losing Johnny. He would not survive it well, but the structure would hold.

**Leverage.** Modest. Threats to Johnny mobilize Franklin but do not unleash him. Johnny is also the family member most likely to *successfully distract* Franklin from a forming spiral — a function clinically equivalent to a behavioral interruption protocol.

---

### 6.5 — BENJAMIN GRIMM (Paternal Surrogate / "Uncle Ben")

**Origin.** Present at birth, present in the Negative Zone for the gestation crisis, present at virtually every crisis since. The single most consistent adult presence in the subject's life, full stop.

**Micro-Behavior Inventory.**
- Franklin climbs on Ben. From toddlerhood through aged-up depictions, the somatic pattern of *physical contact-seeking with Ben as climbable terrain* persists. Ben is the only family member whose body Franklin treats as *furniture* in the affectionate sense — shoulders, back, arms as perches.
- He goes to Ben when he is *scared*, not when he is sad. Sue is for sadness; Ben is for fear. This division is consistent across writers — when something has frightened Franklin, the panel that follows shows Ben.
- He calls him "Uncle Ben." Never "Mr. Grimm," never "the Thing," never "Ben" alone. The honorific is preserved.
- He defends Ben's *appearance* preemptively in interactions with strangers. Tell: he positions himself to manage other people's reactions to Ben's body. Inferred parentified-protector behavior.

**Dynamics.** Ben is, clinically, the *secondary attachment figure of textbook quality* noted in §4. He provides what Reed cannot: *unhurried adult presence.* Ben is never too busy. Ben is never thinking about three other problems. Ben sits down and is fully there. For a child whose father is constitutively elsewhere even when bodily present, this is the corrective experience that has likely prevented a more disorganized attachment outcome.

There is a quiet, profound symmetry in subject's tenderness toward "monstrous" outsiders (Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man — §6.7) and his uncle's appearance. The earliest lesson of his life was *the person who holds you when you are scared looks like a monster to strangers, and the strangers are wrong.* Every prosocial choice toward outsiders he has made since is a generalization from Ben.

**Evolution.** Stable to deepening. Ben's late-canon marriage to Alicia and his own fatherhood (the Slott run children) have added rather than displaced — Franklin folds easily into Ben's expanded household.

**Trust / Safety.** Maximal. The *fear-figure*. Sue is the regulated-mother, Ben is the safe-monster. Together they form a complete safety floor that Reed conspicuously does not occupy.

**Failure Mode.** Loss of Ben would be devastating but survivable, because Ben has already *taught the lesson* — the lesson is internalized, and his ongoing presence is reinforcement rather than precondition. The greater risk is a *betrayal* by Ben (vanishingly unlikely per Ben's own file), which would shatter the lesson and with it the prosocial-protection-of-outsiders core drive (§5).

**Leverage.** Ben's *physical reassurance* — the hand on the shoulder — is the highest-bandwidth non-verbal de-escalator in the file after Sue's voice.

---

### 6.6 — AGATHA HARKNESS (Witch-Governess / Early Surrogate)

**Origin.** Brought in as nanny in the Lee/Kirby tail and retained through the Thomas/Wein/Wolfman eras. The toddler who needed psychic dampening *to keep his powers from incinerating the household* was raised, in significant measure, by a centuries-old witch in a Whisper Hill house full of strange artifacts. This is not background; this is *first cultural soil.*

**Micro-Behavior Inventory.** (Inferentially reconstructed; subject's early childhood with Agatha is sparsely documented but consequential.)
- Subject's *imaginative-symbolic cognition* (§3) bears Agatha's fingerprint. The child who thinks in stories, characters, drawings, pocket-worlds was taught by a woman whose epistemology was narrative-mystical, not propositional-scientific. This is the inverse of Reed's pedagogy.
- His comfort with the uncanny — talking cats, sentient houses, dead-but-still-present figures — derives from this period.
- His tolerance of *psychic intrusion* as a survivable category, rather than a violation requiring decompensation, is partly Agatha's gift. She normalized telepathic contact as a register of communication.

**Dynamics.** Agatha was the *containment* figure of his earliest powered years — the only adult capable of safely modulating him before he could modulate himself. The relationship was therefore one of *managed dependency* on a non-parent — a configuration that, handled by a lesser figure, would have produced significant attachment damage. Handled by Agatha, it produced a child unusually comfortable with being held by someone other than his mother.

**Evolution / Failure.** Agatha's death (the Vision-related events, *Avengers West Coast*; later reanimations and re-deaths) registers in subject's file as a *first death* — the first major attachment figure to be definitively lost. His response across his publication record has been notably contained: Agatha taught him that death is a category among others, not a terminus. This is doctrinal inheritance and clinically protective.

**Trust / Safety.** Was maximal in its window; permanent residue is high. She is one of the *internalized voices* — the figures who have continued to advise him after their physical departure.

**Leverage.** Posthumous. Anything bearing Agatha's signature — sigil, voice, recovered grimoire — would register with subject as authoritative in a way few living figures match.

---

### 6.7 — LEECH (Chosen-Brother / Foundation Ward)

**Origin.** Morlock child, power-nullifier, brought into the Future Foundation in the Hickman *FF* run. Functionally adopted by Franklin and Valeria as a younger brother.

**Micro-Behavior Inventory.**
- Franklin's tenderness toward Leech is the prosocial-signature behavior of his file. Hand-holding, shared meals, shared sleeping arrangements during crises, physical interposition when Leech is mocked or threatened.
- He uses Leech's name often, and softly. Naming frequency is a tell of attachment investment.
- He defers small choices to Leech — what to play, what to eat — beyond what is required. He is teaching Leech that his preferences matter, which is what no one was teaching Leech before.

**Dynamics.** Leech is the *thesis statement* of subject's worldview (§5). A child whose entire function is to *cancel* powers became the chosen brother of a child whose entire function *is* powers. The mutual canceling is not threatening to Franklin — it is *restful.* Around Leech, his powers are quieter; he reports this as relief rather than diminishment. The relationship is, in a real way, *therapeutic for both directions*: Leech receives a brother who is not afraid of him, and Franklin receives intervals of forced ordinariness he cannot otherwise achieve.

**Trust / Safety.** Mutual and high. Leech is one of the few beings in the file Franklin will physically *cling to* under stress — sibling-coded, not child-of-coded.

**Failure Mode.** Loss or weaponization of Leech would activate Franklin's *protector* core drive at the same intensity as a Valeria-jeopardy, but channeled defensively rather than offensively — he would build a shelter, not a counterstrike.

**Leverage.** Anyone perceived as threatening Leech is treated as threatening *the principle of outsider-protection itself*, which is the load-bearing moral structure of subject's chosen self-concept.

---

### 6.8 — THE FOUNDATION CHILDREN (Moloids, Bentley-23, Dragon Man, Alex Power, Onome, Artie Maddicks, et al.)

**Origin.** Co-parented with Valeria across the Hickman *FF* and


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# SECTION 7 — RELATIONSHIPS II: ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*The subject's nuclear and extended family proper (Reed, Sue, Valeria, the Future Foundation cohort treated as siblings) is handled in §6. This section maps the broader relational lattice: the chosen-family adults, the peer alliances, the surrogate caregivers, the proteges, and the small handful of true mentors. The list is shorter than the file's bulk would suggest, because subject's bond-pattern is unusual: he goes very deep with a few, and remains warmly cordial with everyone else. The file's load-bearing relationships outside the nuclear family number perhaps seven.*

---

## 7.1 BENJAMIN J. GRIMM ("Uncle Ben")

**Status: Primary secondary attachment figure. Clinical near-ideal.** If the file had to nominate the single relationship that explains why subject did not decompensate under his exposure load, this is it.

**History.** Present at the natal crisis (*FF Annual #6*); among the three men who went into the Negative Zone for the antimatter that saved Sue and made Franklin's birth survivable. Grimm is therefore, in the subject's earliest neural substrate, *the man whose body went into the dark place so that I could exist.* This is encoded prelinguistically and never overwritten. Across the Lee/Kirby tail, the Thomas/Conway middle, the Byrne era, the Simonson and Waid runs, Hickman, and into the modern Slott/North material, Grimm is the adult Franklin physically *climbs onto* when distressed — lap, shoulder, the crook of the rocky arm. The somatic data is extraordinarily consistent across forty-five years of art.

**Dynamic.** Grimm provides what neither biological parent can: *uncomplicated presence.* Reed is intellectually preoccupied and somatically distant; Sue is warm but frequently in cosmic-scale danger that requires her attention; Grimm is, in the subject's experience, *always available, always the same.* The grammar of the relationship is play, food, physical roughhousing scaled gently to the child, and the verbal register of working-class Yancy Street affection — which the subject has absorbed and quietly mirrors in his speech when relaxed (his "yeah" rather than "yes," his use of "buddy," his shrugging cadence when not in adult company, are all Grimm-isms, not Richards-isms).

**Trust/safety.** Maximum. Subject has, on multiple occasions across runs, defaulted to Grimm as the body to stand behind when frightened, even with Sue present — a tell. He will say things to Grimm he will not say to either parent, because Grimm does not *file* the information into a scientific framework or a maternal-worry framework; Grimm receives it as conversation.

**Evolution.** In toddlerhood, Grimm is the safe monster who proves to the child that monstrousness and tenderness coexist — the substrate for subject's later prosocial signature with Leech, Dragon Man, the Moloids. In middle childhood (the Byrne era), Grimm is the play-partner and the one who notices when Franklin is having a nightmare and sits with him without requiring him to articulate it. In the Future Foundation era, Grimm is the adult who *takes the FF kids' weirdness in stride* — Franklin observes this and uses it as a model for how to be in a room with people who are not like you. In the post-*Secret Wars* era, where Franklin has lived a god's life and chosen smallness, Grimm is the only adult who treats him *exactly the same* as before — no awe, no scientific curiosity, no maternal hovering — and this is the single most stabilizing input in subject's adolescent recalibration.

**Failure mode.** The Grimm tether is the hardest to break in canon — Grimm has been killed and returned, transformed and restored, married off and bereaved, and the bond has persisted through every iteration. The failure mode is not betrayal but *finality*: if Grimm were to die in a way that took, the subject's lower-affect floor would drop sharply, and the file projects a months-to-years withdrawal into constructed worlds in his bedroom. The Onslaught template would not necessarily re-fire from grief alone (it re-fires from acute *threat* to loved ones, not loss after the fact), but the dissociative-creative withdrawal noted in §4's differential would.

**Leverage.** Anyone wishing to *help* the subject in a crisis should route through Grimm before either biological parent. Grimm can ask Franklin to come out of a constructed reality and be obeyed; Reed cannot reliably do this and Sue can only sometimes. Anyone wishing to *harm* the subject by destabilizing him would target Grimm — and the file notes with concern that this has been tried (Frightful Four, Puppet Master, others) and the subject's protective-panic threshold is lowest when Grimm specifically is in danger, lower even than for Sue, because the Grimm-threat triggers no competing executive override (Sue can talk Franklin down from a Sue-threat; nothing analogous exists for Grimm).

---

## 7.2 JONATHAN STORM ("Uncle Johnny")

**Status: Older-brother-by-function. The relationship that teaches him how to be young.**

**History.** Storm is twenty-something when Franklin is born and remains, across publication, the family's perpetual adolescent. He is Franklin's *uncle* by blood (Sue's brother) but in functional role he is the cool older brother who horses around, takes him places he shouldn't, lets him hold things Reed wouldn't, and treats him as a co-conspirator rather than a charge.

**Dynamic.** Where Grimm gives unconditional presence, Storm gives *permission*. Permission to be loud, silly, reckless within scaled bounds, to like things that are not edifying. The subject's capacity for *play* — clinically critical given his exposure load — is co-cultivated by Grimm (physical play) and Storm (imaginative-mischief play). Storm is the adult who will lie on the floor with Franklin and the FF kids and build a blanket fort and then set part of it on fire on purpose to demonstrate flame control, and Franklin will laugh, not flinch. Reed could not do this. Sue would not.

**Trust/safety.** High but qualitatively different from Grimm's. Subject trusts Storm to be *fun* and to be *loyal*; he does not trust Storm for steadiness. He has, observably across multiple runs, gone to Storm with secrets he wants kept *from the adults* (meaning Reed and Sue) but goes to Grimm with secrets that he wants *held* without being kept from anyone in particular. The distinction is sophisticated and present from early childhood.

**Evolution.** Storm's own arc — Inhuman husbandry, deaths and resurrections, the Slott-era cosmic adventures, the Krakoa entanglements — has at times made him intermittently absent. Franklin tracks this with mild, characteristic non-protest: he registers the absences, files them, does not complain, and re-engages instantly on return. There is a small wound here that subject does not articulate: Storm is *the relative most likely to forget to come back on time*, and the subject has built a tolerant model around this rather than a resentful one.

**Failure mode.** Storm betraying confidence (telling Reed something Franklin asked him not to) would damage the relationship in a specific way — not rupture but *demotion* from the "secrets" tier. This has happened in minor form across runs and been recovered from. A larger failure — Storm choosing a romantic partner or cosmic adventure over Franklin during a crisis the subject experiences as acute — would produce the same pattern: tolerated, filed, not protested, quietly cooled.

**Leverage.** Storm is the adult who can make Franklin *laugh* out of a low state when laughter is the necessary intervention. Grimm can hold him; Sue can soothe him; Storm can crack him open. This is a non-substitutable function.

---

## 7.3 AGATHA HARKNESS

**Status: Foundational mentor. First teacher of containment. The complicated witch-grandmother.**

**History.** Engaged as Franklin's governess in the late 1960s (*FF #94*); functions as primary caregiver during the long stretches when Reed and Sue are off-world or otherwise unavailable. She is centuries-old, a witch of the Salem line, and she takes the assignment knowing the child is a reality-warper. She is, in subject's developmental file, the *first adult who was not afraid of him.* This matters disproportionately. She also instituted some of the earliest psychic dampening protocols on the subject, "for his safety" — a fact that complicates her position.

**Dynamic.** Severe-affectionate. Harkness's register is formal, exacting, and warmth-by-implication rather than warmth-by-expression. She holds the child to standards of conduct and self-mastery far beyond his chronological age and he, characteristically, *rises to them* without resentment. The relationship establishes a template the subject will return to repeatedly: *I can be loved by being asked to be more than I think I am, by someone who does not flatter me.* Reed will eventually occupy this slot too but late and incompletely; Harkness occupies it first and cleanly.

**Trust/safety.** High but bounded. Subject trusts Harkness's *judgment* and her *capability* absolutely — knows she will not be overwhelmed, knows she will not lie about what she sees. He does not seek physical comfort from her (the somatic data shows him standing beside, not climbing onto). The relationship is mind-and-conduct, not body-and-feeling.

**Evolution.** Childhood: governess, teacher, the adult who teaches him to *notice* what he is doing with his powers without shame. Middle period: increasingly intermittent as she returns to coven business and as Sue reclaims more of the parenting bandwidth; subject feels these absences as the loss of a *standard-holder*. Tragic inflection: Harkness's death(s) and complications around Wanda Maximoff's arc affect the subject indirectly — he learns, before he can process it cleanly, that even the unafraid adult can be undone. This is one of the encodings underlying his trait hypervigilance for others' safety: *the unafraid die too.*

**Failure mode.** The complication that Harkness *suppressed* aspects of his power "for his safety" is a low-grade unresolved item in his file. Subject has never (canon) confronted it explicitly. If it surfaced in adolescence with sufficient context, it would not rupture his memory of her — his disposition is to integrate rather than reject — but it would deepen a pre-existing wariness about adults who manage his powers *for* him. The relevant operational note: this wariness already exists from Reed; Harkness contributed to it but is not the primary source.

**Leverage.** Harkness's surviving artifacts, sites, and her familiar (Ebony) carry sentimental weight. Invocations of her name in genuine register can settle the subject when he is in a defiant-anxious state; invocations in manipulative register are *immediately* detected (she trained him to notice).

---

## 7.4 LEECH

**Status: Sworn brother. The defining elective bond of his middle childhood.**

**History.** Leech, the green-skinned Morlock child with power-nullification ability, is brought into the Future Foundation in the Hickman *FF* era. Subject latches onto him with an intensity that surprises the adults. The two share a room, share meals, share secrets, are functionally inseparable across Hickman's run and persist as a paired unit through subsequent writers.

**Dynamic.** The clinical underread of this relationship is that Leech is the *only person in the world who can turn Franklin off* — Leech's power negates Franklin's. This is not incidental to the bond; it is, the file assesses, *constitutive* of it. With Leech in proximity, Franklin gets to be a baseline boy. He is not a god in Leech's company; he is just a friend. Leech does not know that this is what he is providing, and Franklin does not articulate it, but the somatic and behavioral evidence is overwhelming: Franklin is *calmest* in Leech's room, *most childlike* in Leech's company, *most easily delighted* when Leech is present.

**Trust/safety.** Total. This is the only peer relationship in the file rated at the Grimm tier for trust, and it surpasses Grimm on the specific dimension of *being known as ordinary.* Grimm loves Franklin as Franklin; Leech does not register Franklin as anything other than Franklin. The difference is subtle and crucial.

**Evolution.** Began as Hickman-era Foundation pairing; survived multiple cast reshuffles, the Slott-era family return, and the post-*Secret Wars* recalibration. Subject has, on multiple occasions, refused arrangements that would separate them and has done so with a quiet stubbornness that is uncharacteristic of his usual deferential register — a tell that Leech occupies a non-negotiable position.

**Failure mode.** Leech's safety is, after Sue and Val, the most likely trigger for protective-panic escalation. Any threat to Leech that the subject perceives as both acute and within his power to prevent will fire his powers ahead of his cognition. The file rates a hypothetical Leech death as a tier-one catastrophic event for subject's psychological structure, comparable to loss of Sue and exceeding loss of either Grimm or Storm in destabilizing potential, because Leech occupies a *function* (turning him off, letting him be ordinary) that no other being currently fills.

**Leverage.** Leech is the single most efficient pacification protocol in subject's file: bring Leech into the room and Franklin's powers go offline and his affect normalizes within minutes. Conversely, Leech is the single most efficient destabilizer if threatened. Both these facts are operationally critical and almost certainly known to no antagonist, which is a security asset that should be preserved.

---

## 7.5 ALEX POWER

**Status: Childhood best friend (peer). The only human kid his own age he has been able to keep.**

**History.** Power Pack crossovers from the mid-1980s onward establish Alex Power as Franklin's age-mate and friend. The relationship has been used intermittently by writers but is consistently warm when revisited.

**Dynamic.** Alex is the friend with whom Franklin can be a *normal kid with weird parents*, because Alex also has weird parents and powers of his own, and the two of them have implicitly negotiated a peer space where the weirdness is the wallpaper, not the topic. Subject's interpersonal range with Alex is closer to the developmental norm for his chronological age than with anyone else — they talk about games, food, school-equivalent topics, family-complaint topics. This is *practice in being a kid* in a way that no adult and no Foundation pairing can provide.

**Trust/safety.** High within domain, modest across domain. Franklin will tell Alex things about wanting to be normal that he won't tell adults; he won't tell Alex about the cosmic-architecture material, partly because Alex couldn't hold it and partly because Franklin doesn't want it in the room when Alex is.

**Evolution.** Underused by canon, which is itself a datum — Franklin has had to develop without the kind of sustained peer-friendship most children have, and Alex is the closest the file has to one. The relationship persists in low-frequency revisits and the subject's affect on each reunion is markedly bright.

**Failure mode.** Low-risk relationship; the structural fragility is *neglect*, not rupture. If Alex were endangered, Franklin would respond, but the relationship is not load-bearing enough that loss would decompensate him; it would *grieve* him in the ordinary register and be integrated.

**Leverage.** Useful as a low-stakes social-bandwidth restorer. Time with Alex Power is one of the few interventions that produces ordinary-kid behavior in the subject without requiring Leech's nullification.

---

## 7.6 H.E.R.B.I.E. & DRAGON MAN

**Status: The household constants. Trusted in the way one trusts furniture and weather.**

**H.E.R.B.I.E.** The robot is, across decades, the ambient adult-presence of the Baxter Building — present, attentive, programmed for child safety, and treated by Franklin with the easy affection a child gives to a beloved pet that talks. Subject talks aloud to H.E.R.B.I.E. when alone in rooms in a way he does not with most living adults; the robot's non-judgmental processing makes it functionally a *journal that responds.* Significant for the file because this is where subject does much of his low-stakes externalization — the small worries that don't rise to "tell Mom" but need to be said out loud.

**Dragon Man.** The reformed android-dragon, post-Hickman-Foundation, is functionally a large gentle pet with intelligence; the subject loves him without complication. Dragon Man's docility around Franklin is consistent across runs and the somatic data shows the subject treating Dragon Man as *climbable safe space* second only to Grimm. The fact that subject's two most beloved non-human household figures are a robot and a dragon is itself a tell about his elective community: he gravitates toward beings whose categorical otherness is total and whose loyalty is unambiguous.

**Failure mode/leverage.** Both function as ambient stabilizers; loss of either would be grieved as the loss of household, not of person. Both are highly responsive to subject's affect and can be deployed as monitoring assets without subject perceiving surveillance — H.E.R.B.I.E. especially has been used this way by Reed historically, and the file notes this as one of the *small ongoing breaches of trust* the subject has not consciously catalogued but somatically registers (he is slightly more guarded around H.E.R.B.I.E. in Reed's presence than in Reed's absence — a tell most observers miss).

---

## 7.7 THE FUTURE FOUNDATION COHORT (Proteges)

**Status: Subject's first true exercise of mentorship/protective fraternity. The clinically critical *outward* relational vector.**

The Foundation gathers, under Reed's nominal aegis but in practice under Franklin and Valeria's daily care, a roster of "monster" and outsider children: Leech (covered separately), the Moloid brothers Mik, Korr, Tong, and Turg; Bentley-23 (Wizard's clone); Onome; Alex Power in rotation; Dragon Man as faculty-pet. With this cohort, Franklin shifts from being *the cared-for* to being *one of the carers*, and the file rates this transition as one of the two or three most psychologically generative arcs of his life.

**The Moloids.** Subject treats them with consistent gentleness, learns their names and their differences, mediates their disputes, includes them in play. They imprint on him as much as on Val. With Tong's eventual self-identification as female, Franklin's response is matter-of-fact acceptance — a data point that reads cleanly into his prosocial-outsider signature: belonging-category questions destabilize him about *himself* but he extends total grace to others on the same questions.

**Bentley-23.** The more difficult Foundation child — clone of a villain, prone to mischief and casual cruelty. Franklin's handling of Bentley is patient and persistent, modeling rather than punishing. This is, the file notes, the first context in which Franklin practices a stance he has only ever received: *holding standards for someone who needs them held.* It is Harkness's stance, transmitted. The subject's capacity to do this with Bentley is evidence that his identifications are functioning and his model of being-cared-for is intact enough to be re-emitted.

**Onome.** Specifically a relationship Franklin treats with attention to her intellectual seriousness, modeling Reed's better register without Reed's distance.

**Failure mode/leverage.** The Foundation as a group is a *load-bearing positive identity structure* for the subject — being the older child to whom others come is one of the few roles in which he gets to feel both competent and ordinary-scaled. Disruption of the Foundation (which has happened in canon during the recurring "FF disbands" beats) produces measurable affect-flattening in the subject within days. Restoration restores affect promptly. The Foundation is, in effect, his *workplace,* and depriving him of it deprives him of one of his more grounded daily structures.

---

## 7.8 ALICIA MASTERS

**Status: Trusted adult outside the inner four. Aunt-by-function via Grimm.**

The blind sculptor's presence in subject's life is steady, quiet, and qualitatively unique: she is the adult most likely to *ask him what he is making* and to take his answer seriously as art rather than as phenomenon. For a child whose creations have included pocket universes, the distinction between *artistic interest* and *cosmological interest* is enormous, and Alicia is one of the very few adults who consistently provides the former. Subject draws and shows her drawings he would not show Reed. Her blindness is not incidental to the bond — she cannot see *him* in the categorical way others do (the famous son, the powerful child, the phenomenon); she perceives him by voice and by the texture of his work, which is closer to how he perceives himself. **Failure mode:** none structural; loss would grieve in the ordinary register. **Leverage:** Alicia is one of three or four people who can ask the subject *what he is feeling* and receive a substantive answer.

---

## 7.9 THE WIDER HERO COMMUNITY (Adult Heroes At Large)

A brief composite, because the file's evidence is consistent: subject is *cordially shy* with the broader Avengers/X-Men/Defenders adult roster. He has been protected by many of them (Captain America notably gentle in the few panels of direct interaction; Thor's reverence for the child as a being of significance is registered by Franklin as *exactly the kind of attention he is trying to avoid*); he has been saved alongside many of them; he does not relax with them. The exception worth noting is **Wolverine** in select crossovers, where the gruff-protective register reads to Franklin as Grimm-adjacent and produces a comparable somatic ease.

**Charles Xavier** must be flagged separately because of the wounding event: Xavier's denial that Franklin is a mutant, in the *X-Men/FF* crossover material, is one of the few specific dismissive acts by a powerful adult that landed in subject's file as a permanent entry. Franklin did not protest in the moment (consistent with his pattern); he filed it. The wound is not that he is or is not a mutant; the wound is that an authority on belonging-categories *publicly excluded him from one* without apparent regard for the cost. Xavier is therefore catalogued in this file as *not a mentor, despite surface eligibility* — a man who, given the opportunity to extend belonging to a child who needed it, declined. The file rates this as low ongoing salience but non-zero, and notes it is one of the items most likely to surface if subject is pressed in adolescence on the mutant/not-mutant identity question.

---

## 7.10 NATHANIEL RICHARDS (Paternal Grandfather)

**Status: Ambiguous elder. The time-traveler who keeps reappearing.**

Reed's father, the time-displaced Nathaniel Richards, has cycled in and out of subject's life in irregular intervals. The dynamic is *fascinated-cordial* on Franklin's side: he likes Nathaniel, finds him interesting, is treated by Nathaniel as a being of cosmic significance (which Franklin tolerates rather than enjoys). Nathaniel has, on occasion, hinted at futures Franklin will architect, which subject receives with characteristic ambivalence — half flattered, half wishing the man would tal


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*Subject is, across nearly the entire publication record, a child or adolescent. The "lovers" category is therefore thin, latent, and largely prospective — it is included because a total-intelligence file does not omit a domain merely because the present file is sparse; the shape of what is absent is itself information. The "rivals" and "enemies" categories, by contrast, are unusually rich: subject has been targeted, possessed, harvested, or instrumentalized by some of the largest entities in the canon since age four. The following maps each principal antagonist by the same protocol — origin of contact, evolution, what the antagonist wanted from him specifically, his felt response, the trust/safety architecture (where applicable), the failure mode, and the operational leverage either holds over the other.*

---

## I. ENEMIES — COSMIC AND METAPHYSICAL

### Onslaught

**Origin of contact.** The defining adversarial event of subject's childhood, *X-Men/Avengers: Onslaught* (1996). Onslaught — the psionic conjunction of Xavier's shadow and Magneto's rage — identified subject, age approximately six, as the single richest psionic battery on Earth and attempted to harvest him as fuel for a reality-revision of his own. Subject was, in the most literal possible sense, *eaten from*.

**Dynamic.** Onslaught is the prototype of every subsequent psychic predator who has approached subject. The encounter established the pattern that recurs: large entity recognizes subject's substrate, attempts to siphon or possess, is *thwarted not by subject's resistance but by subject's reflex generation of a counter-reality* (the Heroes Reborn pocket universe). Subject did not defeat Onslaught; subject *hid the people Onslaught wanted to kill inside himself*, which from Onslaught's perspective was indistinguishable from theft of the prize.

**Evolution.** Onslaught the entity recurs intermittently (the "Onslaught Reborn" cycle, the X-Men's continuing exorcisms), but for subject the encounter is closed and amnestic — he does not consciously remember it. The *somatic* memory, however, is durable: subject's reflex to externalize threat into pocket-reality is the Onslaught reflex, repeated. Every later use of the Heroes Reborn template is, neurologically, the same circuit firing.

**Trust/safety.** Zero. Onslaught is the wound-pattern, not a relationship.

**Failure mode (subject's).** When a sufficiently large psychic pressure is applied to him with hostile intent, subject does not resist — he *relocates*. The failure scenario is that he relocates the wrong people, or to a wrong place, or that the construction outlasts the threat and becomes a prison.

**Leverage.** Onslaught-class entities can compel subject to act through threat-to-loved-ones. The leverage is asymmetric and bad: there is no negotiation surface; subject's powers act before his ego does.

---

### Mephisto

**Origin of contact.** Mephisto's interest in the Richards children is older than subject — it begins with the harvest of Wanda's children Thomas and William (who become, in twisted form, half of the architecture of subject's own later life via Wiccan/Speed). For subject directly, Mephisto's principal moves are the recurring soul-bid plays of the 1980s and 1990s and the long-arc maneuvers around Reed and Sue.

**Dynamic.** Mephisto is the canonical *bidder* on subject's soul-substrate. He understands what Onslaught understood — that this child is a reality-grade asset — and he understands further what Onslaught did not: that the asset is *protected by love*, which is for Mephisto a familiar engineering problem rather than an obstacle. His method is never frontal; it is the cultivation of Reed and Sue into positions where surrendering Franklin (or something of Franklin) becomes the least-bad option.

**Evolution.** From overt soul-grabs in earlier eras to subtler architectures of loss and bargain in modern usage. Mephisto is patient; subject will be a child for a long publication tail and an adult for longer, and Mephisto plans on that timeline.

**Trust/safety.** Negative. Subject, even as a child, *recognizes Mephisto's frequency* — there is a consistent canonical beat in which children of cosmic substrate (subject, Wiccan, Daimon's kin) feel Mephisto before they see him. Subject's somatic response is withdrawal-toward-Sue.

**Failure mode.** Mephisto's leverage runs through the parents, not through subject directly. The failure scenario is Reed or Sue trading something of subject's away under impossible duress and subject discovering it later — at which point the wound is not Mephisto's act but the parental breach. (Compare §3's discussion of Reed's neural suppression: subject's deepest injuries are intra-familial; Mephisto's strategy is to engineer the next one.)

**Leverage (subject over Mephisto).** Nontrivial, in fact. A fully powered Franklin is a being Mephisto cannot afford to provoke into protective panic. The relationship is therefore a stalking dance: Mephisto plays slow because the child is, on the off-ramp, capable of unmaking him.

---

### Annihilus

**Origin of contact.** *FF Annual #6*, before subject is born. Annihilus's Cosmic Control Rod is the antimatter source Reed needs to save Sue and the gestating child. Subject's natal cosmology is therefore *Annihilus negative space* — he is, by the fact of his being alive, a thing Annihilus indirectly contributed to and has a grievance over.

**Dynamic.** Annihilus has attempted to seize or kill infant/toddler subject more than once (the Negative Zone abductions; the *Annihilation* spillover beats; recurring incursion arcs). The relationship is the cleanest enemy line in the file: pure predation, no theology, no bargain. Annihilus wants subject dead or controlled because subject is, in the Negative Zone calculus, an apex anomaly with a Positive-Matter passport.

**Evolution.** Largely static. Annihilus's interest spikes whenever subject is exposed to Negative Zone operations (the *FF* Hickman-era Negative Zone arcs; subject's involvement with the prison-state Old Man and the bridge to N-Zone politics). Otherwise dormant.

**Trust/safety.** Zero, but stable-zero. Subject treats Annihilus the way he treats weather: a known hostile constant.

**Failure mode.** Subject's Negative Zone exposure has been recurrent enough that an Annihilus operation timed to a moment of subject's depowering (compare the Hickman power-loss arc) would be lethal. Operational watch: Annihilus's activity windows should be cross-referenced with subject's power-suppression intervals.

**Leverage.** Subject powered can collapse Annihilus's domain at conceptual scale. Annihilus knows this. The relationship is, like Mephisto's, a held-breath: Annihilus moves only when he believes subject cannot.

---

### Hyperstorm

**Origin of contact.** *Fantastic Four* DeFalco/Ryan run, mid-1990s. Hyperstorm is the grandson of Reed and Sue through a corrupted future line — descended from subject and a future Rachel Summers, via subject's son. He is, therefore, *subject's possible descendant*, a being whose existence is conditional on a future subject has not lived.

**Dynamic.** This is the most psychologically loaded enemy in the file because the enemy is *kin from a road not yet taken*. Hyperstorm's existence proves to subject (when subject is old enough to process it) that he is capable of seeding a line that produces tyrants. The encounter is brief in pages and durable in implication.

**Evolution.** Hyperstorm is largely retired from active continuity. The psychic residue is permanent. Subject's election to remain a child — see §1's Battleworld kenosis — is *partly* readable as a refusal of the developmental trajectory that produces Hyperstorm-class descendants. He stays small in part because the futures in which he grows are bad.

**Trust/safety.** N/A; antagonist is a descendant in a closed branch.

**Failure mode.** Subject internalizes Hyperstorm as evidence of his own genealogical danger. The failure scenario is not that Hyperstorm returns; it is that subject's lifelong reluctance to step into his adult power is partially driven by an unspoken belief that the adult shape is monstrous.

**Leverage.** None operational. Symbolic only — Hyperstorm is the standing argument against subject's own future.

---

### Galactus (ambivalent — herald-line antagonist, not pure enemy)

**Origin of contact.** Galactus's relationship to the FF predates subject. Subject's specific entanglement begins in the cosmic-future threads (the "Galactus's Herald" adult-Franklin variants) and recurs across the Hickman and post-Hickman cosmologies, where adult subject is depicted as Galactus's companion, partner, or successor in the deep-time recalibration of the universe.

**Dynamic.** Galactus is, uniquely in the file, an enemy who in one possible future *becomes the only entity at subject's scale who can keep him company*. The relationship is bracketed by mutual recognition: Galactus is one of the few beings who looks at subject and sees a peer rather than a child. This is flattering and corrosive in equal measure — it threatens the kenotic self-limitation subject has built his identity around.

**Evolution.** From frank antagonist (early FF Galactus arcs subject witnesses or is endangered by) to ambivalent cosmic uncle (the future-Franklin/Galactus pairings) to potential successor-line entanglement (Hickman-era cosmology). The arc tracks subject's own oscillation between child and god.

**Trust/safety.** Conditional. Galactus does not lie; Galactus also does not protect. Subject can rely on Galactus to be exactly what Galactus is.

**Failure mode.** If subject ever accepts Galactus's framing — *you are my kind; come and walk the deep time with me* — he will have abandoned the relational tethers (Sue, Val, Ben) that constitute his stability per §4. This is the cleanest extant pathway from "Franklin Richards" to "Franklin Richards, the entity we were warned about."

**Leverage.** Galactus offers subject *the only honest mirror*. That is the leverage. Subject's defense is that he prefers crooked mirrors held by people who love him.

---

### The Beyonder / the Beyonders / *Secret Wars*-tier entities

**Origin of contact.** First-tier Beyonder of the original *Secret Wars II* takes intermittent interest in the Richards household; subject as toddler is briefly an object of Beyonder curiosity. The Beyonders proper (Hickman) are the entities whose multiversal incursion drives subject and Reed into the Battleworld architecture.

**Dynamic.** The Beyonders relate to subject as a *peer-substrate they did not anticipate*. The Battleworld build is, mechanically, subject and Reed using subject's reality-substrate to *outlast* the Beyonders' demolition. Subject is therefore the load-bearing column of the most important architectural act in modern Marvel cosmology.

**Evolution.** Antagonism is largely closed by the resolution of *Secret Wars*. The residue: subject knows, durably, that he is the substrate the universe rests on. He has filed this knowledge and continues to behave as a boy.

**Trust/safety.** N/A.

**Failure mode.** Subject's compartmentalization (§3) is what allows him to know what he knows and still go to bed at a normal hour. The failure scenario is that the compartment leaks — that he begins to *feel* the weight of being load-bearing — and the kenosis becomes unsustainable.

**Leverage.** Subject is, in fact, the leverage. The Beyonders learned this.

---

### The Mad Thinker, the Wizard, the Frightful Four (early-era recurrent kidnappers)

**Origin of contact.** Lee/Kirby tail and Thomas/Buscema runs. Subject is taken, repeatedly, by mid-tier antagonists who understand he is the FF's softest point. The Wizard's interest is particular — he repeatedly attempts to claim subject as a developmental project, with the Frightful Four serving as twisted mirror-family.

**Dynamic.** This is the foundational class of subject's enemies and the source of his earliest learned environmental fact: *I am the thing villains take to hurt my parents.* (§1.) Each individual antagonist in this tier is a minor figure; the *category* is constitutive.

**Evolution.** Subject ages past easy kidnap-target status as his power becomes legible; the tier shifts to deception (luring, framing) rather than abduction. The Wizard in particular continues to surface across decades, always with the same proprietary interest in the child he could not keep.

**Trust/safety.** Zero, contemptuous-stable. Subject does not fear this tier; he learned by age four that they are weather, not gods.

**Failure mode.** Cumulative. No single kidnapping broke subject; the *pattern* taught him that his existence is dangerous to the people he loves, which is the seed of the kenotic disposition.

**Leverage.** Subject's protective panic can be triggered by this tier when they go after Sue, Val, or Ben — but subject's response will be wildly disproportionate to the actual threat, which is itself a hazard.

---

### Hiro-Kala and the assorted psychic intruders

**Origin of contact.** *Realm of Kings / Incredible Hulks* era; Hiro-Kala (the dark twin of Skaar, Hulk's son) identifies subject as a psionic peer and target. One in a class of intermittent psychic predators — including various telepaths, possessing entities, and dream-realm operators — who have probed subject's CNS over the years.

**Dynamic.** Class-level antagonism. Each individual encounter is brief; the cumulative effect is that subject's CNS has been, since age four, a contested commons. Subject has developed a quiet psychic immune response: hostile presences are felt before they are seen; subject withdraws toward an attachment figure; if the figure is unreachable, the reality-construction reflex fires.

**Evolution.** Subject's defenses have matured; the encounters have become rarer and less successful. The trait *hypervigilance for others' safety* (§4) is partially psychic-immune in origin: the predator who can't reach subject directly tries the people around subject.

**Trust/safety.** Zero, by class.

**Failure mode.** The cumulative load is real even if individually buffered. Subject's resting CNS state runs at higher alert than is appropriate for a child his age, which presents as the *dreamy watchfulness* readers see in quiet scenes — a thousand-yard stare in a boy who looks like he is drawing.

**Leverage.** N/A by class.

---

## II. RIVALS — INTERNAL TO THE EXTENDED FAMILY

*Subject's rivalries are unusually thin because subject does not contest. The following are the relationships in which a rivalrous structure exists, however soft, and the dynamics around it.*
