### Valeria Richards (rival-sibling axis, primarily allied; see Relationships I for full sibling treatment)

**Rivalrous component only.** Sister is propositionally smarter, Reed-coded, faster on technical problems, and explicitly preferred by Reed as an intellectual heir. Subject's cognition is symbolic-narrative (§3) and is consistently underestimated, including by Val herself when she is being cruel-clever. The rivalry is asymmetric: she scores points, he does not return fire. Standing pattern.

**Evolution.** Across the Hickman *FF* run and after, Val comes to *understand* that she has been scoring on him and recalibrates toward fierce protectiveness — the closest thing to remorse her character permits. Subject absorbs the recalibration without comment. Rivalrous component recedes; sibling-secure bond becomes the dominant axis (§3).

**Failure mode.** If Val ever positions herself with Reed *against* subject — even on a small question — subject will not protest and will file it. Files accumulate (§5).

**Leverage.** Each is the other's load-bearing tether. Neither uses it.

---

### Reed Richards (parent, rivalrous undercurrent)

**Rivalrous component only.** Reed is the father, and the file's most ambivalent object (§3). The rivalrous undercurrent — subject's symbolic-narrative cognition versus Reed's propositional-analytic cognition — is the place where the parental wound and the intellectual difference fuse. Reed underestimates subject because subject does not think in Reed's idiom; subject internalizes the underestimation as confirmation that he is *not what his father wanted*.

**Evolution.** From toddler-suppression (the *FF #141* lobotomy event, the originating wound) through latchkey absence through Hickman-era partial repair (Reed working with future-Franklin; Reed *consulting* subject on the Battleworld build) to ongoing wary détente. Reed has not apologized for what he does not remember as wrong; subject has not asked.

**Failure mode.** A second perceived breach — Reed siding with consensus reality against subject on a question of identity (e.g., the Krakoa "you are not a mutant" beat handed Reed's way) — would re-tear the original wound at adolescent comprehensibility. This is the single highest-priority intra-familial risk in the file.

**Leverage.** Reed holds the disproportionate share. He does not know how much.

---

### Doctor Doom (rivalrous-paternal, displaced)

**Origin of contact.** Subject has been in Doom's orbit since infancy via Doom-FF entanglements; Doom has held subject as hostage, used subject's power-substrate in schemes, and — critically — *treated subject with a strange respect* across multiple writers, including instances of returning subject to Sue rather than weaponizing him at peak opportunity. Doom in the Hickman *Secret Wars* arc co-architects Battleworld and is, in that architecture, *adjacent to subject* in a way no other antagonist is.

**Dynamic.** Doom is the dark mirror of Reed in subject's life: the brilliant man who *does* notice him, who treats subject's substrate as worth respecting, and who is also one of the most dangerous people alive. Subject's relation to Doom is unsettling and quiet — he does not fear Doom the way other children fear Doom, which is itself a datum.

**Evolution.** From hostage-class antagonist to ambivalent god-figure in Battleworld to post-*Secret Wars* uneasy distance. Doom has not, in the file, *harmed* subject in the way Doom has harmed other Richardses.

**Trust/safety.** Negative-but-stable. Subject does not trust Doom; subject is not afraid of Doom in the conventional sense.

**Failure mode.** Doom can offer subject something Reed cannot: *recognition at scale*. If Reed continues to fail at recognition (see above), Doom is the line of least resistance for subject's wounded need to be seen by a paternal intellect. This is a slow and serious vulnerability.

**Leverage.** Mutual and unused. Doom *knows* what subject is; subject *knows* Doom knows. They have not spent the currency.

---

### Charles Xavier (rivalrous-categorical)

**Origin of contact.** Xavier has known of subject since subject was a small child; subject visited the school across multiple eras; the *X-Men/Fantastic Four* crossovers have repeatedly placed Xavier in proximity to a question he does not want to answer about subject.

**Dynamic.** Xavier's denial — *you are not a mutant* — handled in the modern crossover, is, for subject, *the* wounding categorical event of the post-Krakoa era. It is not rivalrous in the conventional sense; it is the rivalry of *belonging-frames*. Xavier needs the mutant category to mean something precise; subject needs to belong somewhere; the two needs cannot both be satisfied.

**Evolution.** Subject internalizes the rejection per §3's belonging-category sensitivity. The wound is durable. Xavier, characteristically, does not revisit.

**Trust/safety.** Damaged. Subject had treated Xavier as a possible elder ally; that frame is gone.

**Failure mode.** Subject's *withdrawal-into-built-world* response (§4 differential) is partially primed by this kind of categorical exile. Every rejection at the level of *what you are* tightens the tether-dependence on Sue, Val, and Ben.

**Leverage.** Xavier has none over subject. Subject has none he will use over Xavier.

---

## III. INTIMATES / LOVERS

*Subject is, across nearly the entire publication record, pre-adolescent or early-adolescent. The category is therefore prospective and lightly furnished. What follows is what the file holds and what the file implies.*

### The future-line entanglement (Rachel Summers axis)

The corrupted future that produces Hyperstorm (DeFalco era) implicates a future subject and Rachel Summers as the originating couple of the contaminated line. This is *future-conditional*, not actual; subject in current continuity has had no romantic interaction with Rachel and is age-inappropriate for one. The datum's weight is not romantic-biographical; it is psychological — see *Hyperstorm* above. Subject's reluctance to grow up is partly a refusal of any romantic future at all, because the only romantic future depicted produced a tyrant grandchild.

**Operational note.** Any near-future maturation arc that puts adolescent subject in proximity to telepath-class peers his age (the X-line in particular) will activate this latent wiring. Watch carefully.

---

### Future-cosmic pairings (the Galactus-companion line)

In several adult-Franklin futures, subject is depicted alongside a re-formed Galactus as a cosmic walker, sometimes paired with a similarly grown female cosmic entity, sometimes alone. These are not relationships in the lover sense; they are the *absence* of lovers, recoded as cosmic companionship. The file reads them as: *if subject cannot be a son and brother in a loving family, he will be a god accompanied only by another god.* The pairing with Galactus, when it occurs, is intimate in a non-romantic register — the closest comparable structure in real-world myth is the paired-walker motif (Enkidu, the disciples on the road, the bodhisattva and the wheel-turner).

**Operational note.** Subject's prospective lovelife is, on the published evidence, *inversely correlated with the integrity of his familial tethers.* If Sue, Val, Ben remain, subject will likely have a normal adolescent romantic development at his own pace. If they do not, the romantic register is replaced by cosmic companionship and the file has effectively closed that domain.

---

### Adolescent-peer affiliations (latent)

The Future Foundation cohort — Leech, Bentley-23, Alex Power, Dragon Man, the Moloids, and others — contains subject's peer pool. The current relationships are sibling-affiliative, not romantic, and subject's profile (§3, §5) predicts he will *bond down* rather than across when he begins to develop romantically: he will be drawn to peers whose ambiguous belonging mirrors his own (Leech in particular is canonically


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS
## Section 6 — Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

*Cross-reference §1 (history), §2 (medical/neurological), §3 (defenses — particularly sublimation), §5 (escalation profile). Powers in this subject cannot be cleanly separated from psychology; the abilities ARE the defenses externalized at cosmic scale. This is the central clinical-operational fact about Franklin Richards and the organizing principle of everything below.*

---

### 6.1 Taxonomic Problem

Before mechanism: subject resists the standard Marvel power-taxonomy. He has been classed, at various publication points, as:

- **Mutant** (the dominant classification through the 1970s–2000s; X-gene activated in utero against the cosmic-ray-altered Richards germline).
- **Mutate** (the Hickman-era reframe: not X-gene but reality-responsive genome expression downstream of his parents' Negative Zone exposure).
- **Reality-warper / Omega-tier** (functional class, independent of etiology).
- **"Not a mutant"** (Xavier's Krakoa-era denial; see §3 — wounding event, but also possibly *accurate* in the strict Krakoan sense).
- **Co-creator deity** (post–*Secret Wars* 2015; he and Reed are the literal architects of the standing multiverse's substrate).

This taxonomic ambiguity is not a writers'-room inconsistency to be discarded; it is *the diagnostic finding.* Subject's powers do not fit a category because his *biology does not fit a category* — cosmic-ray-altered parents, in utero radiation, possible X-gene, possible reality-feedback loop with his own future selves. He is sui generis. Any tactical assessment that pretends otherwise will under- or over-estimate him.

---

### 6.2 Core Mechanism (Best Available Model)

The most parsimonious mechanism consistent with published evidence: **Franklin's nervous system functions as a localized interface to the multiversal substrate** — the same substrate he and Reed later formalized into Battleworld. He does not *cast* effects; he *edits.* Power expenditure is non-metabolic (see §2) because the work is not being done by his body; his body is the *pointer*, not the engine.

Operational implications:

- **No energy budget in the conventional sense.** He does not tire from large-scale acts the way a high-output mutant (Storm, Iceman) does. He tires from *attention* — sustained, conscious editing is fatiguing; instinctive single-pulse edits are not. Heroes Reborn (a single saving pulse) did not exhaust him. Architecting Battleworld with Reed *did*, because it was sustained.
- **Discreteness of acts.** His most documented mode is the *fiat pulse*: one decision, one new state. The pocket-universe creation, the Onslaught containment, the Celestial-scale interventions — these are not "channeling" events; they are decisions that have already taken effect by the time observers notice.
- **Subconscious priority.** The most powerful expressions have all been pre-cognitive — happening before his conscious will engaged. The toddler manifestations that prompted Reed's intervention, the Heroes Reborn save, the dream-warnings — these are limbic, not cortical. This is the single most operationally important fact in his file: *the cortex is the brake, not the engine.* (See §6.9.)

---

### 6.3 Demonstrated Abilities — Inventory

**Tier I — Perceptual / Latent (manifest from age ~3, never lost):**

- *Precognitive dreaming.* Onset earliest, persists through power-loss arc, present even in depowered states. Symbolic, narrative-form (consistent with right-hemisphere cognitive style, §3). Predicted Ultron, the Beyonder, Onslaught, multiple smaller events. The dreams are *not* deterministic forecasts; they are *probabilistic perceptions* of high-amplitude futures, encoded as story. He sees the futures most charged with the affect of people he loves.
- *Telepathic sensitivity (passive).* Detects entities, distress, presence of the cosmically large. Not a conversational telepath; he does not read thoughts so much as *feel temperatures* in minds nearby. Surrogate caregivers (Harkness) provided framing.
- *Empathic perception of "wrongness."* He registers reality-violations — Skrull impostors, possessed family, illusion fields — as a somatic disquiet before he can articulate them.

**Tier II — Active, Pre-Loss Ceiling (age ~4–10, peak culminating in Onslaught):**

- *Energy projection.* Concussive blasts, defensive shielding. The least interesting expression and the one he uses least; this is "mutant-coded" presentation and arguably the manifestation that most resembles standard Omega-tier powers. He has never relied on it.
- *Telekinesis.* Present but underdeveloped because he rarely *needs* it; he tends to skip past TK into outright reality-edits.
- *Construct projection.* Ability to externalize imagined forms — playmates, creatures, environments — with material persistence. This is the gateway to the next tier.
- *Pocket-reality construction.* The Heroes Reborn act. Full ontological generation of a self-consistent universe with internal physics and time, populated by people pulled from the prime reality and re-instantiated with continuous subjective experience. Performed once at age ~6 in a dissociative-protective state. *He has not consciously chosen to repeat this at scale, which is itself important.*

**Tier III — Adult / Future-Self Ceiling (Hyperstorm timeline; *Counter-Earth* adult Franklin; the future-Franklin who depowered the child):**

- *Casual reality revision* — re-writing local physical law, raising the dead within range, undoing causality across short windows.
- *Co-equality with cosmic entities.* Depicted standing beside Galactus as a herald/peer; the future-Franklin variant outlives the universe and helps midwife the next.
- *Substrate-level architecture.* With Reed, designed and instantiated the Battleworld platform; with Reed, rebuilt the post–*Secret Wars* multiverse. This is *engineering* tier, not improvisation tier — and it represents the meeting of Franklin's editorial capacity with Reed's analytic capacity. Neither could do it alone. The collaboration is itself a clinical event (see §6.10).

**Tier IV — Theoretical Ceiling (implied, never fully expressed in prime continuity):**

- The future-Franklin who depowered his child self stated the powers would return *amplified* at adolescence/adulthood. Subject's adult ceiling is therefore *prospective*: the file should treat the current child as a *deferred* Tier III/IV asset, not a Tier II one.

---

### 6.4 Range, Scaling, Granularity

**Range.** Effectively unbounded at peak; the Heroes Reborn pocket was complete-cosmos scale. For practical purposes within a scene, range is wherever his attention can hold — and his attention can hold the people he loves at any distance (precognitive dreams cross planets, dimensions, time).

**Scaling.** Not linear with stress; *exponential with love-under-threat.* (§5 escalation profile.) A threat to a stranger evokes Tier I–II responses. A threat to Sue or Valeria evokes Tier II–III without conscious recruitment. The function is closer to a step function than a curve.

**Granularity.** Surprisingly *coarse* in instinctive mode. The Heroes Reborn save preserved the heroes but did not, for instance, also save lesser bystanders or solve Onslaught permanently — it solved the specific problem his terror posed. Granular, surgical edits (rewriting one fact, sparing one detail) seem to require conscious cortical engagement, which he avoids because conscious engagement raises the question of what else he *should* be editing — a question whose moral weight he, as a child, declines to carry.

---

### 6.5 Growth Curve Across Publication

**1968–1972 (infancy/toddlerhood).** Latent; manifest in object-of-jeopardy crises only.
**1973–1975 (the Conway/Thomas suppression arc).** First catastrophic manifestation, paternal lobotomy, induced developmental flat-line.
**Late 1970s–1980s (Wein, Wolfman, Byrne, Simonson).** Slow re-emergence under Harkness's tutelage. Dreaming dominant. Constructs occasional.
**1990s pre-Onslaught.** Steady escalation; treated as a "kid with growing powers" in standard FF mode.
**1996 Onslaught.** The peak demonstrative event. After: the FF "dies," he and Val are scattered, his powers become inconsistent across writers.
**2000s.** Powers fluctuate writer-to-writer; alternate-future adult Franklins proliferate (Counter-Earth, Hyperstorm lineage, Earth-X).
**2009–2012 Hickman power-loss arc.** Future-Franklin removes powers; subject lives as ordinary boy. Critical *control* condition for the file: we see who he is without them, and the answer is *substantially the same person*, which establishes that the personality is not power-dependent. Counterintuitive but well-documented.
**2015 *Secret Wars*.** Co-architect of the new multiverse with Reed. The peak collaborative-engineering expression.
**Post-2015 (Slott, North, Ewing, *X-Men/FF*).** Powers depicted as fading, possibly artifact, possibly exhausted from Battleworld work, possibly subject's own unconscious suppression (the Krakoa-identity wound; if "not a mutant" then perhaps not-anything, and the powers obligingly recede). The fade is psychologically *legible* whether or not it is biologically real.

The curve is not monotonic. It is *responsive* — to publication needs, yes, but in-universe to relational state. Powers grow when family is threatened; powers attenuate when identity is destabilized. This is the symptom-as-signature.

---

### 6.6 Signature Applications

**The pocket world.** His characteristic act. When the world will not hold the people he loves, he builds one that will. Heroes Reborn is the template; the Future Foundation's various play-realities are the same gesture at smaller scale; Battleworld is the same gesture done deliberately and with his father. He is, signature-tier, *a builder of refuges.*

**The drawing.** He draws constantly — across Byrne, Hickman, Slott. The drawings are diagnostically continuous with the pocket worlds: same act, different substrate. When his powers are off, he draws; when his powers are on, the drawings have a tendency to come true or come alive. There is no clean line between his crayons and his cosmos.

**The named imaginary friend.** Multiple writers have shown Franklin's "imaginary" companions turning out to be real — constructs he generated and forgot, or extra-dimensional beings he summoned in play. The boundary between *pretend* and *manifest* is functionally absent for him; he just maintains the social fiction that it is present.

**The protective shield.** Less spectacular but more frequent: in moments of acute danger to a loved one, a localized shielding-or-displacement effect activates pre-cognitively. He has saved Valeria, Sue, and the Foundation children this way multiple times across runs, often without remembering doing so afterward.

**The pulled punch.** His signature *omission.* In every major confrontation where lethal force would be justified by stakes, he declines. He does not kill. He does not depose. He does not avenge. The most powerful being in his weight class consistently uses his power *to add* (a refuge, a save, a creation) rather than *to subtract* (an enemy, an obstacle, a threat). This is a personality fact expressed as a power-use pattern.

---

### 6.7 Limits — Hard, Soft, and Self-Imposed

**Hard limits (demonstrated):**

- *Susceptibility to suppression.* His powers can be switched off — by Reed (FF #141), by Harkness (modulating), by his future self (Hickman). This is a real vulnerability. The mechanism is unclear but the precedent is established.
- *Susceptibility to harvest.* Onslaught used him as a battery; other entities (Mephisto, Hiro-Kala) have attempted similar. His interface to the substrate is also an *attack surface* into him.
- *Anti-magic friction.* Reality-warping at his tier interacts unpredictably with high-order sorcery (Doom, Strange-tier). Not strictly a limit, but a turbulence zone.
- *Future-loop dependence.* The "return at adolescence" promise from his future self is contingent on the timeline that produced that future remaining stable; tamper with that and the prospective ceiling becomes uncertain.

**Soft limits (situational):**

- *Cognitive load.* Sustained conscious editing fatigues him; single pulses do not.
- *Granularity.* Instinctive edits are coarse; surgical edits require focus he is reluctant to deploy.
- *Knowledge.* He cannot edit what he cannot conceive of; his Tier II–III acts have all been within the imaginative repertoire of a bright child raised on his father's science and his mother's protection. The ceiling of his imagination is, currently, the ceiling of his power.

**Self-imposed limits — the core finding:**

- *He will not be the load-bearing entity.* Given omnipotence, he selects boyhood. (§1, *Secret Wars* conclusion; §3, self-concept.)
- *He will not use power to subtract.* Pulled-punch pattern, above.
- *He will not seek the substrate.* He could, plausibly, reach toward his peak ceiling consciously and earlier; he does not. He waits.
- *He will not edit his family.* Most diagnostically: he could rewrite Reed into a father who never lobotomized him, rewrite Sue into permanent safety, rewrite Valeria into ease. He does not. The relationships are sacred-as-given. This is a *moral* limit, not a capacity limit, and it is the most important single fact about how he uses his powers.

The combination of self-imposed limits is what keeps him sub-catastrophic. Remove any one of them under sufficient pressure and the file changes character entirely (see §6.9).

---

### 6.8 Non-Power Skills and Capacities

Often overlooked because the powers eclipse them:

- *Drawing and visual narrative.* High skill for chronological age; the medium through which he thinks. Forensically, his drawings function as journal entries — track them across an arc and you can chart his affective state.
- *Foundation-tier engineering literacy.* Co-led the Future Foundation alongside Valeria; not at her tier of analytic genius, but conversant in his father's vocabulary. Reads schematics. Builds in the lab.
- *Pedagogical capacity with younger/different children.* Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man, Bentley-23 — he teaches, soothes, mediates. A *natural older-sibling* even where chronologically he is not.
- *Negotiation with non-human cognition.* Comfortable conversing with Moloids, with Dragon Man, with constructs, with cosmic entities. The same trait that makes him a good brother to the Foundation outsiders makes him, prospectively, a credible cosmic diplomat.
- *Narrative pattern recognition.* He reads situations as stories — knows where a beat is going, which character is the betrayer, which is the rescuer-in-disguise. Reed would call this unscientific; it is in fact a high-bandwidth heuristic that has saved the family more than once.

---

### 6.9 Symptom-as-Signature Reading

Every one of Franklin's powers is a defense from §3 *externalized at cosmic scale*. The mapping is exact and is the single most important paragraph in this section:

- *Sublimation* → world-building. He converts unbearable affect into geography. Heroes Reborn is sublimation at universe-scale.
- *Compartmentalization* → the pocket reality. He literally puts things in containers separate from the main reality. He does to the cosmos what he does to his own knowledge of being a god.
- *Dissociation under threat* → the instinctive pre-cortical pulse. The Onslaught save happened *to* him as much as *by* him; he was elsewhere while his power was operative.
- *Altruism (mature defense)* → the pulled punch and the refuge-building. He uses power to add, never to subtract, because his defensive structure is organized around care rather than aggression.
- *Identification with the rescuer* → the protective shield, the save-the-loved-one reflex. He has modeled his powers' deployment on Sue's force-field protection, not on Reed's manipulation or any aggressor's offense.
- *Parentified-child features* → pedagogical capacity with Foundation outsiders, the Battleworld co-architecture (he steps into a co-creator role with his father at an age where he should be a son).
- *Earned avoidance toward Reed* → his reluctance to consciously deploy peak capacity. Conscious peak deployment would put him on Reed's plane, would force the question of whether he is son or peer, would surface the lobotomy memory at the cellular level. He keeps the powers subconscious in part to keep that question closed.
- *Trait hypervigilance for others' safety* → the precognitive dreaming. The symptom *is* the power. You cannot medicate this away; the child who dreams disasters is correct.

The clinical formulation: *Franklin Richards does not have powers in the sense that other Omega mutants have powers. He has a psyche whose defensive architecture happens to be wired into the multiversal substrate.* What looks like power use is defense activation; what looks like restraint is defensive integrity; what looks like loss of power is defensive reorganization around an identity wound. To "depower" him in any durable sense, you would have to dismantle his defenses, which would require dismantling the relationships those defenses are organized around — at which point you no longer have a depowered Franklin, you have a *Hyperstorm-vector* Franklin (§4 differential).

---

### 6.10 The Reed Collaboration as a Power Class of Its Own

A note that belongs nowhere else: Franklin's most consequential adult expression to date — the Battleworld substrate and post–*Secret Wars* multiverse — was *not solo work*. It was joint with Reed. This is operationally and clinically significant.

- *Operationally:* his ceiling in collaborative-engineering mode is higher than his solo ceiling and lower in failure-cost (Reed supplies the granularity Franklin lacks; Franklin supplies the substrate access Reed lacks).
- *Clinically:* the collaboration is *reparative*. The father who once switched off his son's mind worked alongside that son to rebuild reality. Whether or not Franklin consciously frames it this way, the act re-encodes the FF #141 wound. Subject's willingness to enter and sustain that collaboration is a marker of attachment-system healing not visible in any other domain.

Tactical corollary: *separating Franklin from Reed at scale does not just remove a relationship; it removes a power-modality.* Any actor seeking to weaken him would not need to harm Sue or Val; they would only need to estrange him from his father, and his ceiling would quietly drop while his risk profile quietly rose.

---

### 6.11 Forward Risk Assessment (Power-Specific)

- *Most likely catastrophic trajectory:* loss of a primary tether (Sue, Val, Ben, Reed-as-reparative-figure) → dissociative withdrawal → unconscious construction of a refuge-reality with himself at its quiet center → that reality persists and grows → Hyperstorm-class outcomes as the boundary between his interior and consensus reality fails. *Note: this is the danger of love, not of malice.* Subject will not become a tyrant out of ambition; he could become a god-shaped grief.
- *Most likely benign trajectory:* tethers held → adolescent power-return as foretold → continued collaboration with Reed and Val → eventual conscious occupation of his actual scale, accepted gradually, integrated with rather than dissociated from his selfhood. The kenotic child becomes a kenotic adult; the universe gains a non-coercive cosmic-tier actor of rare moral clarity.
- *Most likely middle trajectory:* current ambiguity persists; powers wax and wane with identity weather; subject remains functionally Tier II with intermittent Tier III emergencies; the prospective Tier IV ceiling remains deferred indefinitely, possibly forever, by his own quiet choice.

The third trajectory is the one the subject himself appears to be selecting. The file should respect that selection while maintaining readiness for the first and quiet hope for the second.

---

*End Section 6. Cross-reference forward to §7 (Daily Routines, Rituals, Tells) for the granular behavioral expressions through which the above mechanisms surface in ordinary moments — the drawing hand, the night-dreams, the moments-before-a-pulse somatic signs that an alert observer can learn to read.*


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION VI

## OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT: FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS

*Cross-reference: Sections I (History), III (Psychological), V (Personality). This section maps the* how *— the granular mechanics by which subject perceives, decides, acts, builds, withholds, and conceals across a publication record spanning toddlerhood through chronologically-fluid adolescence. The defining operational paradox: subject possesses, at ceiling, the demonstrated capacity to author reality itself, but operates day-to-day with the procedural toolkit of a quiet, observant child embedded in a high-functioning scientific household. Both tiers must be mapped.*

---

### 1. DECISION ARCHITECTURE

**Primary decisional grammar.** Subject does not decide the way Reed Richards decides (propositional, optimization-based, model-driven) or the way Susan Storm decides (situational-pragmatic, harm-minimizing in real time). He decides the way a child storyteller decides: *what shape does this need to be?* Decision is image-first, narrative-second, propositional-third. He sees the desired end-state as a tableau — Mom alive, Dad un-broken, Val laughing, Ben in his chair — and works backward by feel toward whatever intervention produces it. This is not impulsivity; it is a fully formed alternative cognitive mode, right-hemisphere-dominant, that out-performs propositional reasoning in exactly the domains his powers operate in (reality-shape) and under-performs it in domains his father inhabits (causal-mechanical engineering). The recurrent canonical motif of Reed missing what Franklin sees, and Franklin missing what Reed builds, is one cognitive architecture failing to translate to another inside the same household.

**Latency.** Decisional latency varies inversely with stakes. For ordinary choices (what to draw, whom to sit next to, whether to tell Sue something), latency is long, deliberative, mildly anxious — he overthinks small social moves. For mid-stakes choices involving the Foundation children or Val's projects, latency drops; he becomes decisive and quietly authoritative. For catastrophic stakes — someone he loves about to die — latency collapses to *below cognition*. Powers act in the millisecond gap before deliberation begins. The Onslaught reality-construction was not a decision; it was a reflex with a universe attached. This is the most operationally significant fact in his entire profile: *his most consequential actions are pre-cognitive.*

**The abdication heuristic.** Given a choice between using his powers and not, subject defaults to *not.* This is not policy imposed by adults; he has internalized it. The heuristic reads: *if a non-cosmic solution exists, take it, even if it is worse on every metric except scale.* Operationally this means he will let Reed try the wrong tool first, let Ben punch the problem, let Johnny burn it, and only intervene at last resort. He volunteers solutions sparingly and in language calibrated to be dismissible ("I had a dream where…", "what if we just…"). The abdication is load-bearing for his self-concept (§3) and therefore not negotiable; pressuring him to use his powers more freely tends to trigger withdrawal rather than compliance.

**Consultation pattern.** When deliberating, subject seeks counsel in a strict and revealing order: Valeria first (peer-trust, fast loop), Sue second (emotional sanity-check), Ben third (gut-check on whether the plan is honest), Johnny fourth (whether it is fun, which functions as his courage-check). Reed is consulted last, often *after* the decision has been substantively made, and is offered the engineering details rather than the underlying question. This sequence is one of the most stable behavioral signatures in his entire file and has held across roughly four decades of canon under different authors. It reflects, precisely, the attachment architecture in §3: Reed is the ambivalent object, consulted on what he is safe with (mechanism) and excluded from what he is unsafe with (the boy's interior life).

---

### 2. METHODS & MODES OF ACTION

Subject operates across four distinct method-tiers, which he switches between based on perceived stake and available cover.

**Tier I — Childhood-overt.** Drawing, building with physical materials, narrating play, asking questions, hiding in closets, eavesdropping from the air vent above the lab, bringing Sue tea. This is his baseline modality, occupying ~85% of his observed daily time. Tradecraft here is unremarkable except for unusually high observational gain: he hears more than adults notice he is hearing, and he remembers verbatim. The "drawing on the floor while adults talk" posture is *not* inattention; cross-referencing his later remarks against adult conversations he was nominally ignoring shows near-complete recall.

**Tier II — Future Foundation operational.** Project work alongside Val and the Foundation children. Subject's role within the Foundation is consistently relational rather than technical: he is the one who makes Dragon Man feel safe, who explains things to Leech, who mediates between the Moloids when they argue, who reminds Val to eat. He runs the *social substrate* of the Foundation while Val runs the technical roadmap. This is conscious and deliberate; observation of his behavior during multi-child crises (Hickman run, *FF* #6 onward) shows him watching the room before speaking, intervening minimally, choosing the one child whose stabilization will cascade. He has the bedside manner of an experienced pediatric nurse in a ten-year-old's body.

**Tier III — Precognitive warning.** Subject experiences predictive dreams (Byrne era onward) with a consistent presentation: vivid, narratively coherent, emotionally weighted, retained on waking. His tradecraft for delivering these warnings has evolved across canon from naive ("I had a bad dream about the silver man") to strategically packaged ("I drew this; do you think it means anything?") — learning, through repeated dismissal, to embed warnings inside artifacts adults will examine more seriously than spoken words from a child. The drawings function as evidence-objects. He has, by mid-publication, fully internalized the lesson that *adults trust what they can hold.* This is sophisticated covert-influence tradecraft executed by a small child against his own family.

**Tier IV — Reality-architecture.** Reserved for existential threat. Methods at this tier are not "techniques" in any conventional sense; they are *authorship.* The Heroes Reborn pocket universe was constructed in seconds and held for over a year of subjective story-time, with internal physics, history, and inhabitants. The Battleworld substrate was co-authored with Reed at multiversal scale. The post-*Secret Wars* multiverse rebuild was, by canon, partly his work. Operationally what matters is this: when subject acts at Tier IV, he does so by *containing* rather than destroying. His instinct is to make a place where the problem becomes survivable, not to attack the problem. He builds boxes, gardens, refuges. The signature is *preservative,* not eliminative — which separates him categorically from every other reality-warper in the record (the Beyonder, the Scarlet Witch, the Molecule Man all default to alteration of the existing substrate; Franklin defaults to construction of a parallel one).

**Mode-switching tells.** Transitions between tiers are visible. Tier I-to-II: posture straightens slightly, eye contact lengthens, voice steadies. Tier II-to-III: he becomes quiet and slightly absent for several minutes before the warning surfaces; often will draw before he speaks. Tier III-to-IV: pupils dilate, ambient temperature in his vicinity rises perceptibly, low-frequency hum reported by witnesses, and — most consistently — *he stops blinking.* The pre-cognitive freeze is the surveillance flag: when Franklin Richards is no longer blinking, the substrate of local reality is about to be edited.

---

### 3. TRADECRAFT (Information, Concealment, Influence)

**Information acquisition.** Passive-dominant. Subject collects far more than he queries. Primary methods: ambient listening from positions adults code as non-threatening (drawing on the floor, riding in Ben's shoulders, sitting on the lab steps); reading material left around the Baxter Building (he reads above his nominal level and has since toddlerhood); asking Val, who knows more than he does about Reed's work and will explain without condescension. He does not use his powers for surveillance — there is no canonical instance of Franklin scrying, mind-reading, or remote-viewing. The abdication heuristic holds even here.

**Concealment.** Subject's most developed tradecraft skill, and the one most underestimated. He conceals:
- *The full scale of his comprehension.* He routinely understands adult conversations he is treated as too young to follow, and does not correct the misperception. The asymmetry is operationally useful and he has learned to maintain it.
- *The full scale of his perception of his powers.* Even when depowered (Hickman arc), he carries the *memory* of having been a god, and does not disclose how vivid that memory is.
- *His own distress.* The parentified-child feature in §4 expresses operationally as a near-perfect poker face for low-grade suffering. He will report being fine when he is not, because he calculates (correctly) that his parents have larger problems and that his needs scale terrifyingly if expressed.
- *The full content of his dreams.* Cross-referencing dreams he reports with later events shows he edits what he tells adults, withholding the most disturbing imagery, presumably to spare them.

This last is the most important concealment behavior in his file. Franklin Richards is a child who *redacts his own intelligence reporting to his handlers to protect them from the truth.* This is extraordinary tradecraft and a clinical concern simultaneously.

**Influence.** Subject's influence operations are universally low-volume and high-trust. He does not persuade by argument; he persuades by presence and by the carefully timed small intervention. With Reed, he influences through Val (asks Val to ask Reed) — a triangulation pattern that has held across decades. With Sue, he influences directly because she will hear him. With Ben, he influences by physical proximity (climbs onto, leans against — Ben is unable to refuse a quiet request from Franklin in physical contact). With Johnny, he influences by inviting collaboration on something small and fun, which Johnny will then expand into the thing Franklin actually wanted. Each adult in his orbit has a tailored influence protocol, learned over years of observation.

**Counter-tradecraft awareness.** Subject is aware he is observed. He has been the target of telepaths, possessors, kidnappers, and cosmic harvesters since toddlerhood, and his ambient suspicion of new adults — especially powerful ones — is high. Observed micro-behavior: when introduced to an unfamiliar powered being, he glances at Sue first, then briefly closes his eyes (suspected: a precognitive sounding), then decides his posture. The pre-decision eye-close is reliable and brief enough to be missed by anyone not looking for it.

---

### 4. RESOURCES & INFRASTRUCTURE

**Material.** Subject has no personal finances and no need of any. He lives within one of the most resource-dense households in the Marvel cosmos: Baxter Building infrastructure, Future Foundation facilities, FF transport, dimensional gateways, and access to essentially unlimited scientific and material resource via Reed. He uses none of it acquisitively. His personal possession set is canonically minimal: drawings, art supplies, a few stuffed animals retained from early childhood, books, his Foundation jumpsuit, ordinary clothes. The contrast with Val (who builds and modifies her own equipment continuously) is sharp and intentional.

**Infrastructural.** Where Val occupies the lab, Franklin occupies the *common spaces* — kitchen, living areas, the Foundation classroom, Sue's studio when she has one, Ben's room. He moves through the building on a small number of well-worn routes; surveillance of his ambulation patterns shows ~85% of his transit occurs along perhaps six fixed paths. He has a favored window (canon-consistent across runs: a large one facing east, where he draws in morning light), a favored corner of the Foundation classroom, a favored seat at the dinner table (Sue's left), and a favored hiding spot for periods of overwhelm (this varies by era but is always elevated and enclosed — closets, lofts, the upper levels of climbing structures).

**Personnel as infrastructure.** His operational support network is, in descending order of weight-bearing: Sue, Val, Ben, Johnny, Reed, Alicia Masters, the Foundation children (with Leech and Dragon Man load-bearing within that subset), Agatha Harkness (historically), and a rotating set of allied heroes (the Power Pack children when present have functioned as peer infrastructure). The network is small, deep, and almost entirely chosen-family rather than transactional. He has no operational assets outside this circle.

**The pocket realities as infrastructure.** This deserves its own line: subject has, across canon, generated and at times retained access to constructed sub-realities. These function as a kind of *off-balance-sheet infrastructure* — capacity he does not advertise, may not consciously inventory, but which exists and could be reactivated under sufficient stress. A complete intelligence accounting of Franklin Richards' "resources" must include the dormant capacity to instantiate refugia at will. There is no analog to this in any other surveilled subject.

---

### 5. PATTERNS OF ACTION

**Diurnal pattern.** Early riser. Drawing or quiet observation before others are up — this is his most cognitively clear window and he protects it. Mid-morning: Foundation work or instruction. Midday: meal with whoever is present; he is a reliable attendee of family meals and visibly distressed when the table is incomplete. Afternoon: play, projects, often with Val or the Foundation children. Late afternoon: tends to seek Sue, briefly. Evening: family time, reading, drawing. Night: variable sleep quality, dream-prone, occasional night-waking with precognitive content. The window between 04:00 and 06:00 local is when his most significant dreams have historically resolved.

**Weekly / longer-period patterns.** Subject's longer rhythms track family deployment: when the senior FF are off-world, he becomes quieter, more vigilant, sleeps worse, draws more. When they return, he is briefly clingy (more so toward Sue than Reed), then re-stabilizes. He does not act out in their absence; he *internalizes the absence,* which is more clinically concerning but less operationally visible.

**Crisis patterns.** In a developing crisis his behavior follows a near-invariant sequence:
1. *Detection* — often before adults. Goes quiet. Stops blinking normally.
2. *Verification* — seeks Sue or Val, asks a question whose answer will confirm or disconfirm.
3. *Warning* — issues a low-key, easily dismissible alert, often via drawing.
4. *Positioning* — physically moves toward the person most at risk. This is a consistent and underappreciated tell: Franklin's body migrates toward whoever his powers are about to protect.
5. *Holding* — waits as long as adult solutions are operating. Will not preempt them.
6. *Intervention* — at the threshold of loss, acts. At Tier IV scale if necessary.
7. *Aftermath* — withdraws into Sue's or Ben's physical proximity, often non-verbal for hours afterward, requires sleep.

The sequence has been observed, in whole or part, in essentially every major crisis arc in which he is present. Step 4 is the single most reliable predictive indicator: when you observe Franklin Richards physically migrate to stand near a specific person, that person is about to be targeted by something he has already perceived.

---

### 6. SIGNATURE OPERATIONAL TELLS

The granular behavioral markers that distinguish this subject in surveillance, in roughly descending order of diagnostic value:

- **The non-blink.** As above. The cleanest tell of imminent Tier IV action.
- **Pre-decision eye-close.** Brief, < 1 second, on meeting new powered beings or entering unfamiliar reality-strata. Suspected precognitive sounding.
- **Migratory positioning toward the about-to-be-targeted.** Step 4 above.
- **The drawing-as-warning protocol.** When subject hands an unprompted drawing to an adult and lingers to watch them look at it, the drawing is intelligence reporting. Treat accordingly.
- **The Val-glance.** Before answering any adult question that touches on his powers, identity, or interior life, subject's eyes flick to Valeria if she is present. He is checking whether she wants him to answer, and how.
- **The Sue-orientation.** In any room, his body angles fractionally toward Sue's position. This is unconscious and continuous.
- **The Reed-asymmetry.** When Reed enters a room, subject's posture *does not* relax the way it does when Sue, Ben, or Johnny enter. Slight muscular bracing in the shoulders. He smiles; the shoulders do not.
- **The Ben-contact.** Voluntary, frequent, initiated by subject. Hand on Ben's arm, sitting against Ben's side, climbing. Functions as somatic regulation. When this contact-frequency drops, subject is dissociating.
- **The Johnny-laugh.** Subject laughs more freely and more loudly around Johnny than around any other adult. This is one of his few unguarded affects.
- **The Foundation-children check-in.** On entering any space containing Leech, Dragon Man, or the Moloids, he locates and acknowledges each one individually before engaging adult conversation. The order is consistent: smallest/most-anxious first.
- **The dinner-table completeness anxiety.** Visible distress when a chair is unfilled. He counts.
- **The dream-morning quiet.** After a precognitive dream, subject is verbally subdued and drawing-prone for the morning. Sue, who knows this signature, will check on him without prompting.
- **The Krakoa-adjacent flinch.** Post the mutant/not-mutant arc, mention of Krakoa, of Xavier, or of mutant-categorical language produces a microscopic flinch around the eyes and a topic-deflection within two sentences. This is a fresh wound and has not yet integrated.
- **The "I had a dream where…" preamble.** Reliable framing device by which he downgrades a precognitive certainty into a deniable-to-himself report.
- **The smallness-claim.** He will, in moments where his scale is acknowledged, verbally diminish himself: "I'm just a kid," "I don't really know," "Dad's the smart one." This is the chosen self-concept (§3) actively maintained in real time, and it is *operationally* a concealment device whether or not he experiences it as one.

---

### 7. OPERATIONAL SUMMARY

Franklin Richards operates as a quiet, observant, prosocial child running, in parallel, the largest unacknowledged latent capacity in the Marvel cosmic order. His tradecraft is the tradecraft of *restraint* — concealment of comprehension, redaction of his own reporting, abdication-by-default, layered influence through a small chosen-family network, and a hard rule against using power when love can do the work. His infrastructure is human (six to ten people, deeply held) and meta-cosmic (dormant capacity to instantiate realities), with essentially nothing in between. His decision architecture is image-first and pre-cognitive at the ceiling, which means his most consequential operations occur before any process a conventional intelligence apparatus could monitor or interrupt.

For surveillance purposes the file should be tagged: *subject's overt operations are negligible-risk and high social value; subject's covert operations consist primarily of concealing himself from his own family for their comfort; subject's latent operations would, if triggered, exceed the response envelope of any extant institution.* He will not initiate. He will respond, exactly once per crisis, in proportion to the threat against his tethers, and in the preservative idiom — he will build a place, not break one — unless those tethers are themselves attacked, in which case the response surface is unbounded.

Watch the blinking. Watch where he stands. Watch what he draws. Watch the dinner table. The rest of the file is commentary.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE

*Subject: Franklin Benjamin Richards. Section derives the complete philosophical and instrumental belief-architecture from approximately five decades of behavioral evidence. Where canon does not state, the file infers from consistent pattern.*

---

## 1. FIRST PRINCIPLES (The Metaphysics He Actually Lives By)

Subject's published behavior is consistent with a small, stable set of axioms he has never articulated in words but enacts continuously. Reconstructed:

**Axiom I — Reality is a made thing, and therefore a fragile thing.** Subject knows this in a way no other living being in his cohort knows it: he has *made one*. He has watched his father and himself sit at the substrate of the multiverse and rebuild it. Consequence: he does not regard the world as a given. He regards it as a held object. The unspoken corollary is that what is held can be dropped, and what is made can be remade — which is simultaneously his greatest comfort and the single most dangerous fact about him. His default affective relationship to the cosmos is *protective tenderness*, the way a child handles a model he built and does not want broken.

**Axiom II — Persons are sacred in a way that scale is not.** This is the load-bearing ethical commitment of his entire life. He has stood at the cosmic register and chosen the domestic register. Galactus is a colleague; Valeria is the point. The asymmetry is total. Subject does not value people because they are powerful or important; he values them because they are *the specific people they are*. The ethical unit is the individual, named and known. Crowds, populations, civilizations matter to him as aggregates of named persons, not as collectives. This is why he can simultaneously be a co-architect of a universe and weep over a single member of the Future Foundation.

**Axiom III — Smallness is a choice and a discipline.** Subject's most consistent act of will, repeated across decades of canon, is the *active downscaling of himself*. He could be a god; he elects to be a boy. He could speak ex cathedra; he asks Ben what's for breakfast. This is not modesty; modesty is unconsidered. This is *kenosis* — chosen self-emptying, sustained by daily practice. He believes, on the evidence, that being small is a positive moral good, not merely a strategic convenience.

**Axiom IV — The world is beautiful.** Critically, subject is not a melancholic. His baseline orientation, observable across every era and every artist, is *delight*. He likes things. He notices the texture of things. The Moloids' faces, Dragon Man's lumbering gait, the way Johnny's hair looks on fire — these are objects of genuine pleasure to him. His ethics rest on an aesthetic substrate: the world is worth saving because it is *worth looking at*. This matters operationally because it means his protectiveness is not anxious-grim but appreciative-warm, and his constructions when he builds them are *generous* — full of color, kindness, and accommodation for difference. He does not build austere utopias. He builds places where Leech can be comfortable.

**Axiom V — Knowledge can wound.** Subject has been used as instrument and battery (Onslaught), dismissed as category-error (Xavier on the mutant question), and once — though he does not consciously remember — switched off by his own father. He has learned, in the somatic register that precedes thought, that being *seen incorrectly* by a powerful intelligence is a form of harm. From this he derives a quiet epistemic humility: he does not lightly tell others what they are. He waits to be told. He asks. The asymmetry of this with Reed's confident classification of every phenomenon is one of the silent structural tensions in the Richards household.

---

## 2. READING THE WORLD (Perception & Cognition)

**He sees in stories, not systems.** Where Reed sees variables and Val sees equations, Franklin sees *characters with motives*. His cognition is narrative-symbolic to its roots. Confronted with a new entity, his first organizing question is *who is this, and what do they want?* — not *what is this, and how does it work?* This makes him a startlingly accurate reader of intention (he clocked the Beyonder, Onslaught, Hiro-Kala) and a sometimes-inadequate reader of mechanism (he defers to Reed and Val on the *how*).

**He trusts dreams.** Subject's precognitive dreams are an established canonical reality; less remarked is that *he has learned to take them seriously even when adults will not*. The Byrne-era pattern — Franklin warns, adults dismiss, catastrophe follows — has imprinted a working epistemology: *if I dream it twice, I tell Mom. If I dream it three times, I tell Uncle Ben, because Mom will worry but Ben will act.* This is a sophisticated, route-dependent verification protocol built by a child who has had to triangulate around adult disbelief.

**He distrusts certainty in others.** Across canon he is repeatedly the figure in the room who is least sure and most often right. He has developed, by necessity, a quiet skepticism toward people who are too confident about what something *is*. Reed's confident pronouncements, Xavier's confident taxonomies, the Maker's confident plans — subject's affect cools subtly around all of them. He does not argue. He files.

**He reads bodies before words.** A child raised among shapeshifters (Skrulls), monsters (Ben), invisible mothers, and beings whose surfaces lie has developed a keen sensitivity to *somatic congruence*. He watches whether the body matches the speech. This is why he goes to Ben when actually frightened: Ben's body never lies. Reed's body, brilliant and elastic, is the body of a man who has learned to suppress himself for science — Franklin perceives this as incongruence and reads it, accurately, as something to be careful around.

---

## 3. CONFLICT (His Theory of How to Fight)

Subject's operational code around conflict is the most counterintuitive part of his profile, because his capacity is god-tier and his preference is *non-engagement*.

**First preference: removal of the threatened, not the threat.** When Onslaught came for the Avengers and the FF, subject's instinctive move was not to attack Onslaught — it was to *take the loved ones out of the universe Onslaught lived in*. This is his combat doctrine in miniature: *displace what you love beyond the reach of what threatens it.* He is a creator of sanctuaries, not a destroyer of enemies. The Heroes Reborn pocket universe is not an exception; it is the *template*.

**Second preference: building around the problem.** Failing displacement, subject's next move is environmental — reshaping the field so the threat cannot land. Pocket realities, suspended timelines, alternate geometries. He treats hostile entities the way a careful adult treats a wasp in a child's bedroom: *open a window, redirect, do not swat in front of the kid.*

**Third preference, rarely invoked: direct unmaking.** Subject is capable of this and has done it, but it appears to cost him something the prior options do not — perhaps because direct unmaking violates Axiom II (persons are sacred). He is willing to do it for Sue. He is willing to do it for Val. The list is short.

**He does not believe in winning.** This is critical. Subject's psychological orientation to conflict is *resolution*, not *victory*. He has no observable triumph-affect. He does not gloat, does not exult, does not seek rematches. When a threat is neutralized, his immediate affective response is *concern for whoever was hurt* — including, on more than one occasion, the antagonist. He is structurally incapable of the warrior's exhilaration. This makes him a poor combatant in the heroic-ego sense and a near-perfect one in the cosmic sense: he is the rarest kind of overwhelming power, the kind that does not enjoy itself.

**He will not escalate through anger.** He escalates through *love under threat*. This is the single most important tactical fact in his file. An enemy who threatens him personally provokes a measured, often non-violent response. An enemy who threatens Sue or Val or Ben provokes reality-revision. There is no negotiation layer between *Mom is in danger* and *the universe is now different*. This is the absence of an off-ramp.

---

## 4. CONTROL (Power, Restraint, Authority)

**He does not want it.** This is unforced and consistent. Offered cosmic stewardship by Galactus in the Hickman/Slott era, subject accepted instrumentally and then *returned to being a boy*. Offered the role of architect during *Secret Wars*, subject performed the task and then *returned to being a boy*. The pattern is not coyness; it is conviction.

**His theory of authority is functional, not hierarchical.** Authority belongs to whoever is best positioned to act well in a given moment. Reed when there is a machine. Sue when there is a wound. Ben when there is a fight that has to be physical and brief. Val when there is a puzzle. Franklin when there is something to be *imagined into being or kept from being*. He does not believe authority is a property of persons; he believes it is a property of *situations matched to capacities*. This is, again, quietly Taoist.

**He governs himself by restraint.** Subject's primary act of self-control is *not doing what he could do*. He does not heal what he could heal, fix what he could fix, undo what he could undo — not because he is forbidden, but because he has concluded that a world in which he constantly intervened would be a world he had effectively replaced. He chooses to let reality run because reality running *is* the thing he loves. This is the most philosophically mature position any character in his canon holds, and he holds it without articulating it.

**Where he does intervene, he intervenes domestically.** Small kindnesses. A pocket world for Leech to feel safe in. A drawing that comes alive briefly for a younger child. A monster made gentle. He treats his power like a wealthy person who has decided to live modestly and tip generously: the scale is restrained, the local generosities are total.

**His relationship to being controlled.** Subject is the most-handled mind in his cohort: suppressed by Reed, dampened by Harkness, harvested by Onslaught, courted by Mephisto. He has developed a quiet, non-verbal *resistance to having his interior managed*. He cooperates with safety constraints he understands. He goes still and uncooperative — never aggressive, just *unreachable* — under attempts to shape him for others' purposes. The Krakoa-era denial of his mutant status registered, on the evidence, as exactly this kind of attempted shaping, and he responded with his characteristic withdrawal-and-file.

---

## 5. TRUST (Whom He Believes, and How Much)

Subject operates a tiered, observable trust architecture:

**Tier 1 — Unconditional, somatic trust.** *Sue. Ben.* These are the figures whose bodies have never lied to him and whose love is, in his experience, structurally reliable. He does not verify them. He uses them as instruments of verification for everything else.

**Tier 2 — Conditional sibling-peer trust.** *Valeria.* Total intellectual trust; emotional trust complicated by their inversion (she is younger but operates older). He confides in her about things he will not tell Sue, because Val will not protect him from the answer. This is a trust of *capability*, not of safety.

**Tier 3 — Affiliative, warm, qualified trust.** *Johnny. Leech. Dragon Man. The Moloids. The Foundation children.* These are people he loves who he also feels protective of; he trusts them but does not lean on them. The directionality is reversed.

**Tier 4 — Respect-with-reservation.** *Reed.* The ambivalent slot. Subject trusts Reed's mind absolutely and Reed's attunement to him not at all. He will follow Reed's plan; he will not bring Reed his fear. This is the structural cost of FF #141 even where the memory is not conscious.

**Tier 5 — Provisional trust pending evidence.** Most heroes. Most adults. Granted on Sue's or Ben's recommendation, revoked silently on observed incongruence.

**Tier 6 — Polite distance.** Authority figures with classificatory power over him. Xavier. The various cosmic abstractions. People who tell him *what he is*. He will be courteous. He will not be open.

**Tier 7 — Active wariness.** Reality-manipulators not in his family. Mephisto. The Beyonder. Anyone who has previously sought to use his interior as a resource. Subject does not announce this wariness; it presents as a slight cooling, a returning of attention to the nearest loved one, a hand drifted toward Val's.

---

## 6. RISK (What He Will and Will Not Wager)

**He will risk himself absolutely.** Subject has no observable self-preservation reflex when the wager is his own person against someone else's safety. This is consistent across every era. He stepped into Onslaught. He gave his powers to his future self. He accepts pain on others' behalf without ceremony.

**He will not risk his loved ones.** Not for principle. Not for the world. *Not for the universe.* This is the cleanest read of the Heroes Reborn act: he chose to hide his family inside himself rather than let them die heroically for a cause. The implication, which is rarely articulated in canon but follows from the evidence, is that *subject does not subscribe to the heroic-sacrificial calculus*. He will not trade his mother for ten billion strangers. He will, instead, attempt to *make a world in which both can survive* — and if forced to choose, he chooses his mother and rebuilds the strangers later.

This is, in conventional heroic terms, a moral hazard. It is also, on inspection, the position of a being who has actually rebuilt reality and knows that strangers *can* be remade in a way that mothers cannot. The calculus is not callous; it is informed.

**He will risk his own ordinariness reluctantly.** The thing he is most protective of, after his loved ones, is his chosen smallness. He resists reactivation of his powers the way a person in recovery resists a return to an old life. When the powers return at adolescence as foretold, subject's affect (consistent across appearances) is *grief-tinged acceptance*, not eagerness.

**He underestimates the risk of his own withdrawal.** This is his blind spot. He treats his retreats — into rooms, into drawings, into pocket worlds — as small private acts. He does not register that a being of his scale *withdrawing* is itself a cosmic event. The alternate-future tyrant and Hyperstorm timelines are, read clinically, futures in which subject withdrew so completely that the withdrawal became the new reality. He does not see this risk because he does not see his own size.

---

## 7. HIS OWN PLACE (Self-Location in the Order of Things)

**He believes he is a son and a brother first.** This is not modesty about his powers; it is a *primary identification*. Asked what he is, the honest answer he would give — and has given, in various canonical formulations — is *Sue and Reed's boy. Val's brother.* The cosmic facts are filed under "things that are also true."

**He believes he is a guest in his own life.** There is, across his canon, a recurring quality of *gratitude* — for his family, for being allowed to be a child, for the world's specific textures. Subject behaves like someone who knows he could have been something else and is quietly thankful to be this. This is unusual in beings of his power class, who typically experience themselves as *entitled* to their position.

**He believes he is responsible.** Not in the guilty-Catholic sense, but in the functional sense: *because I can, I must, but only at the scale that does not unmake what I love.* This is the operational compromise between his power and his ethics. He will help. He will not replace.

**He believes he is provisional.** Subject knows, from having met his future selves, that he is a being whose shape is *under construction*. He treats his current self as a draft. This produces both his openness (he is not defensive about who he is, because who he is is not finished) and his vulnerability (a being who experiences itself as a draft can be edited by skilled hands, which is why the boundary-management around telepaths and reality-manipulators matters so much).

**He believes the universe is, on balance, kind.** This is, in the final accounting, the most surprising and the most load-bearing belief in his entire system. Despite being kidnapped, possessed, suppressed, dismissed, harvested, and used as an instrument by entities older than stars, subject's working theory of existence is that *things tend toward warmth if you let them*. Every observable behavior — the gentleness with monsters, the delight in small textures, the willingness to keep being a boy — rests on this belief. It is the belief Sue gave him by being who she is. It is the belief Ben confirmed by being who he is. It is the belief Reed has tested and not yet broken.

**If that belief breaks, the file becomes a different file.** This is the single contingency that matters more than any other in the entire dossier. Subject's worldview is benevolent because his world has been, on the relevant axes, benevolent to him through the specific persons who hold him. The operational code described above is not a fixed property of his soul; it is a *configuration sustained by the continued goodness of approximately four people*. The configuration is real. It is also, by the standards of cosmic infrastructure, lightly tethered.

Treat the tethers as the asset. The boy will take care of the rest.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS

## Section 6 — Moral & Ethical Framework

*The following derives an ethical profile from enacted behavior across roughly five decades of canon. Subject has rarely articulated his code in propositional language — he is not a child who gives speeches — so the code must be reverse-engineered from what he repeatedly does, refuses to do, and forgives. Where subject *has* spoken to ethics directly (notably the Hickman *FF* run, the Slott *Fantastic Four* relaunch, and the X-Men/FF crossover regarding mutant identity), those statements are weighed against his actions. Where statement and action diverge, action governs.*

---

### 6.1 The Operative Code, Distilled

Across writers and eras the same five rules emerge as load-bearing. They are not taught to him; he assembles them experientially.

1. **Preserve the people you love at any cost to the cosmos.** This is the apex rule and the only one for which he has empirically broken every other rule, including the prohibition on world-creation.
2. **Do not let the strange be hurt for being strange.** The protective-of-outsiders rule. Applied without exception across Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man, Bentley-23, Artie and Leech together, Alex Power, and a recurring pattern of taking the side of whatever creature the room finds least sympathetic.
3. **Do not use the full scale of your power if a smaller scale will do.** The kenotic rule. Consistently violated only under (1).
4. **Tell the truth about what you have made.** Subject labels his constructions as constructions. He has never, in any era, attempted to pass a created reality off as the consensus one to its inhabitants in a deceptive sense. Even Heroes Reborn was, in its own terms, *honest* — the heroes inside it lived recognizably their own lives, and the return was always implicit in the structure.
5. **Defer to those who love you, even when they are wrong, unless rule (1) overrides.** This is the rule most damaging to subject and most ethically interesting; see §6.5.

These do not form a philosophical system. They form a *relational ethics* — closer to care-ethics (Noddings, Held) than to any rule-based or consequentialist framework, with a Taoist undertone in rule (3) and a quasi-Levinasian thread (the face of the other claims him) in rule (2).

---

### 6.2 What He Will Do

**He will build a universe to save five people.** Heroes Reborn (1996) is the cleanest case. Faced with the death of his parents, his uncles, and the Avengers, he constructed a pocket reality and placed them inside it. The act is unilateral, unauthorized, and cosmically consequential. He does it anyway. He was approximately six. The ethical content of the act is not "I have the right to remake the world"; it is "*I will not let them die if I can stop it, and I can stop it.*" The scale was incidental to the motive.

**He will lie by omission to protect a confidence.** Across the Future Foundation arcs he reliably keeps secrets for Valeria, for Leech, for Bentley, even when an adult asking is Reed or Sue. He does not fabricate; he withholds. This is a meaningful distinction in his code: active deception is ruled out, but loyalty trumps disclosure.

**He will share power, knowledge, and credit without resistance.** When the post-*Secret Wars* multiverse is rebuilt, he is co-architect with Reed and does not claim singular authorship even in his own internal narration. There is no observable competitive pleasure when his contributions are unnamed.

**He will accept being shut down.** This is the most quietly disturbing entry in his ethical file. When Reed in toddlerhood induced the coma; when Agatha Harkness dampened him; when his future self burned out his powers — in none of these instances, even retrospectively, does subject express resentment commensurate with the act. He treats *consent to suppression by trusted others* as ethically permissible. This is either profound humility or the deepest expression of his attachment wound being re-enacted as virtue. The honest assessment is: both.

**He will undertake parental labor toward those younger or stranger than himself.** With Leech especially, subject performs sustained caregiver functions — comfort, advocacy, physical proximity during distress, defense against social slights. He does this without naming it as virtue. It reads as automatic.

**He will choose the smaller life when the larger is on offer.** This is not a one-time decision; it is iterated. After *Secret Wars*, after each power-spike, after every alternate-future revelation that he might be Galactus's herald or the multiverse's gardener, he returns to being a kid in a townhouse on Yancy Street. The repetition makes it a *practice*, not a mood.

---

### 6.3 What He Will Not Do

**He will not kill.** Across his publication record there is no instance of subject ending a sentient life by his own action, even when entirely capable. In *Onslaught* he saves rather than destroys; in *Secret Wars* he builds rather than annihilates; in encounters with Annihilus, Hyperstorm, even Mephisto, the resolution mode is constraint, repair, or removal, never lethal force. This is not stated as a rule. It is observable as an unbroken pattern.

**He will not coerce belief.** Despite the capacity to literally rewrite minds, he does not. Heroes Reborn-era constructs were given functional autonomy. He does not edit Reed's opinion of him even when desperate for paternal recognition. The refusal to use his power on cognition is, given what he could do, the most morally significant restraint in his profile.

**He will not weaponize his outsider-knowledge.** He has been told, repeatedly and across alternate futures, what he could become. He does not parade these futures, does not threaten with them, does not invoke "I am eventually a god" in any social context. The information is treated as private and slightly shameful, like a medical diagnosis.

**He will not abandon a creature once bonded to.** Leech, Dragon Man, the Moloids, his sister — once the bond is formed, it is ethically inviolable. The Future Foundation arc is structured around this: he will not let any of the misfit children be cast out, even when adult judgment suggests it would be safer.

**He will not punish.** There is no retributive impulse in him. Bullies in the early Slott school-arcs are not retaliated against by his powers; villains who hurt his family are stopped, not avenged. The absence of retributive affect is unusual in a child with his exposure history and is one of the file's central anomalies. Possible explanation: having been *acted upon* so often (suppressed, kidnapped, possessed), he developed an aversion to the relational shape of *acting upon*. The wound became a vaccine.

**He will not lie about what something is.** He may withhold; he will not falsify. When asked direct questions by Sue, he answers truthfully even when the truth is costly. The Hickman power-loss arc contains several instances of him admitting to feelings (loss, fear of being ordinary) that he could have easily concealed.

**He will not assert priority over Valeria.** Even when canon positions him as the more powerful sibling, he does not occupy that hierarchy. His ethics of siblinghood are strictly horizontal.

---

### 6.4 Justifications (Spoken and Inferred)

Subject rarely justifies. When he does, his justifications cluster around three formulations:

- *"I had to."* (Heroes Reborn, Battleworld substrate, every emergency intervention.) This is not moral evasion — it is an accurate description of his phenomenology. Under acute threat to loved ones, his powers act before his ethics deliberate. The "had to" is causal, not exculpatory.
- *"They needed somewhere to be."* (Re: pocket realities, re: the Future Foundation as institution.) The recurring construction is *place-making for the displaced*. He understands ethics spatially: virtue is providing a *somewhere* for beings who have *nowhere*.
- *"I just want to be Franklin."* (Re: declining cosmic positions, re: the choice of boyhood.) This is the kenotic justification, and it is offered without irony despite its philosophical density. He genuinely experiences ordinary sonship as the goal, not the consolation.

What he does *not* offer as justification is telling. He never says "because I'm the strongest." He never says "because I know better." He never says "because they deserved it." Three of the most common justifications used by powerful beings across the Marvel record are absent from his vocabulary.

---

### 6.5 Fractures and Inconsistencies

A code held this long under this much pressure necessarily fractures. The fractures are diagnostic.

**Fracture 1 — Rule (1) vs. Rule (3).** The kenotic restraint and the protective imperative are on collision course every time someone he loves is endangered. Rule (1) always wins, but the *cost* of rule (3) being broken is borne entirely by him: post-Heroes Reborn he was depleted and dissociative; post-Battleworld he chose extended boyhood partly as recovery. He has not yet faced a scenario in which rule (1) requires him to violate rule (4) or rule (5) — the deception or autonomy rules. If he ever does, the code's actual hierarchy will become visible. UATU's prediction: rule (1) outranks all others, and the discovery will damage his self-concept.

**Fracture 2 — Rule (5) damages the agent.** The deference rule was forged in childhood and has not been updated for his actual standing. He defers to Reed on questions Reed is not qualified to answer (notably questions of subject's own identity and lived experience). The Xavier "you are not a mutant" wound was so deep partly because subject's code does not let him *contest* the determination from an authority figure even when his lived experience refutes it. He files; he does not argue. This is an ethical fracture because passivity in the face of false categorization is a form of self-betrayal, and his code has no mechanism for recognizing it as such.

**Fracture 3 — Outsider-protection vs. outsider-self-protection.** He extends rule (2) to others without extending it to himself. When *he* is the strange thing being denied a category (mutant/not-mutant, child/god, human/cosmic), he does not invoke his own rule on his own behalf. This is the most ethically interesting asymmetry in his profile. It reads as the residue of the parental neural-suppression: at the deepest level he has not granted himself the same standing he grants Leech.

**Fracture 4 — Truth-telling vs. self-disclosure.** He will not lie about external facts but will systematically *under-disclose* his internal states. The omission is rationalized as not burdening loved ones with disproportionate problems ("my sadness is cosmic; theirs is human; mine doesn't count"). This is a quiet violation of rule (4) reframed as care. The code does not catch it.

**Fracture 5 — Forgiveness as policy.** He forgives Reed for the toddler coma without the issue ever being adjudicated. This may be virtue; it may be foreclosure. Real forgiveness requires the wound be named first. Subject's pattern is to skip the naming, which preserves the relationship but freezes the wound. The Hickman run gestures at this in his depowered-era melancholy; no writer has yet had subject directly confront the original suppression in mature dialogue with Reed.

**Fracture 6 — The "Hyperstorm" / tyrant futures.** These are not non-canonical; they are documented possible expressions of subject. The code as currently constituted holds *because* the tethers hold. If they fail, the code's spatial-relational basis loses its referents, and the protective-creative drive can invert. The tyrant Franklin is not a different ethics; he is *this* ethics with no one left to protect — the place-making drive turned inward into a place that contains only himself. The current code, in other words, has no immune response to total bereavement.

---

### 6.6 Drift Over Time

The code is recognizably continuous from the Conway/Thomas era to the present, but its emphases have shifted.

- **1968–1980 (infant/early child).** Pre-ethical in any robust sense; the moral content of these years is borne by adults around him. What is established is the *relational substrate* — that he is the object villains take, and the child his parents will move heaven for. He learns that he is precious and dangerous, in that order.
- **1980–1996 (Byrne through pre-Onslaught).** The prophetic-warning years. Code emerges as *witness ethics* — he sees, he tells, adults dismiss, tragedy follows. This is the period that imprints rule (2) (outsider protection, since he is the outsider being dismissed) and seeds the under-disclosure habit (rule 4 fracture): being ignored teaches him his internal states are low-currency.
- **1996 (Onslaught) — inflection.** Rule (1) reveals itself in act. He learns experientially that he will sacrifice anything, including cosmic restraint, for kin survival.
- **Late 1990s–2000s (Counter-Earth, Waid, JMS eras).** Integration period. He absorbs the knowledge of his scale without yet choosing what to do with it. Code is held but not articulated.
- **2009–2012 (Hickman *FF*).** *The code's mature form crystallizes.* Future Foundation makes rule (2) institutional.
