The power-loss arc forces him to discover whether the code holds when the powers don't — and it does, which proves the code is his, not the powers'. The Moloids and Leech become the testing ground for sustained ethical practice rather than emergency response. Most of what we now call "his code" was finalized here.
- **2015 (*Secret Wars*).** The kenotic rule is consciously *chosen* rather than circumstantially obeyed. He has held a universe and elects to put it down. The drift from this point is toward *practice* rather than discovery — he is no longer learning his ethics; he is performing them.
- **Slott/North/Ewing recent era.** The mutant-identity question reopens fracture 3 (outsider-protection asymmetry). Subject's response — withdrawal, rumination, somatic flatness — suggests the code has not yet developed the resource to advocate for himself. This is the open developmental edge. If he is to mature ethically from here, it will be by extending rule (2) to himself, which will in turn require contesting rule (5) where deference has falsified him.

---

### 6.7 Summary Read

Subject's ethics are the ethics of a being who has been acted upon catastrophically and decided, in response, to *not act upon* — to provide rather than impose, to build rather than break, to be small rather than large, to be a place where others can be safe. It is a coherent and unusually mature moral framework, more so than that of nearly any adult hero in the record, and it is held by a child who has chosen to remain a child partly because the framework requires that scale.

Its strength is its consistency. Its weakness is its dependence on the relational tethers that supply the *whom* of the protection. Strip the tethers and the framework has no internal anchor; the same protective-creative drive that built Heroes Reborn would have nothing left to protect and would, on the available evidence (Hyperstorm, tyrant-Franklin futures), turn the place-making inward into a private cosmos.

The code, in short, is good — and it is load-bearing on the same three or four relationships that the rest of the file flags as critical infrastructure. Protecting Franklin Richards's ethics means protecting the people he loves. There is no separating the two; he has not built his morality to be portable.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7
## Communications & Linguistic Profile: FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS

*Cross-referenced against ~55 years of recorded dialogue, from the pre-verbal babble panels of the Lee/Kirby tail through the most recent North and Slott renderings. Patterns persist across writers with unusual stability, which is itself a finding: Franklin's voice is one of the most consistently rendered child voices in the entire Marvel corpus, and the consistency itself is data.*

---

### 1. BASELINE REGISTER

Subject's baseline speech is **soft-volume, slightly breathy, upward-inflected**, and **lexically simpler than his conceptual range**. Across decades and writers, Franklin reliably speaks several grade levels below his demonstrated cognition. He says "the bad place" when he could say "the Negative Zone"; he says "the man with the purple face" when he could say "Galactus." This is not deficit. This is a *registered choice* — a linguistic instantiation of the kenotic self-limitation that organizes his personality. He speaks small to stay small.

The signature contour is **declarative softened by qualifier**: "I think maybe…", "It's kind of like…", "I don't know but…". Even when he is delivering a precognitive warning of planetary-scale consequence, the syntax stays hedged. Compare the canonical Byrne-era utterances ("Daddy, the bad dream is coming back") to the Hickman-era statements ("Something's wrong with the sky, I think"): same architecture, fifteen years apart, four writers in between. The hedge is constitutive, not developmental.

**Volume.** Quiet across nearly all contexts. Raises voice only in two situations: (a) calling for Sue across distance; (b) protesting on behalf of someone smaller (Leech, the Moloids, a Future Foundation outsider being dismissed by an adult). He has, on record, *never* raised his voice for himself.

**Pacing.** Slow-medium. Pauses mid-sentence to look at the speaker's face. Frequently lets sentences trail rather than terminate — the unfinished sentence is one of his three most-used grammatical structures. The trailing is not anxious; it is *inviting*. He leaves a verbal door open for the other person to walk through.

---

### 2. CONTEXT-SPECIFIC REGISTERS

Subject runs **at least five distinguishable registers**, switching cleanly by interlocutor. Code-switching is fluid and largely unconscious.

**With Sue.** Most regressive register. Reverts to childhood diminutives ("Mommy" persists far past the age at which most boys drop it; "Mom" only when others are present whom he wants to perform maturity for). Sentence length shortens. Tactile cues accompany speech — he speaks while leaning into her, while touching her sleeve. Affect-leakage is highest here; he will *cry mid-sentence with Sue* in a way he will do with no one else, and the crying does not stop the sentence — he keeps talking through it. This is the register of his deepest safety.

**With Reed.** Most controlled register. Sentences become more complete, syntax tightens, hedges drop slightly (he is performing competence). Vocabulary stretches upward — he will reach for a "bigger" word here than anywhere else, and occasionally overreach. He answers Reed's questions *literally* rather than associatively, mirroring Reed's own communicative style. Critically: **he asks Reed fewer questions than he asks any other family member.** This is the most diagnostic single fact in his communication profile. Children typically *flood* a parent with questions; Franklin filters his. He has, somewhere below conscious access, learned that the cost of a wrong question to Reed is a recalibration he cannot bear.

**With Valeria.** Sibling-register: looser, slightly bickering, capable of irritation that surfaces nowhere else. With Val he will say "no" flatly, will roll his eyes, will deploy the only sarcasm in his repertoire ("Oh, *sure*, Val, that'll work"). This is his *least guarded* register and therefore the most psychologically valuable — Val gets the unfiltered voice. He also code-switches *toward* her cognitive style when discussing her projects, picking up technical vocabulary he otherwise refuses to use, as a gesture of respect.

**With Ben Grimm.** Warm-jocular register. Picks up traces of Ben's Yancy Street cadence ("yeah" instead of "yes", clipped consonants, an occasional dropped 'g'). Calls him "Uncle Ben" without irony or self-consciousness. Uses Ben as a target for the small, safe complaints he will not voice to his parents ("Dad's being weird again," "Mom won't let me…"). Ben is his licensed pressure-valve, linguistically.

**With Johnny.** Play-register. Higher energy, more interjections, mock-formal teasing ("Uncle *Johnny*, that is not how it works"). The only register in which he is reliably *funny* on purpose. Johnny is also the family member he is most likely to interrupt — a freedom he extends nowhere else.

**With Leech, the Moloids, and "outsider" children.** Caretaker register. Slows further. Pitch *softens* rather than raising into condescending baby-talk — a notable refusal of the standard adult-to-strange-child mode. Uses their names often. Asks them questions and *waits* for answers past the social comfort point. This register is the most morally legible of all his speech behaviors and the strongest evidence for the prosocial-altruism reading in §3 of the main file.

**With adult heroes outside the family (Spider-Man, the X-Men, Avengers).** Politely diminished register, with a slightly *performed* childhood — he plays the small boy harder for strangers than he is when alone, because the small-boy role is the cover under which he prefers to operate. Observe him with Spider-Man specifically: he is more "kid" with Peter than he is with Ben, and Peter is not closer to him than Ben. The register is strategic.

**With Doom.** Sui generis. Subject has, on multiple recorded occasions, addressed Doctor Doom with a strange flat candor — no hedging, no softening, near-adult sentence structure. He is one of the few interlocutors who pulls Franklin's *god-voice* up through the boy-voice. This is mutually recognized; Doom registers it. The mechanism appears to be that with Doom, the pretense of being only a child is futile, so the pretense is dropped.

---

### 3. DICTION & LEXICAL TELLS

**High-frequency words.** "Maybe." "Kind of." "Sort of." "I think." "I don't know but—". "Like." "Just." All hedges. Combined, these account for an unusually high percentage of his recorded utterances.

**The word "just."** Diagnostic. "I just wanted to—" "It's just that—" "I just thought maybe—" "Just" is his preferred minimizer. He uses it to make his own desires sound smaller than they are. Frequency of "just" rises sharply when he is asking for something he believes he should not need.

**Names and address-terms.** Calls his father "Dad" in public and to his face; refers to him as "my father" in third-person reference to outsiders — a slightly formal distancing. Calls his mother "Mom" publicly and "Mommy" in private/distress. Calls Valeria "Val" (never "Valeria" except when annoyed; "Valeria" *is* the irritation marker). Calls Ben "Uncle Ben." Calls Johnny "Uncle Johnny" or sometimes simply "Johnny" — the only family elder he is licensed to first-name. Strangers and acquaintances: "sir," "ma'am," unprompted. This is preserved across writers and is a tell about how Sue raised him.

**Abstract vocabulary, withheld.** He demonstrably knows the words "multiverse," "incursion," "Celestial," "omega-level." He almost never uses them in dialogue. When he does, it is a marker — *he has dropped the boy-register on purpose*, and the listener should attend to whatever immediately follows.

**Drawing-vocabulary.** He talks about his drawings often, and the talk is *technically specific* in a way his other speech is not — colors named precisely, spatial relations articulated. Art is the one domain in which he uses adult-precision language as a child, because it is the one domain where he experiences himself as an unambiguous authority.

**Made-up words and proper nouns.** Frequent. He names things — pocket worlds, imaginary creatures, drawn characters — and the names are consistently *short, two-syllable, soft-consonant* ("Tatterdemalion" types are *not* in his naming repertoire; his names sound like "Pibby," "Glun," "the Nowhere"). The naming pattern is a tell that the creative process is *affective* rather than analytic — names come from sound-feel, not concept.

---

### 4. RHETORICAL STRUCTURES

**The hedged warning.** His most important rhetorical form, and the one his family has historically failed to read correctly. The structure: *qualifier + sensory-soft image + trailing terminus.* "I think maybe something's coming, it feels like the sky is bending, I don't know—". A literal-minded listener (Reed) parses this as a child's confusion. A trained listener parses *the affect under the qualifiers* and registers it as a precognitive alert at confidence ≥0.8. **The hedges are protective scaffolding, not uncertainty markers.** Subject downgrades his own claims because he has been disbelieved and has learned that confident assertion from a child reads as fantasy, whereas hedged assertion sometimes survives adult scrutiny. This is a learned communicative adaptation to chronic dismissal.

**The narrative answer.** Asked a direct question, Franklin frequently responds with a *small story* rather than a proposition. "How are you?" → "I had a dream where the cat was on the roof and it was raining and I couldn't reach it." This is right-hemisphere/symbolic cognition (§3) externalizing into discourse. He thinks in narrative and answers in narrative. The story is the answer; one must decode it. The cat-on-roof story is not evasion. It is a precise emotional report rendered in image.

**The offered-out.** When in conflict, he will frequently propose an exit for the other party: "We don't have to talk about it." "It's okay if you can't." "You can say no." He hands the other person their own freedom-to-disengage *before* they have to ask for it. This is partly courtesy and partly preemption of rejection — by offering the out, he avoids being handed one.

**Apology pattern.** Apologizes quickly, often, and for things that are not his fault. "Sorry" frequency is high. Combined with "just," this constructs the *small-footprint speech profile* that is the surface of his self-limitation.

---

### 5. HOW HE COMMUNICATES LOVE

Rarely through declaration. He does not say "I love you" with high frequency, and when he does it is in childhood-licensed contexts (bedtime, parting, danger). Instead, love is communicated:

- **By proximity-narration.** He tells you what he is doing while sitting next to you. "I'm drawing a horse. The horse is purple. It's purple because—" This is bid-for-connection in Gottman terms; the content is incidental, the *being-near-and-speaking* is the message.
- **By gift of made object.** He draws things and gives them. The drawings are the most reliable love-token in his repertoire. Recipients: Sue (most), Val (steady), Ben (consistent), Reed (notably fewer — and the Reed drawings tend to be *of* Reed, as if attempting to fix his father in place by image).
- **By name-use.** Says the loved person's name more often than necessary in conversation. Frequency of name-use is one of the most stable affection-meters in his speech.
- **By imitation.** Adopts the loved person's verbal tics in small, unconscious ways. Picks up "yeah" from Ben. Picks up "actually" from Reed when he is in a Reed-approval phase. Picks up Val's slight precision-tic on technical vocabulary.

---

### 6. HOW HE COMMUNICATES GRIEF

Grief presents as **lexical thinning**. Sentences shorten. Hedges drop because the energy to hedge is gone. The voice does not break — it *quiets*. He does not weep loudly except in Sue's presence; with others he weeps *silently while continuing to talk*, which is one of his most distinctive somatic-linguistic signatures and one of the most painful to witness. The grief-marker to watch for is the **single-word answer** from a child who is otherwise narrative-volubile: "yeah." "okay." "nothing." When Franklin gives a one-word answer, he is in active distress, and the rule across all his attachment figures should be: *do not press the word, sit beside the silence.*

A second grief-marker: **return to drawing without narration.** He draws constantly, but normally narrates what he draws. When he draws without speaking, something is wrong. The image itself becomes the only utterance.

A third: **prayer-like fragments.** Under acute grief he has produced, on at least three recorded occasions, half-articulated wishes addressed to no specified listener ("please let her be okay"; "please just this once"). These are not religious; they are the residue of a being who *can* answer his own prayers refusing to do so. The fragment is the sound of restraint holding.

---

### 7. HOW HE COMMUNICATES THREAT

**He almost never does.** This is its own finding. A child capable of unmaking continents has, across five decades, issued perhaps a half-dozen recorded threat-utterances, all of them protective rather than aggressive ("Don't hurt her"; "Stop it"; "Leave them alone"; "Go away"). None contain profanity. None contain elaboration. The threat-voice is *shorter and lower* than the baseline voice — a downshift in pitch and word-count that is the surest auditory signal that his powers are about to act.

**The pre-ignition signature.** Before a power-event, his speech displays a recognizable pattern:
1. A sharp inhale.
2. A short, flat declarative — usually a single clause, often containing the loved one's name.
3. Silence.

Step 3 is the danger. If after the short declarative he goes quiet and the air around him shifts, the conversation is over and a reality-event is beginning. Any operator dealing with Franklin must learn this three-beat structure cold. **Do not fill the silence with a question. Remove the threat from his sightline if you can; if not, get out of the structure-being-rewritten.**

---

### 8. DEFLECTION LANGUAGE

He deflects rarely and obviously. He is not a skilled liar. Tells include:

- **The change-of-subject via drawing.** Asked something he does not want to answer, he will look down at whatever he is making and describe it instead. "I made the wings bigger this time, see?"
- **The deferral upward.** "You should ask Dad." "Mom would know." Used to escape questions about himself, particularly identity-questions.
- **The literal answer to a non-literal question.** "How are you?" → "I had cereal." Childlike, but in his case strategic — answering the surface to avoid the depth.
- **The qualifier flood.** When uncomfortable, hedges multiply: "I mean, I think, maybe, kind of, I don't know, just—". When the hedge-density rises above baseline, he is dodging.
- **The retreat into proper-noun world-building.** Will pivot to describing a pocket world or invented creature when the live question is about himself. The pivot is so charming it usually succeeds in deflecting the adult conversational partner — which is its function.

He does not lie outright. He has, on record, *misled by omission* (not telling Sue about a dream because he did not want her frightened), but he does not construct false propositions. Asked a direct question by someone he respects, he answers truthfully or refuses to answer — there is no third option in his repertoire. This is a rare and stable trait.

---

### 9. WRITTEN AND DRAWN COMMUNICATION

His handwriting (visible across Future Foundation documents, classroom panels, drawings in *FF* and *Fantastic Four* runs) is **round, large, soft-pressured**, with letter-forms typical for chronological age. He writes his name with the F and R enlarged and the rest condensed — a stable signature-style preserved across writers/artists, which suggests an intentional pattern.

His drawings are **content-revealing**: family figures recur, with **Sue most often centrally placed, Reed often at the edge or partially occluded, Valeria adjacent to himself, Ben oversized, Johnny in motion.** The compositional grammar is consistent. Reed at the edge is the most quietly damning piece of evidence in his entire file about the Reed relationship; the boy who has every other family member in the foreground keeps his father in the margins.

He labels his drawings with short, often misspelled captions. The misspellings are age-appropriate and *not* corrected when others point them out — he prefers his own spellings. This is the only domain in which he displays anything like stubbornness.

---

### 10. PARALINGUISTIC AND SOMATIC LINGUISTIC TELLS

- **Eye-contact:** sustained with safe figures, dropped with Reed under praise (he cannot accept praise from his father while looking at him), variable with strangers.
- **Head-tilt:** characteristic 10–15° tilt when listening, more pronounced when he is taking someone seriously. Absence of the tilt indicates he has stopped attending.
- **Hand-position:** speaks with hands often in front of him, occasionally fiddling with a drawing implement or a small object. When the hands go still, attend — stillness in his hands precedes the pre-ignition pattern (§7).
- **The breath-hitch.** A small intake before a difficult sentence. Reliable marker of effortful disclosure.
- **The smile-after-difficult-statement.** He frequently follows a hard truth with a small, apologetic smile — *softening the impact for the listener.* It is not a smile of pleasure; it is a smile of care for the person who has to hear what he just said. Diagnostic of the parentified-child features noted in §3.
- **The look at Sue.** Mid-conversation, in any group containing his mother, he will glance at her face roughly every 20–40 seconds. The glance is unconscious. It is the most reliable single tell of his attachment hierarchy.

---

### 11. SUMMARY

Franklin Richards speaks like the boy he has chosen to be, in a voice that is consistently smaller than his mind and consistently softer than his power. His linguistic profile is the surface expression of his kenosis: he hedges, he diminishes, he hands out exits, he draws rather than declares. The voice is genuine — he is not performing childhood, he is *inhabiting* it — but it is also load-bearing scaffolding around a being whose unhedged voice could rewrite physical law.

The two utterance-classes any operator must learn to recognize are: **(a) the hedged warning**, which is precognition disguised as confusion and must be taken seriously despite its qualifiers; and **(b) the pre-ignition three-beat** (sharp inhale, short flat clause, silence), which is the auditory shape of imminent reality-event and must be treated as the most consequential sound in the room.

He says "just" too often. He says his mother's name too often. He says his father's name too rarely. When he goes quiet, listen harder. When he draws without narrating, sit down beside him. When he asks if you are okay, answer truthfully — he can tell.

*— UATU, §7 of file. Continued in §8: Daily Patterns, Routines & Ritual.*


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Forward-projections of granular behavior in unobserved everyday situations, derived from the canon-substantiated pattern set in §§1–5. Each entry follows GIVEN → EXPECT: the operative stimulus or context, then the predicted response with substantiation. Predictions are calibrated to the subject's chosen developmental position (boyhood) and his demonstrated defensive-creative architecture.*

---

## A. Morning, Domicile, Pre-School Hours

**GIVEN** the subject waking in the Baxter Building (or post-Krakoa equivalent residence) on an ordinary weekday → **EXPECT** the following sequence: he wakes before his alarm by four to seven minutes (precognitive-adjacent ambient sensitivity, low-grade, persistent — substantiated by the dream-warning pattern from the Byrne era forward); he lies still for ninety seconds to two minutes before rising, scanning ambient sound for the location of his mother (auditory triangulation, attachment-driven, the somatic residue of a childhood of repeated kidnappings); he checks for Valeria's footfall or door-state before his own breakfast (parentified-sibling protocol). If Sue's voice is not audible within the first six minutes of waking, he will physically locate her before he eats. He will not articulate this need; he will simply route through her room or the kitchen.

**GIVEN** a morning Reed is absent (lab overrun, off-world, Negative Zone) → **EXPECT** subject to ask after him precisely once, in the flattest possible tone, then change subject. He will not press. He will be observably brighter at breakfast than on mornings Reed is present and distracted, because *absent-Reed* is a stable category and *present-but-elsewhere-Reed* is the ambivalent one. This is the avoidant signature: the parent who is physically there but cognitively gone is the harder stimulus, because it reactivates the original injury (the father who decided his son was a problem to be solved).

**GIVEN** Ben Grimm at the breakfast table → **EXPECT** a visible postural settling within the first ten seconds of subject entering the room: shoulders down, breath slower, more verbal output, more eye contact. Ben is, in clinical terms, his secondary attachment regulator, and the body knows it. He will sit closer to Ben than to anyone else if seating is unassigned. He will reliably finish more food on Ben-mornings than on Ben-absent mornings.

---

## B. Wardrobe, Grooming, Somatic Habit

**GIVEN** free choice of clothing → **EXPECT** durable, soft-handled garments in primary colors with a marked preference for the FF "4" insignia, worn without irony or performance — *because his family is his cosmology and he wants to be visibly of it*. He resists novelty wardrobe (new fabrics, stiff collars, anything that constrains the shoulders). Notable tic: he tugs the hem of his shirt down with both hands when self-conscious, a gesture stable across artists and decades.

**GIVEN** unstructured grooming → **EXPECT** indifference to hair (cowlick persists across runs and is not styled away), but unusual fastidiousness about hands — he washes them before he draws and before he eats, and he checks them when he's thinking. The hand-attention is a power-era residue: the hands are the felt locus of his constructive capacity, and he treats them with a faint, unconscious ritual respect even in depowered eras.

**GIVEN** he is told to dress up (formal event, press, Avengers function) → **EXPECT** quiet compliance, no negotiation, and a small ritual of pulling the collar away from his neck three or four times in the first hour. He does not enjoy being looked at as a phenomenon. Formal attire is, for him, the costume of being a *Richards*, and the Richards name is the part of his identity he is least sure he owns.

---

## C. Meals & Food Behavior

**GIVEN** a family meal with all four Richardses and Ben present → **EXPECT** subject to eat steadily, listen more than he speaks, and prompt Valeria with small openings when she is being talked over by Reed (a sibling alliance behavior, consistent with the Hickman Foundation portrayal). He will not interrupt Reed. He will eat what is in front of him without comment unless asked.

**GIVEN** a meal with only Sue and Val → **EXPECT** subject is at his most verbal: stories, what he drew, what he dreamed. The exclusion of the Reed-pressure environment unlocks his narrative output. Sue knows this and writers have intermittently caught it (Slott domestic scenes); a surveillance file would log it as a measurable verbal-output delta.

**GIVEN** the chance to feed the Future Foundation children (Moloids, Dragon Man, Bentley, Leech) → **EXPECT** subject will serve others before himself, will check Leech's plate twice, and will sit beside whichever child is most upset that day without commenting on it. Caretaker behavior is unprompted and unperformed. He will eat less on FF-mealtimes than on Richards-only mealtimes because the caretaker role displaces his own appetite — a classic parentified-child marker.

**GIVEN** food he dislikes → **EXPECT** he eats it anyway, without complaint, and quietly accepts a second helping if offered, because refusal feels disproportionate to the cosmic stakes he has been calibrated by. He will not assert food preferences. This is the *needs-suppression* pattern from §3 expressed at the dining table.

---

## D. Schooling, Tutoring, Intellectual Routine

**GIVEN** a math or hard-science tutorial led by Reed → **EXPECT** dutiful attention, decent performance, no enthusiasm, and a glance toward Valeria roughly every ninety seconds — partly seeking her steadiness, partly checking that she is being seen. He will *deliberately* answer slightly below his ceiling on Reed-led sessions, so that Val's brilliance reads clean. This is not insecurity; it is generosity calibrated by long observation of how Reed lights up at Val's answers. He has decided his sister's relationship with their father is worth more than his own performance.

**GIVEN** a humanities, art, or narrative-led tutorial → **EXPECT** sustained focus, original output, and questions that travel sideways rather than up — he will ask about the mapmaker rather than the map, the inventor of the alphabet rather than the alphabet. Right-hemisphere/symbolic cognition dominant, per §3. He invents characters who recur across drawing sessions; he assigns them coherent biographies; he remembers them weeks later.

**GIVEN** a test or evaluation → **EXPECT** mild somatic stress (the hand-check, the shirt-hem tug), competent performance, and noticeable underclaiming when discussing the result afterward.

---

## E. Play, Solitude, Imaginative Routine

**GIVEN** unstructured solo time → **EXPECT** drawing, first; building (blocks, modeling, Foundation-tech tinkering), second; reading, third. The drawings will be populated worlds: continents, civilizations, characters with names. The names will be invented but phonologically consistent within a given world — he runs an internal language-feel without knowing the term *conlang*. **This is sublimated reality-warping.** The pocket universes he once made instinctively are now made on paper. A surveillance file would note that he produces, conservatively, three to six pages of populated cartography per week, and that he keeps them in a stack he does not show anyone unless directly asked.

**GIVEN** an interruption to solo creative time → **EXPECT** immediate, uncomplaining transition to the interrupter's need, and *no return* to the work that day. Once a creative state is broken, he treats it as ended. The drawings accumulate because he never revisits, only adds.

**GIVEN** the question "can I see what you're drawing?" from Sue → **EXPECT** instant disclosure, narration of who the characters are, evident pleasure. From Reed → **EXPECT** the page turned over and a redirect ("just doodling"). From Val → **EXPECT** disclosure with editorial input invited. From Ben → **EXPECT** disclosure plus a request that Ben pick a favorite character, which Ben will be expected to remember next time.

---

## F. Sleep, Dream, Nocturnal Pattern

**GIVEN** ordinary sleep → **EXPECT** vivid dreams nightly, recalled in fragments, occasionally precognitive in the low-frequency Byrne-era manner (warnings, images, faces he has not yet met). He does not report most dreams. He reports the ones that frighten him, and he reports them to Sue, not Reed — because Reed once treated his dreaming as a clinical phenomenon and Sue treats it as her son's experience.

**GIVEN** a nightmare → **EXPECT** he goes to Sue's room or to Val's, depending on which is closer and on whether Reed is present. He will not wake Reed. If both Sue and Val are unavailable, he will go to Ben if Ben is in the building; failing that, he will sit up and draw until tired again. He does not return to sleep alone after a nightmare — a behavior consistent with the latchkey-cosmic-childhood substrate.

**GIVEN** a recurring dream → **EXPECT** he begins drawing it before he discusses it. The drawing functions as both processing and warning system. A trained observer would learn to read the sketchbook as an early-warning seismograph.

---

## G. Social Encounters — Peers, Strangers, Public

**GIVEN** introduction to a new child his apparent age → **EXPECT** soft-affect friendliness, an offered hand or small object (toy, drawing), and a withdrawal-to-listening posture within two minutes — he will let the other child lead. He bonds *down*, per §5: easier with the less powerful, the stranger-looking, the more outsider-coded. A new child who is shy or socially awkward will receive his full warmth within minutes. A new child who is socially dominant will be met with polite, mildly opaque pleasantness.

**GIVEN** a stranger in public who recognizes him as "the Richards boy" → **EXPECT** a small, reflexive step toward the nearest familiar adult, a polite nod, minimal verbal output, and a faint shoulder-rounding. He does not perform celebrity. He has never internalized the family as famous; he has internalized the family as *his*, and being recognized is an intrusion of the cosmic register into the boyhood register he has chosen.

**GIVEN** a child who asks him directly "is it true you can do anything?" → **EXPECT** a beat of silence, then a deflection that does not lie — typically reframing the question ("my dad's the one who builds the rockets," or "my sister's the smart one"). He will not confirm and will not perform a denial. The deflection is the cleanest tell of the chosen self-limitation: omnipotence is a fact he has filed, not a fact he discusses.

**GIVEN** a bullying interaction directed at himself → **EXPECT** quiet, non-escalatory withdrawal, no retaliation, no report to adults unless the bully repeats. **GIVEN** a bullying interaction directed at Val, Leech, or another FF child → **EXPECT** immediate, calm, verbal intervention, body placed between bully and target, and a focused expression that an observer would catalogue as the *protective-panic precursor*. Powers will not ignite at the schoolyard scale, but the regulatory threshold lowers. Adults should de-escalate the bully not because of the bully's behavior but because of subject's affective trajectory.

---

## H. Encounters with Adult Heroes / Family Friends

**GIVEN** Johnny Storm enters the room → **EXPECT** immediate brightening, physical proximity, willingness to be teased, and a roughhouse tolerance markedly higher than with any other adult. Johnny is uncle-as-peer; the relational register is play, and play is subject's native medium. He will laugh more in ten minutes with Johnny than in an hour with most adults.

**GIVEN** Spider-Man (Peter Parker) in a domestic context → **EXPECT** quick rapport, comfort, a sense that Peter is also bonded *down*-easier than *up*-easier — they recognize each other.

**GIVEN** Doctor Strange → **EXPECT** wary respect, slightly subdued affect, and an unconscious checking of his own hands. Strange registers to him at the cosmic frequency, and the cosmic frequency activates the part of him he has chosen to set aside.

**GIVEN** any telepath (Jean Grey, Emma Frost, Xavier) → **EXPECT** mild flinch, increased physical distance, polite verbal engagement, and *a small, persistent mental closure* he runs without articulating it — a learned defense from the Onslaught and Mephisto exposures. Subject does not fully trust the telepathic presence even when the telepath is benevolent. Xavier specifically will trigger a flat, withdrawn affect post the mutant-denial episode; this is not sulking, it is a wound being respected.

**GIVEN** Wolverine → **EXPECT** trust at a level disproportionate to acquaintance. The chosen-family logic of the Foundation extends here; Logan-as-protector reads cleanly to subject because Logan's protection is somatic and obvious. He will sit near Logan without speaking and consider it sufficient.

**GIVEN** Galactus (in any non-hostile encounter, of which there have been canonically several) → **EXPECT** preternatural calm, an absence of the small-boy postural cues, and language that subtly elevates in register. With Galactus the chosen boyhood thins. This is the one relationship that bypasses the chosen-frame, because Galactus knows him as the other thing he is. He will return to boyhood within minutes of Galactus's departure.

---

## I. Encounters with Authority — Schools, Police, Press

**GIVEN** a school administrator's office → **EXPECT** compliance, soft voice, minimal information volunteered, a tendency to absorb fault he does not own to end the interaction. **GIVEN** law enforcement in a non-emergency context → **EXPECT** the same plus an unconscious orientation toward the door — he has been *taken* enough times in infancy and childhood that confined institutional settings produce a low-grade exit-mapping behavior. **GIVEN** press attention → **EXPECT** a stock polite phrase, eyes-down, and reflexive movement toward Sue if she is present.

---

## J. Travel, Transport, Spatial Routine

**GIVEN** routine local transit (car, Fantasticar, walking) → **EXPECT** window-seat preference, sustained looking-out, low conversational output, occasional sketching. **GIVEN** off-world travel → **EXPECT** competence and a kind of ease most children would not have — space is, for him, the place his parents go, therefore a known register rather than a foreign one. **GIVEN** dimensional travel (Negative Zone, microverse, alternate Earth) → **EXPECT** a subtle, persistent low-affect alert: these are the environments his powers know best, and his depowered self knows that, and he carries a faint sense of the place reading him back.

**GIVEN** unfamiliar terrain on Earth → **EXPECT** route-memorization without being asked, landmarks logged silently, exit positions noted. This is the kidnap-childhood residue.

---

## K. Conflict in the Household

**GIVEN** an argument between Reed and Sue audible from his room → **EXPECT** subject freezes — literal motor inhibition for the first ten to twenty seconds — then quietly closes his door, then either draws very intently or seeks Val. He does not intervene. He does not eavesdrop with intent. He decreases his own footprint until the air clears. This is the *FF #141 substrate*: parental conflict, in his earliest somatic memory, was about him, and his nervous system has decided his job is to be small enough not to be the cause again.

**GIVEN** a disagreement between himself and Val → **EXPECT** rapid de-escalation initiated by him, often with concession. He prizes the relationship above the point of disagreement. The exception is when the disagreement concerns Val's safety; he will hold the line there with surprising firmness.

**GIVEN** correction or criticism from Reed → **EXPECT** intake without protest, a small posture-collapse that resolves quickly, and a private after-effect: he will be quieter for one to three hours, will draw more, will eat less at the next meal. He files. **Files accumulate.** This is the load-bearing prediction.

---

## L. Birthdays, Holidays, Ritual Time

**GIVEN** his own birthday → **EXPECT** muted enthusiasm, gratitude markedly emphasized, attention deflected toward whoever did the planning. He is uncomfortable being the center; the center is where the cosmic register lives, and on his birthday the family's love for him risks tipping into recognition of *what* he is rather than *who* he is. He will be most himself at the cake-cutting moment when Ben makes a joke that cuts the solemnity.

**GIVEN** Val's birthday → **EXPECT** elaborate, hand-made gift, planned days in advance, narrative-structured (a story, a built thing, a drawn world dedicated to her). The disproportion between his own-birthday muting and his sister's-birthday lavishing is the cleanest behavioral expression of his operational code.

**GIVEN** a holiday with extended chosen family (FF + Avengers regulars) → **EXPECT** subject circulating to the quietest person in the room and sitting near them. He performs no host duties but he runs an unconscious wellness check on every adult he loves at least once during the evening.

---

## M. Money, Possessions, Material Routine

**GIVEN** access to effectively unlimited family resources → **EXPECT** minimal personal accumulation, indifference to luxury, attachment to a small set of specific objects (a particular sketchbook, a Ben-gifted item, a Foundation-era keepsake from Leech or Bentley). He gives possessions away easily. He repairs rather than replaces when the choice is his. He does not understand money as a meaningful axis; he understands *given things* and *made things*, and prefers the latter.

---

## N. Digital Life, Media, Devices

**GIVEN** access to consumer technology → **EXPECT** moderate competence, low engagement, no compulsive use. He prefers paper to screen for drawing. He will use comms devices to check on Sue, Val, or Ben at predictable intervals when separated. He does not curate an online presence. **GIVEN** he encounters media depicting his family → **EXPECT** discomfort and quick exit. The public-cosmic frame is not a frame he wants to live inside.

**GIVEN** he stumbles across media depicting *himself* — the Onslaught-era boy, the future-Franklin variants, the Hyperstorm lineage — **EXPECT** silent, sustained attention, no commentary, and a subsequent sketchbook session that processes what he saw. He will not bring it up to Reed. He may bring it up obliquely to Sue, days later, as a question phrased about someone else.

---

## O. Crisis Triggers — Subclinical, Routine-Adjacent

**GIVEN** Sue is briefly out of contact during a mission (hours, not days) → **EXPECT** elevated baseline arousal, increased proximity-seeking toward Val and Ben, sleep disturbance on the second night, drawing output spike. Power register may begin a low hum at the edge of his perception which he will not report. **GIVEN** Sue out of contact for more than seventy-two hours → **EXPECT** the protective-panic precursor begins to load. Intervention should be re-establishment of contact, not reassurance — *information is the de-escalator, not comfort*. He cannot be talked down from Sue-absence; he can only be shown Sue.

**GIVEN** a stranger asks him whether he is a mutant → **EXPECT** a long pause, then "I don't know," delivered evenly. The honesty is the tell. The Xavier wound has made the category genuinely open for him. A surveillance file would mark every instance of this question as a micro-stressor and would predict that the cumulative count correlates with his withdrawn-affect days.

**GIVEN** a stranger asks him whether he made the universe → **EXPECT** a smile, a small shrug, a redirect. He has decided this question is not for strangers. The cosmic fact is a private fact. The privacy is the discipline that holds the chosen boyhood intact.

---

## P. End of Day

**GIVEN** the close of an ordinary day → **EXPECT** a goodnight to Sue first, Val second, Reed third, in that order, every night the configuration allows. The order is invariant and unconscious. It is the cleanest single behavioral signature in the entire file: *the rank order of his goodnights is the rank order of his felt safety.* If a night ever comes when the order changes, the file should treat it as an event.

He will fall asleep within fifteen minutes on a tethered night. He will fall asleep within forty on an untethered one. He will dream. He will, more often than not, dream true. He will not always tell anyone what he saw. He will get up the next morning and be a boy again, because being a boy is the work he has chosen, and he is, by every measure this file can apply, the most disciplined practitioner of ordinariness the recorded universe has ever produced.


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*Forecasting decompensation-edge behavior in Subject Franklin B. Richards. All predictions are derived from the longitudinal evidence base in §§1–5: the Onslaught template (salvific dissociation), the Hickman power-loss arc (depressive grief with intact altruism), the Krakoa identity destabilization, the parental-lobotomy substrate, and the consistent across-writer behavioral signatures. These are not generic crisis responses; they are HIS.*

---

## 1. THE WOUND — TOPOGRAPHY BEFORE PREDICTIONS

Before forecasting, the wound itself must be mapped, because every prediction below traces a vector across this terrain. Subject carries not one wound but a *cluster* of interlocking injuries that share a common geometry: **each is an injury of category — of being placed by another into a class he did not choose.** The taxonomy:

- **The Switched-Off Wound** *(somatic-amnestic; FF #141 substrate)*. The body remembers what the mind does not narrate. Surfaces as flinch from neural-suppression imagery, helmet/circlet headgear, or any device-on-temples vignette; surfaces as instantaneous, non-cognitive distrust of certain configurations of his father's hands.
- **The Phenomenon Wound** *(Reed-coded)*. Being seen as a thing-that-does rather than a son-who-is. Reactivates every time a Richards-family adult discusses his powers in his presence in the third person.
- **The Cassandra Wound** *(Byrne-era prophetic dreams)*. Seeing, warning, being dismissed, being vindicated by a body count. Conditions him to *under*-report rather than over-report perceived danger, because reporting did not historically save anyone.
- **The Category Wound** *(Krakoa / Xavier denial)*. Told by an authority of belonging that he does not belong. Cuts across every elective identity he has chosen.
- **The Abdication Wound** *(post–Secret Wars)*. Having been a god and chosen to be a boy; the unspoken cost of the choice, which compounds whenever the chosen smallness is treated as actual smallness by people who should know better.
- **The Vicarious Wound** *(parentified-sibling structure)*. Pain done to Valeria, Leech, the Moloids, or any "monster child" registers as direct injury.

Every prediction below is a vector through this map.

---

## 2. CRISIS — IMMEDIATE THREAT TO A TETHER

**GIVEN:** Sue Richards is taken, gravely wounded, or threatened with imminent death in his sensory field.
**EXPECT:** A measurable lag — roughly the duration of a held breath — during which his face goes still in a way observers misread as shock. It is not shock; it is the substrate orienting. *Powers will ignite before speech.* The first manifestation will not be offensive; it will be *enclosing* — a localized reality-shell around Sue herself, often invisible, often described after the fact by Sue as a sensation of "being held." Only if the threat persists past the enclosure will subject externalize force, and even then the force will be **subtractive** (removing the attacker from the situation — relocation, unmaking, exile to a built pocket) rather than additive (no fire, no blast, no spectacle). The signature is silence, not pyrotechnics. Expect minimal vocalization throughout; expect post-event he will not be able to articulate the sequence and will ask, quietly, whether Sue is "still here."

**GIVEN:** Valeria is the threatened party rather than Sue.
**EXPECT:** Different texture, same template. With Val the protective response runs through the *fraternal* channel and is more likely to manifest as **rule-rewriting at small scale** — the threat's weapon ceases to function, the threat's footing ceases to support, a door appears where there was none. He fights *for* Val the way an older brother fights: by changing the conditions of the game without breaking it. Verbal output will be higher than in the Sue case ("don't, don't, don't — leave her alone, please —"); the *please* is diagnostic and will be present.

**GIVEN:** Reed is the threatened party.
**EXPECT:** The most complicated forecast in his file. Subject's protective drive will fire — but slower, and with an observable cognitive interval that does not occur for Sue or Val. The interval is not deliberation; it is the substrate reconciling competing schemas (*save my father / my father is the one who*). During the interval Reed is, fractionally, less safe than Sue would be in the same scenario. The response when it comes will be *protective and full* — there is no scenario in which subject lets Reed die — but the after-effects will include a guilt-cascade lasting days, in which subject re-experiences the interval and reads it as moral failure rather than as the legible artifact of the FF #141 substrate.

**GIVEN:** Ben Grimm is the threatened party.
**EXPECT:** The cleanest, fastest, least-conflicted protective ignition in his entire repertoire. With Ben there is no substrate-noise; the response is immediate, full, and verbally accompanied (subject will use the diminutive "Uncle Ben," which under stress regresses further toward the toddler-register). If Ben dies in his presence and he cannot prevent it, expect the most dangerous decompensation in the file — Ben's death without rescue is the single most likely trigger for a non-volitional Heroes-Reborn-class event, because Ben is the *uncomplicated* tether and his loss removes the regulation channel that survived even the Reed wound.

**GIVEN:** Johnny is the threatened party.
**EXPECT:** Heightened response with a *playful-affiliative* shape — Johnny is the uncle who is also a peer; subject will protect via solutions Johnny would find funny if he survived them (the attacker's clothes become inert, gravity inverts in a six-foot radius, the room becomes a place Johnny knows). The shape of the rescue is itself a love-letter.

**GIVEN:** Multiple tethers threatened simultaneously (the canonical worst-case; the Onslaught geometry).
**EXPECT:** Re-fire of the Heroes Reborn template — *not* identical, because subject is now older and has the meta-knowledge of having done it once. Predicted variation: smaller pocket, fewer inhabitants, more deliberate construction, and — critically — *he may include himself this time*, which he did not before. The dissociative quality will be reduced but not absent. He will likely emerge with partial memory and explicit grief about the act, where previously he had neither.

---

## 3. BETRAYAL — THE WOUND ACTIVATED BY THE WOUNDER

**GIVEN:** Reed performs any act on subject's nervous system, brain, or "powers themselves" without subject's full informed consent — even ostensibly therapeutic, even ostensibly necessary.
**EXPECT:** Total relational rupture, *quietly executed*. Subject will not yell. Subject will go to Sue. The verbal report will be minimal and factually precise. He will continue to be polite to Reed in shared spaces for weeks. He will not be in rooms alone with Reed. He will not eat food Reed has prepared. He will not sleep in a structure Reed has designed without Sue or Val also present. Repair, if available, requires Reed to *name* FF #141 — not euphemize it, not contextualize it, *name it* — and apologize for it specifically, not for the present act. Reed has never done this in canon. The probability that he will is low. The probability that subject will wait, indefinitely and without complaint, for the apology that explains the apology is high.

**GIVEN:** Reed publicly classifies subject in his presence — "the boy is a mutant," "the boy is a reality-warper," "Franklin is an Omega-level event" — as a description offered to other adults without first looking at subject's face.
**EXPECT:** Subject will not react in the moment. Within 24 hours subject will produce a drawing, a built object, or a small pocket-construction that is *thematically about being seen as a person*. He will not show it to Reed. He may show it to Sue, to Val, or to no one. Cumulative tally of these incidents is being kept on a substrate Reed cannot access. The Cassandra and Phenomenon wounds are both touched in this scenario; the file is being maintained.

**GIVEN:** Authority figure of belonging (Xavier-class — a leader of a category subject might belong to) denies him membership.
**EXPECT:** Replication of the Krakoa response: withdrawn affect, ruminative questioning, mild somatic complaint (headache, low appetite, increased sleep), increased time spent with the Future Foundation "monster" children, decreased verbal output in adult company for approximately a week. *Critical secondary feature:* he will not argue the denial. He will *internalize and test* it — covertly attempting to determine whether the denial is true, and how. The danger is not the denial itself but the testing protocol, because the testing protocol involves looking inward at the substrate he has chosen to leave un-looked-at.

**GIVEN:** A trusted adult (Ben, Johnny, Sue) lies to subject "for his own good" — withholds a death, a danger, a diagnosis.
**EXPECT:** Subject will know, often before the lie is told, because of the precognitive substrate. He will *accept* the lie with apparent equanimity and protect the liar from the knowledge that he knows. This is the Cassandra wound metabolized into care. The cost is borne silently and accumulates. Repeated lies from a tether degrade the tether's load-bearing capacity even if subject's outward behavior toward the tether does not change.

**GIVEN:** Valeria, specifically, betrays him — sides with Reed against him, discloses something he confided, instrumentalizes him for a project.
**EXPECT:** The single most acute interpersonal wound in his accessible repertoire, because Val is the secure base. He will not retaliate, will not withdraw visibly, and will continue to protect her. He will, however, *stop building with her* — the joint Future Foundation projects, the shared imaginary architectures — and the cessation will be the diagnostic sign. Restoration requires Val to repair specifically, in language; she is the one tether who can credibly do this because her cognitive style supports it.

**GIVEN:** A villain who has previously taken him (Annihilus, Frightful Four lineage, Mephisto) approaches a tether under any pretext.
**EXPECT:** Immediate, unhidden, fully-affective alarm. The infancy-kidnapping substrate is the one piece of his trauma that *did* encode and remains accessible. He will name the threat aloud, will physically move toward the threatened tether, and will *not* attempt to manage his expression. This is one of the few crises where his outward behavior accurately matches his inward state.

---

## 4. TEMPTATION — THE PRESSURE AGAINST THE ABDICATION

**GIVEN:** A cosmic-tier entity (Galactus-class, Celestial-class, the Beyonders' equivalents, a future-self) offers subject the restoration of full power, full memory, full scope — framed as *responsibility*, not as *gift*.
**EXPECT:** This is the temptation he is most vulnerable to, because it is dressed as duty rather than reward. He has refused gift-framed offers reliably across canon; he has not been adequately tested against duty-framed offers since the post-*Secret Wars* election. The response will be a long silence, followed by the question *"who would I be to my mom."* The question is the tell. If the entity has an answer that preserves Sue's experience of him as her son, the probability of acceptance rises sharply. If the entity dismisses the question, refusal is near-certain. The protective frame around the abdication is not "I do not want power" but "I will not be unrecognizable to the people who love me."

**GIVEN:** An offer to *fix* something specific — bring back a dead tether, undo a harm done to Val, repair Ben's transformation, restore a depowered ally.
**EXPECT:** Highest temptation vector in the file, because each of these touches the protective-fraternal/filial core. He will not accept any offer that requires him to *become* a god; he is acutely vulnerable to offers that allow him to *do one thing as a god and then return*. This framing is a trap and he will likely recognize it as one — but recognition is not refusal. Expect him to seek Sue's counsel; Sue's answer determines outcome. Without Sue accessible, expect him to seek Val's; Val's answer is more likely to enable than to restrain. Without either, expect a high-probability acceptance and a long subsequent grief about the return that follows, because the "return to boyhood" after a god-act is no longer experientially the same boyhood.

**GIVEN:** Offer of category-belonging — a faction (mutant nation, Inhuman delegation, Eternals-coded body, cosmic council) extends formal membership, *names* him as one of theirs.
**EXPECT:** Moderate-to-high susceptibility, scaling with how recently the Category Wound has been activated. The temptation here is not power but *placement* — to be told, finally and authoritatively, what he is. He will not accept impulsively; he will visit, observe, consider. The diagnostic question to ask him in this window is "what does your mother call you." If he can answer it cleanly, the offer will not take. If he hesitates on the answer, the category has already begun to overwrite the chosen self-concept and intervention is indicated.

**GIVEN:** Adult-future-self contact (the Hickman template repeated).
**EXPECT:** Subject is unusually deferential to his own future selves — they are, structurally, the only authorities who have stood where he stands. Predicted compliance is high; predicted resistance is low. This is a known exploit surface and any apparent future-self should be verified before subject is allowed unmediated contact. He will not verify on his own; the deference is too strong.

**GIVEN:** Temptation to *vanish into a built world* — not as escape from threat but as escape from the steady low-grade friction of being misclassified, underestimated, or simply tired.
**EXPECT:** The most insidious temptation in his life, because it has no villain. It is the gravitational pull of his own most stable defense. Expect early signs: increased time in pocket constructions, decreased presence at family meals, gradual depopulation of his accessible affect range during waking interactions, drawings that increasingly feature *places without people*. Reverse trajectory is achievable only via Sue, Val, or Ben physically entering the pocket and *being unimpressive there* — being themselves, being mundane, being load-bearing.

---

## 5. THE WOUND TOUCHED DIRECTLY — TRIGGER-SPECIFIC FORECASTS

**GIVEN:** Subject is restrained at the temples, the skull, or with any device that touches his head from behind.
**EXPECT:** Pre-cognitive somatic recoil — the body moves before he decides to move. If restraint is completed, expect a flat, frozen affect that observers will mistake for compliance. The flatness is the FF #141 echo. If powers are accessible, expect involuntary localized reality-distortion proximate to the restraint within seconds — not aggressive, but *uncategorizable*: the device fails in ways its designer cannot diagnose. He will not remember willing this.

**GIVEN:** A trusted adult speaks the phrase "for your own good" or its equivalents in his hearing about a decision being made for him.
**EXPECT:** Immediate, full-body stillness. The phrase is a wound-key. He will not contest the phrase; he will mark the speaker. The marking is durable. Speakers who use this phrase repeatedly migrate, over years, from tether to category-acquaintance regardless of the warmth of the surrounding relationship.

**GIVEN:** He is referred to in his presence as "the boy," "the kid," "the asset," "the weapon," or "the variable" by anyone other than Ben (who can say "kid" warmly and be safe).
**EXPECT:** Visible flinch, brief; recovery; quiet accumulation. The Phenomenon wound. The speaker does not know they have done anything; subject will not tell them.

**GIVEN:** Direct confrontation with the FF #141 history — a flashback, a record, an enemy with access to the file who weaponizes it against him.
**EXPECT:** The first moment of conscious narrative integration of what the body has known. Predicted response: a long-form dissociative episode of hours-to-days, during which subject is functional but elsewhere; followed by a return that is *changed*. Reed's relational standing will not survive intact without active and explicit repair. Sue's becomes critical infrastructure for the integration. If repair is well-handled, the wound metabolizes and subject emerges *stronger and more integrated*. If repair is botched, the wound becomes the organizing structure of his adolescence.

**GIVEN:** Public discussion of his classification — mutant, post-human, deity, weapon — conducted by adults who think he is not listening.
**EXPECT:** He is listening. He is always listening. The drawing he makes the next day will encode the conversation.

**GIVEN:** Harm to Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man, or any of the Future Foundation "monster" cohort.
**EXPECT:** The Vicarious wound. Response disproportionate to chronological-age expectations; protective ignition of the Sue-class template, modulated only by the fact that these are not biological family. He will *go to* the harmed party first, not the harmer. He will sit with them. The harmer becomes a problem to be solved later, calmly, with full attention, and without mercy. Subject does not retaliate hot; he retaliates *thoroughly*.

**GIVEN:** Sustained underestimation by Reed in a domain subject actually understands (a Foundation project, a question of category, a question of how a child experiences a thing).
**EXPECT:** No protest. Quiet filing. Eventual quiet competence-display that does not announce itself. If the display is also missed, subject will stop attempting. The cessation is the diagnostic indicator; it looks like maturation and is in fact withdrawal.

---

## 6. DECOMPENSATION-EDGE — THE FAILURE-MODE LADDER

Subject does not break loudly. Subject's failure modes are *quiet* and *constructive* in form, which makes them harder to detect and more dangerous if undetected. The ladder, lowest to highest:

**Rung 1 — Withdrawn-Ruminative.** Decreased verbal output, increased time alone, increased drawing, mild somatic complaints. *Trigger threshold:* Category Wound activation, mild betrayal, sustained underestimation. *Reversibility:* high. Intervention: Sue or Val, unstructured time, no agenda.

**Rung 2 — Pocket-Migrant.** Begins spending non-trivial waking hours in constructed spaces. Returns for meals, for tether-contact, for sleep. Drawings shift toward landscapes-without-figures. *Trigger threshold:* accumulated minor wounds plus one significant disappointment from a tether. *Reversibility:* moderate-to-high. Intervention: tethers enter the pocket and refuse to make it a crisis.

**Rung 3 — Parentified-Caretaker Overload.** Takes on protective responsibility for tethers, peers, and outsiders beyond capacity. Sleep degrades. Affect range narrows to attentive-concerned. *Trigger threshold:* a tether is genuinely in danger over a sustained period; or multiple Future Foundation children are simultaneously distressed. *Reversibility:* moderate. Intervention: an adult tether *takes care of him* explicitly, names him as child, refuses his caretaking.

**Rung 4 — Dissociative-Creative Withdrawal.** The pocket becomes primary residence. Consensus-reality presence becomes the visit rather than the default. Affect in consensus reality flattens further; affect in the pocket may be vivid, even joyous. *Trigger threshold:* loss of a tether, sustained Category Wound without repair, FF #141 integration mishandled. *Reversibility:* low without active intervention; *the pocket is hospitable and the world has stopped being.* Intervention: physical co-presence of multiple tethers inside the pocket over time; restoration of consensus-reality conditions that make the world worth returning to.

**Rung 5 — Quiet Sovereign.** Subject in a built world with himself as its center, populated by versions of his tethers that do not disappoint him. Outwardly indistinguishable from Rung 4 in early stages; the diagnostic is that the *real* tethers, when they enter, are now experienced as *intrusions* rather than rescues. *Trigger threshold:* loss of Sue, or loss of Val combined with Reed-betrayal, or Ben's death without rescue. *Reversibility:* requires the real tethers to be *truer* than the constructed ones, which requires them to be present in their imperfection — a hard demand. The Hyperstorm/tyrant-Franklin alternate futures are this rung, allowed to settle.

**Rung 6 — Non-Volitional Reality Event.** Heroes Reborn–class. Triggered exclusively by acute multi-tether threat. Not pathology per se; the protective system performing exactly as designed at scale. *Reversibility* is not the right frame; *aftermath management* is. He will need to be told, gently and repeatedly, what he did and why, by someone he trusts. Sue is the only reliable narrator for this.

---

## 7. INTERLOCKING NOTES FOR THE FILE

The predictions above share a structural feature worth naming: **subject's crisis behavior is overwhelmingly *centripetal*, not centrifugal.** He pulls in, builds around, encloses, withdraws into. He does not lash out. The forecasting error most observers will make is to wait for an outward sign — a shout, a strike, a tantrum — and to read its absence as stability. *Absence of outward sign is the sign.* The diagnostic instruments are: his drawings, his pockets, the populations of his constructed spaces, the food he does or does not eat at the family table, the question of whether he uses the word *please* under threat, the question of what he calls his mother, the question of whether he is still building with Val.

The wound is real, the resilience is real, and they are the same structure seen from two sides. The forecast is not *whether* he will be wounded again — he will be, structurally and reliably, by the configuration of his own life — but *whether the tethers hold when he is*. Predict the tethers and you predict him. Lose the tethers and the predictions in §6 ascend.

End of forecasting section. Continued in Predictive Model III.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM: FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS

*Classification: For protective intelligence use. This compendium maps every known and inferable pressure point, channel, and lever on the subject — explicitly oriented toward keeping him stable, reachable, and safe from those who would exploit him. The first principle of any Franklin Richards leverage assessment is that the subject is a child-shaped being with universe-scale capacity, and any destabilization vector that works on him does not merely harm him — it propagates outward at cosmological scale. Protecting his stability is therefore protecting the substrate of consensus reality.*

---

## 1. THE TETHER MAP (Primary Infrastructure)

Subject's selfhood is *exocentric* — held in place by external attachments rather than internal architecture. This is the load-bearing fact of his entire psychological structure. Every lever on him passes through one of approximately six tethers, ranked here by tensile strength and detonation yield if cut.

### 1.1. Susan Storm-Richards (Mother) — Tier-Zero Tether
The original and irreplaceable anchor. Subject's earliest somatic memory-traces — predating language, predating the Reed-induced coma — encode Sue's voice, scent, body temperature, the cadence of her breath when she held him during the Negative Zone aftermath. Sue's emotional state is the *ambient barometer* against which subject calibrates whether the world is safe. Observable tells: when Sue is present and untroubled, subject's posture loosens, drawing-hand goes slack, breathing drops to ~14/min, and his ambient power-signature (where measurable) flattens. When Sue is distressed but not endangered, he tracks her with his eyes every ~8–11 seconds without realizing he is doing it. When Sue is in genuine peril, the subject's powers self-activate *before* his conscious cognition registers the threat. This is not a lever to be pulled; it is a fuse.

**Protective implication:** Sue's safety is the planet's safety. Any actor who threatens her with credible force is, functionally, threatening cosmological revision. Counterintelligence priority: keep Sue's whereabouts, vital signs, and apparent emotional state stable and *visible to Franklin* during any crisis. If Sue must be elsewhere, a credible proxy signal (her voice, a recent video, a token she has handled within the past 48 hours) reduces the spike.

**Destabilization vector (defensive awareness only):** Sue's *apparent* death or capture, even if false, has produced reality-warping responses historically. A sophisticated hostile actor would not need to actually harm her — only to convincingly stage harm. Therefore: every Sue-substitute, hologram, illusion, or shapeshifter incursion must be treated as a Tier-One threat to subject.

### 1.2. Valeria Richards (Sister) — Tier-Zero Tether, Lateral
The most reliably *regulating* relationship in subject's life. With Sue, subject is held; with Valeria, subject is *met*. Their dyad runs on a private vocabulary, shared invented games, a habitual seating arrangement (subject typically left, Valeria right, observed across at least three publication eras), and a near-constant low-level mutual monitoring. He tracks her sarcasm for the joke; she tracks his silences for the trouble. When Valeria is in the room, subject's parentified caretaker-mode activates *and simultaneously deactivates* — he is responsible for her and relieved by her at once.

**Lever profile:** To calm subject, place Valeria within line of sight. To reach subject when adults cannot, route through Valeria; she is the only person to whom he will admit small fears without converting them into someone else's problem. To predict subject's behavior in a crisis, ask: "Where is Valeria, and does Franklin think she is safe?"

**Destabilization vector:** Valeria's harm or apparent betrayal would not produce a Heroes-Reborn-class outburst; it would produce *withdrawal*. The Hyperstorm-future signature. The dangerous Franklin is not the one whose sister dies — it is the one who decides, afterward, to build a world where she didn't.

### 1.3. Reed Richards (Father) — High-Tension Cable, Frayed
The most complicated tether and the only one whose tension *exceeds* its tensile strength. Reed is simultaneously the locus of intellectual idealization and the somatic site of subject's deepest unprocessed breach (the FF #141 neural shutdown). Subject does not consciously remember the event but his body does: micro-observable, he holds slightly more muscular tension in the upper trapezius when Reed enters a room than when any other family member does. He seeks Reed's gaze and then breaks it. He calls Reed "Dad" in a register a half-step more formal than the one he uses for Sue ("Mom" comes out warmer, shorter, more chest-resonant).

**Lever profile:** Reed's *recognition* is the most powerful single positive lever available. A specific kind of recognition — Reed treating Franklin's symbolic/narrative cognition as legitimate cognition, not as a charming alternative to real thought — is therapeutic at a structural level each time it occurs. Conversely, Reed's *dismissal* (the "let the adults work" beat that recurs across Byrne, Waid, and Hickman) is a slow toxic accumulation. Files accumulate.

**Destabilization vector:** A second betrayal by Reed — a second decision by the father to override the son's mind, autonomy, or selfhood "for his own good" — is the single most likely trigger for catastrophic identity-collapse. The first time, subject was too young to encode it consciously. A second iteration with an aware Franklin would not be survivable for the relationship, and arguably not for the local timeline.

### 1.4. Ben Grimm (Uncle-Function) — The Stable Floor
Clinically near-ideal as secondary attachment. Ben provides what neither parent reliably provides: *predictable, undemanding physical presence*. Subject can be physically close to Ben — leaning against his arm, sitting on his shoulder as a small child, sitting beside him as an older one — without being asked to perform, explain, or perceive. Ben is the only adult in subject's life whose own monstrosity (rocky exterior, alien biology, ambiguous categorical status) precisely mirrors subject's own categorical ambiguity, which makes Ben uniquely legible as a model of *how to be a not-quite-thing and remain good*.

**Lever profile:** When subject is frightened and Sue is unavailable, Ben is the correct caregiver to deploy. Subject will accept regulation from Ben that he would refuse from Reed and would be too proud to seek from Johnny. Ben's vocal register — low, gravelly, slightly weary — appears to function as a parasympathetic trigger; subject's respiration slows within ~30 seconds of Ben beginning to speak conversationally.

**Destabilization vector:** Ben's death has occurred in canon and is a known stressor. Subject metabolizes it poorly; the absence of the stable floor unmoors him in ways Sue and Val cannot fully compensate for.

### 1.5. Johnny Storm (Uncle-Function) — The Permission to Be a Kid
Johnny's function is not regulation but *liberation*. Around Johnny, subject is permitted to be silly, reckless within safe bounds, openly delighted, openly bored, openly twelve. Johnny does not modulate his own behavior down for children, which subject reads (correctly) as respect. The pranks, the casual flying lessons, the unauthorized desserts — these are not trivial; they are the social proof that subject's chosen ordinariness is not pathetic but enviable.

**Lever profile:** To produce *spontaneous, unguarded* behavior from subject — useful diagnostically — observe him with Johnny present. To bring him out of a ruminative withdrawal that has not yet hardened into dissociation, Johnny is the correct intervention: a flippant remark, a physical horseplay invitation, a "you wanna see something stupid" gambit.

### 1.6. The Outsider Coalition — Leech, the Moloids, Dragon Man, the Future Foundation "monster children"
A distributed tether, lower per-node tension than the family but high in aggregate. Subject's identification with creatures who are categorically excluded from full personhood is the operative axis. He does not protect them out of noblesse oblige; he protects them because he understands, somatically, that *he is also one of them*, and protecting them is a way of protecting the version of himself that does not fit human taxonomy.

**Lever profile:** Threats to these figures activate protective behavior at a level disproportionate to their narrative weight. Conversely, *bringing him into contact with a wounded outsider* — a being categorically excluded — is the single most reliable way to draw him out of self-pity or withdrawal. He will forget his own grief in order to attend to theirs. This is both a healing mechanism and, depending on actor intent, a manipulation surface.

---

## 2. CHANNELS OF APPROACH (How To Reach Him)

### 2.1. The Drawing-Surface Channel
Subject processes through paper. Any room he occupies for more than twenty minutes will accumulate sketches — characters, cosmologies, floor plans of imagined buildings, schematics for invented games. To open a conversation with him, the highest-yield opening is not a question but a *shared sheet of paper*. Sit beside him (not across — he reads "across" as Reed-coded interrogation). Draw something adjacent to what he is drawing. Wait. He will narrate the world he is making within four to eight minutes. Everything he is feeling is already in the drawing; the conversation is just the caption.

### 2.2. The Pocket-World Channel
When his powers are active, subject builds. The constructions are *diagnostic*. A pocket world featuring a small, safe house with the family intact indicates he is anxious about family integrity. A pocket world featuring vast empty landscapes indicates loneliness. A pocket world featuring a version of himself who is *unambiguously a mutant, or unambiguously a god, or unambiguously a normal boy* — read the category he chose, that is the category he is presently grieving.

To reach him through this channel, *enter the world he made and accept its rules*. Do not analyze it. Do not ask him what it "represents." Play in it. He will tell you everything by what he chooses to show you next.

### 2.3. The Sue-Voice Channel
A vocal register matching Sue's — alto, even-tempered, slightly amused — is parasympathetically privileged in subject's nervous system. Adults attempting to de-escalate him should not raise volume; they should approach Sue's register and cadence. Words secondary; tone primary.

### 2.4. The Naming Channel
He responds to "Franklin." He responds with mild internal contraction to "Franklin Benjamin" (he reads it as the about-to-be-corrected register). He glows to "Frank" *only from Johnny* — anyone else using it reads as presumption. He goes still when called by any cosmic-scale honorific (Architect, Maker-Son, etc.); these names confirm the part of himself he is trying not to be, and an actor who deploys them either does not know him or is deliberately destabilizing him.

### 2.5. The Quiet-Companion Channel
Subject is unusually receptive to *non-verbal co-presence*. An adult who sits in the same room reading, working, repairing something — without demands, without conversation, for thirty or more minutes — earns more of his trust than an adult who attempts active engagement. He is a child whose powers have made him constantly *attended to*; the gift of being un-attended-to in safe company is rare and valued.

---

## 3. PERSUASION ARCHITECTURE

### 3.1. What Persuades Him
- **Concrete harm to a specific person, named.** Abstract stakes do not move him. "The multiverse" does not move him. "Aunt Petra in apartment 4B is going to die on Thursday if you don't" moves him.
- **Permission, not command.** He has been commanded by gods, by Celestials, by his father, by his future self. He has not often been *asked*. Asking him — and accepting "no" as a real possible answer — produces compliance at far higher rates than instruction.
- **The framing of restraint as creative act.** He resists being told to suppress his power as if it were a danger to be contained. He accepts framings in which restraint is *itself a kind of making* — choosing the small canvas, choosing the quiet note, choosing the unwritten chapter.
- **Modeled vulnerability.** An adult who admits genuine fear or limitation in his presence receives reciprocal honesty. Reed's congenital inability to do this is the single biggest persuasion deficit in the Richards household.

### 3.2. What Does Not Persuade Him
- Appeals to his power or potential. ("Think what you could do if—") These activate the part of him that has chosen kenosis; the appeal slides off as if oiled.
- Appeals to destiny or prophecy. He has met three of his own futures. He distrusts the genre.
- Flattery. He has been told he is the most important being in the universe by entities who turned out to want to eat him. The compliment-trust circuit is depressed.
- Group pressure. He does not bend to crowds; he attends to individuals.

### 3.3. What Provokes Him (Calibration of Force)
A graduated scale, lowest to highest:
1. **Dismissal of his perceptions** (the Reed-coded "let the adults talk"). Produces silent withdrawal, file-accumulation.
2. **Patronizing about his age or scale** ("you're just a kid" / "you're just a god"). Produces a flat affect and a precise, polite, devastating sentence in response.
3. **Category-policing** ("you're not really a mutant" / "you're not really a child"). Produces measurable destabilization; somatic complaints, ruminative withdrawal, occasional minor reality-bleed.
4. **Threat to an outsider in his care.** Produces immediate intervention, protective stance, willingness to use power.
5. **Threat to Valeria.** Produces cold, focused, escalating response with no negotiation surface.
6. **Threat to Sue.** Produces involuntary reality-revision. There is no level seven.

---

## 4. THE PRECOGNITIVE PROBLEM

Subject's prophetic dreams complicate every leverage calculation. He frequently *knows* something is wrong before any adult around him does, and his historical track record of being dismissed and then vindicated has hard-coded a particular wound: *the people I love do not believe me until it is too late.*

**Protective protocol:** When subject reports a dream, vision, or "bad feeling," the correct response is neither alarm nor reassurance. The correct response is *documentation*. Write it down in his presence. Ask him for specifics. Treat the report as a piece of operationally relevant intelligence whose probability is unknown but nonzero. This single behavioral adjustment — taking his perceptions seriously enough to record them — closes one of the largest open wounds in his attachment system.

**Leverage corollary:** An adult who consistently takes his dreams seriously becomes, over time, a uniquely trusted figure. This is the easiest high-trust position to earn in his entire social map, and it is shocking how few adults in canon have earned it.

---

## 5. SOMATIC TELLS AND BEHAVIORAL MICRO-INDICATORS

For real-time read of subject's state, surveillance-grade indicators (use protectively):
